State v. Alfonso


No. 99-KA-1546


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


99-1546 (La. 11/23/99); 753 So. 2d 156; 1999 La. LEXIS 3242



November 23, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Granted In Part December 7, 1999. Released for Publication December 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Thirty-Fourth Judicial District Court, for the Parish of St. Bernard, Honorable David S. Gorbaty, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This was a direct appeal, pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 5(D), from a judgment of the Thirty-Fourth Judicial District Court, for the Parish of St. Bernard (Louisiana) declaring unconstitutional La. Admin. Code tit. 76, Part VII, § 343E5 (1995).


OVERVIEW: Defendants, commercial fisherman, were charged with violating La. Admin. Code tit. 76, Part VII, § 343E5 (1995) (regulation). After a hearing on defendants' motion to quash, the trial court declared the subject regulation unconstitutional as an impermissible exercise of legislative authority by the executive branch of the government. Although the Legislature had delegated to the Wildlife and Fisheries Commission (Commission) the power to adopt rules to regulate the "taking" of mullet, the court held that the Commission exceeded its authority by adopting the subject regulation, which criminalized the commercial mullet fishermen's failure to report their catch. The court found the conduct criminalized by the administrative rule did not fall within the statutory definition of "taking." As the regulation was unconstitutional, it could not be used as a basis for the offenses charged. The judgment declaring the regulation unconstitutional and granting defendants' motion to quash was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment declaring regulation unconstitutional and granting motion to quash charges against all defendants affirmed. Trial court correctly held that Wildlife and Fisheries Commission, in adopting mullet reporting requirement improperly exceeded its statutory authority. As regulation was unconstitutional, it could not be used as a basis for the offenses charged.

3 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Jurisich v. Jenkins


99-C-0076


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


99-0076 (La. 10/19/99); 749 So. 2d 597; 1999 La. LEXIS 2603



October 19, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 La. LEXIS 3135. Released for Publication November 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), to determine an action for a preliminary injunction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' oyster lease renewals were made contingent upon the inclusion of a clause that would have made the oyster leases subservient to normal, usual, and permissible mineral and oil-field activity sanctioned through a prior existing lease, permit, or contract. The court found that defendant Secretary for the Louisiana Department of Wildlife and Fisheries (defendant secretary) could not deny renewal of plaintiffs' oyster leases, because it was not shown the leases were incapable of supporting oyster populations. Unless the oyster beds initially leased were incapable of supporting oyster populations, defendant secretary had a mandatory duty to renew. Further, the court found the clause was against the spirit and contrary to defendant secretary's legislative mandate in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:425 (C), to make clauses in oyster leases as he deemed necessary and proper to develop the oyster industry.


OUTCOME: Denial of the preliminary injunction reversed and remanded; there was no authority for defendant secretary's actions, and the clause at issue was against the spirit and contrary to defendant secretary's legislative mandate to make such clauses in oyster leases as necessary and proper to develop the oyster industry.

 

4 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Falgout v. Dealers Truck Equip. Co.


98-C-3150


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-3150 (La. 10/19/99); 748 So. 2d 399; 1999 La. LEXIS 2606



October 19, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied November 19, 1999. Released for Publication November 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION, DISTRICT # 8.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Forth Circuit, Office of Workers' Compensation, District #8 (Louisiana) to determine whether the prescriptive period contained in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1209 applied to actions to modify a workers' compensation award.


OVERVIEW: On writ of certiorari to determine whether the prescriptive period contained in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1209 applied to actions to modify a workers' compensation award. The appellate court read La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.8 in conjunction with the prescriptive period found in § 23:1209 and concluded plaintiff's claim had prescribed since it was filed more than one year from the date of the last compensation payment. The court held that absent express legislative intent to the contrary, prescription was not applicable to claims for modification of a workers' compensation award. The amendment of § 23:1310.8 applied prospectively only, because to apply it retroactively would have divested plaintiff of his vested property right to file a claim for modification of his compensation award. Plaintiff's claim for modification was not barred by prescription, and defendant's exception of prescription should have been denied. Judgment reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: Absent express legislative intent to the contrary, prescription did not apply to claims for modification of workers' compensation award. Plaintiff's claim for modification was not barred by prescription, and defendant's exception of prescription should have been denied. Judgment reversed and remanded.

 

5 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Price v. U-Haul Co.


No. 98-CA-1959


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-1960 (La. 09/08/99); 745 So. 2d 593; 1999 La. LEXIS 2233; 39 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 579



September 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied October 8, 1999. Released for Publication October 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS, HONORABLE RONALD J. SHOLES, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) that the Self-Service Storage Facility Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 9:4756-9:4760, was unconstitutional as a violation of due process guarantees.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, owners and lessors of a self-service storage facility, seized and sold plaintiff's property pursuant to the Self-Service Storage Facility Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 9:4756-9:4760, after plaintiff became delinquent in his rent payments. The trial court ruled that the act was unconstitutional as a violation of due process guarantees. The appellate court reversed, concluding that defendants were private actors, who proceeded under the private enforcement provisions of the act and were not acting under color of state law. Therefore, due process guarantees were not implicated. Moreover, the state neither encouraged nor benefitted from the private action authorized in the act. The appellate court concluded that the act, with its fair notice requirement and other safeguards, presented no fundamental unfairness in the creditor-debtor relationship between the parties. The court cautioned that the its decision did not necessarily mean that private self-help could be utilized in every creditor-debtor relationship and that such matters were to be decided on a case-by-case basis. However, the act in the context of the facts of the case did not warrant judicial intervention.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed trial court's judgment that act, which allowed a lessor to seize and sell a lessee's property if the lessee defaulted, was unconstitutional as a violation of due process, concluding that defendant's actions as a lessor under the act were private actions and thus did not implicate due process guarantees.

 

6 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Louisiana Associated Gen. Contrs., Inc. v. New Orleans Aviation Bd.


No. 99-CA-0025


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


99-0025 (La. 07/07/99); 764 So. 2d 31; 1999 La. LEXIS 1715



July 7, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, HONORABLE PATRICK J. McCABE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an aviation board, appealed a judgment of the 24th District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), finding defendant's business program was unconstitutional because it created unconstitutional race- and gender-based classifications. Plaintiffs, general contractors, cross-appealed the trial court's ruling that defendant had the authority under local law to authorize the program.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, general contractors, filed a petition for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendant, an aviation board, contending that defendant's business program was unconstitutional because it created unconstitutional race- and gender-based classifications. The trial court ruled that the program was unconstitutional and imposed a permanent injunction. The trial court also ruled that defendant had authority under local rules to authorize the program. The court reversed the trial court's ruling that defendant had authority to authorize the program but maintained the permanent injunction imposed. The court held that defendant's program facially violated the City of New Orleans' Interim Disadvantaged Small Business Development Ordinance (interim ordinance). The court held that defendant's program's standard for determining if an individual was socially and economically disadvantaged fell far below the standard commanded by the interim ordinance. The court held further that defendant's program provided preference toward individuals on the basis of race and gender when awarding public works contracts and, therefore, was prohibited.


OUTCOME: Court reversed portion of trial court's judgment which found that defendant had authority to authorize its business program. Court held that program violated ordinance because its standard for determining if an individual was socially and economically disadvantaged fell below ordinance standard, and because program provided preference toward individuals on basis of race and gender. Court upheld permanent injunction against the program.

 

7 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Jenkins v. St. Tammany Parish Police Jury


No. 98-CA-2627


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-2627 (La. 07/02/99); 736 So. 2d 1287; 1999 La. LEXIS 1706



July 2, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit (Louisiana), which granted a conditional use permit to plaintiff land owner, holding that a local ordinance was unconstitutional. The court held that defendant unreasonably and arbitrarily denied plaintiff's application for a conditional use permit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a writ of certiorari to determine whether the appeals court erred in declaring its zoning ordinance unconstitutional and ordering the grant of plaintiff's application for a conditional use permit to construct a family cemetery. Zoning commission denied plaintiff's request for a conditional use permit alleging too many cemeteries in the surrounding area. The commission informed plaintiff that it would issue the conditional use permit if he would agree to construct the cemetery on another portion of the same tract; however, plaintiff refused. On appeal, the court concluded a willingness to issue the permit if plaintiff agreed to relocate the cemetery contradicted commission's statement that there were too many cemeteries in the area. Commission also stated it denied plaintiff's request for a conditional use permit because funeral processions would disrupt traffic. The court determined this argument lacked merit because a private family cemetery would not disrupt the flow of traffic. However, the appellate court should not have determined the constitutionality of the ordinance because that was not essential to the decision. The order granting the permit was affirmed.


OUTCOME: An order granting plaintiff's conditional use permit was granted; however, it was error for the court to address the issue of whether the zoning ordinance was unconstitutional when the case was easily decided on a non-constitutional basis.

 

8 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wessinger


No. 98-KA-1234


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-1234 (La. 05/28/99); 736 So. 2d 162; 1999 La. LEXIS 1601



May 28, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 2, 1999. Released for Publication July 2, 1999. Certiorari Denied December 6, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 8089.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. HONORABLE RICHARD D. ANDERSON, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree murder and sentenced to death for each count. La. Const. art. V, § 5(D). Defendant filed a direct appeal to the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: After riding his bicycle to a restaurant where he used to work, defendant shot and killed two former co-workers. During the shooting spree, defendant also took $ 7000. Following a bifurcated capital trial, jury sentenced defendant to death for each count of first degree murder. Jury found three aggravating circumstances: defendant was engaged in perpetration or attempted perpetration of aggravated burglary or armed robbery; defendant knowingly created a risk of death or great bodily harm to more than one person; and the offense was committed in an especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel manner. Raising eighteen separate assignments of error, defendant appealed directly to the state supreme court. Finding no merit to any issue raised by defendant, the court affirmed the murder convictions and death sentences. Both because the same policies that applied to require a contemporaneous objection in the guilt phase also applied to the penalty phase and because the accused's rights were protected regardless of the contemporaneous objection rule's application, the court prospectively ruled that it would no longer consider alleged penalty phase errors absent a contemporaneous objection.


OUTCOME: Prospectively ruling that contemporaneous objections were a prerequisite for appellate review of penalty phase errors, the state supreme court affirmed the two first degree murder convictions and death sentences that jury imposed upon defendant. Except for the possibility of review by the United States Supreme Court, the judgment served as a condition precedent to defendant's execution.

State v. Ferris


No. 98-KA-2442


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-2442 (La. 05/18/99); 747 So. 2d 487; 1999 La. LEXIS 1502



May 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF EVANGELINE, HONORABLE PRESTON N. AUCOIN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment from the Thirteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana), which granted defendant's motion to quash, finding La. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 14:98.1 discriminated against underage drivers on the basis of their age.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with underage driving under the influence of alcohol. The trial court granted defendant's motion to quash, finding La. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 14:98.1 violated his rights to equal protection for making it a crime for persons under twenty-one years of age with a blood alcohol concentration of .02 percent or more to drive, while persons twenty-one years of age or older could legally drive if not under the influence and with a blood alcohol concentration of less than .10 percent. The state appealed the ruling on grounds that the trial court erred in failing to admit evidence relevant to the showing that underage drivers were over-represented in alcohol related accidents. The court vacated the order to quash and remanded, holding the trial court erred in failing to admit relevant evidence in its determination whether the statute discriminated against underage drivers.


OUTCOME: The order to quash was vacated and the court remanded because the trial court failed to admit relevant evidence in its determination whether the underage drunk driving statute discriminated against underage drivers.

 

10 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Jacobs v. City of Bunkie


No. 98-CA-2510


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-2510 (La. 05/18/99); 737 So. 2d 14; 1999 La. LEXIS 1503



May 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 2, 1999. Released for Publication July 2, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWELFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF AVOYELLES, HONORABLE TED R. BROYLES, JUDGE AD HOC.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed a judgment rendered by the Twelfth Judicial District Court (Louisiana), that held that an amendment to La. Const. art. XII, § 10(C), was not curative or remedial and therefore could not be applied retroactively to plaintiff's case against defendant for personal injuries.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged strict liability and negligence against defendant city for injuries that resulted after plaintiff's car went into a sinkhole. Defendant's defense was "limitations of liability for public bodies" under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800. Plaintiff then asserted the unconstitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800. The trial court found the statute unconstitutional under La. Const. art. XII, § 10(A). Defendant appealed but case was dismissed and remanded due to technical flaw. The legislature passed 1995 La. Acts 1328 which proposed a constitutional amendment to La. Const. art. XII, § 10(C), and 1995 La. Acts 828 in which La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800 was reenacted in the same form originally enacted. On remand, the court held that the amendment was not remedial, and therefore could not be applied retroactively to plaintiff's case. Defendant appealed to the Supreme Court. The court found that that "new" La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800 was a substantive change in law and could only be applied prospectively. The old statute was an impermissible legislative act limiting defendant's liability in direct conflict with La. Const. art. XII, § 10(A)'s waiver of sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that held that an amendment to the constitution was not curative or remedial because changes to the amendment were substantive and could not be applied to pending cases retroactively.

 

11 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Howard


No. 98-KA-0064


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-0064 (La. 04/23/99); 751 So. 2d 783; 1999 La. LEXIS 1073



April 23, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 28, 1999. Released for Publication May 28, 1999.
Rehearing denied by, 05/28/1999
Writ of certiorari denied Howard v. Louisiana, 528 U.S. 974, 120 S. Ct. 420, 145 L. Ed. 2d 328, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7232 (1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF RAPIDES, HONORABLE DONALD T. JOHNSON, JUDGE.
State v. McCullough, 734 So. 2d 643, 1999 La. LEXIS 109 (La., Jan. 6, 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Raising 25 assignments of error, defendant challenged a judgment of the Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), sentencing him to death after a jury convicted him of participating in a gang-related, brutal-beating death of an elderly woman who was attacked in her home during a robbery. After a sentencing hearing, the same jury charged with determining defendant's guilt unanimously returned a verdict of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction and death sentence for the gang-related murder of an elderly woman in her home after he and nine other men broke into the victim's home with the intent of robbing her. After a plea bargain, a co-defendant testified that he observed defendant and the other men beating, kicking, and stabbing the victim. Among numerous other issues, defendant claimed the trial court erred when it found him competent to stand trial after, while detained, he suffered a cerebral aneurysm that required surgery. Defendant also argued the court erred in granting the state's challenges of prospective jurors for cause, in denying the defense's challenges for cause, and by allowing the prosecution to misstate the law during voir dire. Defendant also claimed the bargained-for testimony of his co-defendant was insufficient to convict him. Finding the bargained-for testimony was corroborated, the appellate court affirmed the conviction because there was no abuse of discretion either during voir dire or in determining defendant's mental capacity, and misstatements of the law by the prosecution were not reversible error where jury instructions were given at the proper time.


OUTCOME: Upon reviewing the 25 assignments of error raised by defendant, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence, holding that the lower court properly instructed the jury after both the guilt and penalty phases. Prosecutorial misstatements of the law during voir dire were not reversible error and the trial judge committed no manifest error in determining defendant was mentally competent to stand trial.

 

12 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lucky


No. 96-KA-1687


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-1687 (La. 04/13/99); 755 So. 2d 845; 1999 La. LEXIS 3656



April 13, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied September 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 La. LEXIS 3657. Released for Publication September 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Previously Reported at: 750 So. 2d 801 and Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.

ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, HONORABLE CLARENCE E. MCMANUS, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of first degree murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant claimed the trial court erred by denying defense counsel's challenge for cause based on a prospective juror's ability to consider a recommendation of life imprisonment, and by discharging an entire panel of seven prospective jurors based on remarks one of them made.


OVERVIEW: Judgment convicting defendant of first degree murder and sentencing him to death was affirmed. The appellate court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by finding that a juror's need for substantial mitigating evidence to justify a life sentence did not significantly impair his performance. There was no abuse of discretion in dismissing a jury panel where the trial court saw and heard the jurors and determined the panel had been tainted. Defendant knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily waived his constitutional rights before he gave a statement to police, who were not required to obtain another waiver before his second statement 20 minutes later. Admission of an accomplice statement was error where it was not sufficiently self-inculpatory to be admissible under La. Code Evid. Ann. art 804B(3) as a statement against interest, but the error was harmless. The prosecutor's closing statement regarding additional evidence was not a reference to evidence applicable to the guilt phase. Even if the remarks were improper, the error was harmless. The evidence was sufficient to support the jury's finding of aggravating circumstances, and the penalty was proportionate.


OUTCOME: Defendant's first degree murder conviction and death sentence were affirmed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying a challenge for cause or by dismissing a panel based on comments by a juror. Defendant's confession was knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily given. Admission of an accomplice statement was harmless error. The evidence supported a finding of aggravating circumstances, and the sentence was proportionate.

 

13 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Hawkins


98-C-1259 CONSOLIDATED WITH 98-C-1288


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-1259 (La. 03/18/99); 731 So. 2d 216; 1999 La. LEXIS 336



March 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF CADDO.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the appellate court is reversed on the issues of the City's liability and amended on the issue of the award of the minor's medical damages to his mother in her individual rather than her representative capacity.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both plaintiff mother and defendant city sought writs of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), in suit filed by plaintiffs, mother and father, against defendants, driver, insurer, house owners, and city, in connection with an accident involving their son.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, mother and father, filed suit against defendants, driver, insurer, house owners, and city, in connection with their son's injuries. Defendant city argued lack of actual or constructive notice of defect at intersection under La. Rev. Stat. § 9:2800. After no liability was found, plaintiffs appealed, and defendant city and defendant owners of house were found liable, with damages granted to plaintiff mother. Plaintiff mother and defendant city sought writs of certiorari. Court held that lack of maintenance plan did not constitute constructive knowledge of defect. Further, court held that plaintiffs had failed to prove that the overgrown vegetation surrounding defendant house owners' home at intersection was a substantial factor in the accident. Finally, court held that since plaintiff mother had brought suit as tutrix for medical expenses, it was improper to award her damages for medical expenses in her individual capacity and to reduce these by finding plaintiffs partially at fault for the accident.


OUTCOME: Court granted both writs of certiorari, holding that defendant city's lack of maintenance plan did not create constructive notice of defect under the relevant statute, such that defendant city was not liable, and further holding that since plaintiff mother had sued as son's tutrix, individual damages award was improper.

 

14 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Caruso


No. 98-KA-1415


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-1415 (La. 03/04/1999); 733 So. 2d 1169; 1999 La. LEXIS 308



March 2, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, HONORABLE KERNAN A. HAND, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed a decision of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), granting defendant's motion to quash a bill of information on the ground that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:220 was unconstitutional because it contained a mandatory presumption and made a petty matter a felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by bill of information with violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:220 in that with fraudulent intent he willfully refused to return a leased vehicle to a car company. Defendant moved to quash the bill of information on the ground that § 14:220 was unconstitutional because it contained a mandatory presumption and made a petty matter a felony. The trial judge granted the motion finding that the final sentence of § 14:220 was unconstitutional. Plaintiff state appealed, and the court reversed. The court held that the language "shall be presumptive evidence" in § 14:220 created a permissive presumption or inference, not an impermissible mandatory presumption. The court determined that the application of the presumption under the statute allowed, but did not require, the trier of fact to infer the presumed fact of intent to defraud from evidence that defendant failed to return or surrender the car within 15 days after notice to make such return or surrender. The court remanded the matter for consideration of defendant's other constitutional challenges that the trial court did not address.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision granting defendant's motion to quash a bill of information on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional because it contained a mandatory presumption. The court explained that the language "shall be presumptive evidence" in the statute created a permissive presumption or inference, not an impermissible mandatory presumption.

 

15 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Louisiana Dep't of Agric. & Forestry v. Sumrall


No. 98-C-1587


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-1587 (La. 03/02/99); 728 So. 2d 1254; 1999 La. LEXIS 345; 75 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P45,924



March 2, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 1, 1999.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of certiorari from the decision of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which held that the rules promulgated by respondent were a constitutional exercise of respondent's rulemaking authority under La. Const. art. X, § 10.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Commission promulgated rules which afforded employees the right to an administrative appeal on claims of discrimination on grounds other than those specified in La. Const. art. X, § 8(b). Petitioner government department objected to the rules on grounds that La. Const. art. X, § 8(b) provided for administrative appeals to respondent for discrimination based on political beliefs, religious beliefs, sex, and race. Reversing the judgment of the lower court that respondent's rules were constitutional, the court found that the rules promulgated by respondent unconstitutionally expanded respondent's authority and appellate jurisdiction. Giving the straightforward language of § 8(b) its ordinary meaning, the court held that respondent's quasi-judicial power was limited to hear only four types of discrimination claims. The court applied a two-part test in determining that the rules were unconstitutional where the court found that respondent did not have any statutory authority to hear discrimination cases outside of those specified and where the broadening of respondent's power was not necessary to achieve the goals and principal objectives of the civil service.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court holding that the rules promulgated by respondent were constitutional was reversed and rules held to be unconstitutional where respondent did not have the statutory authority to expand the type of discrimination cases over which it had administrative appellate jurisdiction where the constitution specified what discrimination claims were subject to respondent's quasi-judicial authority.

 

16 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. T.L.R. v. R. W. T.


No. 98-CA-2274


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-2274 (La. 01/20/99); 737 So. 2d 688; 1999 La. LEXIS 4



January 20, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 3, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Juvenile Court, For the Parish of Caddo, Honorable Vernon Claville, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED; REMANDED TO JUVENILE COURT FOR EXPEDITIOUS TREATMENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state, on behalf of the mother of the minor child, appealed the decision by the Juvenile Court, for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which held that defendant putative father's objection to the admission of the blood test to determine parentage was timely and that the Uniform Interstate Family Support Act, La. Child Code art. 1301.1 et seq., was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff state, on behalf of the mother of the minor child, filed an action seeking to have defendant declared the father of the minor child and have support assessed. Defendant, the alleged biological father, sought to delay the proceedings by filing objections to the admission of the blood test and arguing that the Uniform Interstate Family Support Act (UIFSA), La. Child Code art. 1301.1 et set., was unconstitutional because he did not have the right to cross-examine the witnesses who examined the blood. The mother's and child's blood was drawn in California and defendant's was drawn in Louisiana, but all three samples were sent to Virginia for analysis. The lower court determined that defendant had not received proper notice and therefore his objections were timely and that the UIFSA was unconstitutional. Plaintiff appealed and the court agreed with plaintiff that the UIFSA was constitutional and provided multiple methods for cross-examination, of which defendant had not used any. The court also held that defendant did have proper notice and that paternity was prima facie established by a 99.98 percent probability. The lower court's decision was therefore vacated and remanded.


OUTCOME: The lower court's judgment, that the Uniform Interstate Family Support Act (UIFSA) was unconstitutional and that defendant had not received proper notice of test to establish paternity, was vacated because the UIFSA provided multiple methods of cross-examination of out-of-state witnesses and because defendant received proper notice.

 

17 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Brinker v. Junction City Wood Co.


No. 96-CA-2896


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-2897 (La. 01/20/99); 728 So. 2d 1252; 1999 La. LEXIS 11



January 20, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 3, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CLAIBORNE, HONORABLE JENIFER WARD CLASON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana) transferred plaintiff nonconsenting landowners' action due to lack of subject matter jurisdiction to hear the issue of constitutionality after the trial court declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.2 unconstitutional as applied to plaintiffs in their action, which triggered defendant corporation's right to a direct appeal pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 5(D).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowners purchased five percent of a tract of land. Defendant corporation purchased the right to cut timber on the remaining land. Defendant notified plaintiffs of its intent to remove the timber from the tract and escrow the money due to them. Plaintiffs later requested that defendant cease cutting operations, but it refused. Defendant contended it was entitled to cut the timber pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.2. Plaintiffs filed a petition for an injunction and a declaratory judgment seeking to have § 3:4278.2 declared unconstitutional. The trial court permanently enjoined defendant from removing timber from the tract and declared § 3:4278.2 unconstitutional as applied to plaintiffs, which triggered defendant's right to a direct appeal pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 5(D). The appellate court transferred the case. The trial court had determined that defendant did not comply with the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.2. Therefore, the matter was resolved based on nonconstitutional issues. The trial court should not have passed on the constitutionality of § 3:4278.2 unless it was essential to its decision. Judgment vacated in part and remanded.


OUTCOME: The supreme court vacated the declaration that the statute at issue was unconstitutional and remanded plaintiff nonconsenting landowners' case to the appellate court for consideration of the other assignments of error. The matter was resolved based on nonconstitutional issues; therefore, it was clear that the constitutionality of the statute was not essential to the decision. The trial court prematurely ruled on the issue of constitutionality.

STATE v. FROST


No. 97-KA-1771


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-1771 (La. 12/01/98); 727 So. 2d 417; 1998 La. LEXIS 3510



December 1, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied January 29, 1999. Released for Publication January 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE BONNIE P. JACKSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 19th Judicial District, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which convicted him of first degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 and was sentenced to death upon a finding of two aggravating circumstances. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence and held that all 112 of defendant's assignments of error were without merit. The exclusion of several jurors for cause was proper because the trial court was given wide discretion in determining the capabilities and potential biases of the jurors. The court held that the prosecutor's conduct in lecturing, arguing, and conditioning a juror during voir dire was harmless error because the trial judge sustained the objection, and the remarks did not influence the juror's impartiality. Victim impact testimony from non-family members was harmless error. Evidence regarding the victim's IQ was intended to show the victim's uniqueness. Prosecutor's closing argument that attempted to discredit mitigating factors was not error because the existence of the factors was a question for the jury. Defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive or disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.

State v. Chester


No. 97-KA-2790


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-2790 (La. 12/01/98); 724 So. 2d 1276; 1998 La. LEXIS 3501



December 1, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied January 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 La. LEXIS 12. Released for Publication January 15, 1999.
Modified and rehearing denied by State v. Chester, 724 So. 2d 1276, 1999 La. LEXIS 12 (La., Jan. 15, 1999)
Related proceeding at State v. Ratcliff, 731 So. 2d 356, 1999 La. App. LEXIS 326 (La.App. 5 Cir., Feb. 23, 1999)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Chester v. Louisiana, 528 U.S. 826, 120 S. Ct. 75, 145 L. Ed. 2d 64, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5122 (1999)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Remanded by State v. Chester, 27 So. 3d 837, 2010 La. LEXIS 265 (La., 2010)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Chester v. Cain, 46 So. 3d 1254, 2010 La. LEXIS 2272 (La., 2010)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Chester v. State, 99 So. 3d 664, 2012 La. LEXIS 3021 (La., 2012)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Chester v. State, 118 So. 3d 429, 2013 La. LEXIS 1575 (La., 2013)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Chester v. State, 118 So. 3d 429, 2013 La. LEXIS 1576 (La., 2013)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Chester v. State, 137 So. 3d 1216, 2014 La. LEXIS 873 (La., 2014)
Writ denied by State v. Chester, 151 So. 3d 610, 2014 La. LEXIS 2315 (La., 2014)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Chester, 2016 La. LEXIS 2506 (La., Dec. 16, 2016)
Concurring Opinion at, Post-conviction proceeding at State v. Chester, 2016 La. LEXIS 2689 (La., Dec. 16, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, HONORABLE MARTHA B. SASSONE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction and death sentence for the murder of John Adams are affirmed for all purposes, except that this judgment shall not serve as a condition precedent to execution, as provided by La. R.S. 15:567 until either (a) defendant fails to petition the United States Supreme Court timely for certiorari; or (b) that Court denies his petition for certiorari and either (i) defendant, having filed for and been denied certiorari, fails to petition the United States Supreme Court timely, under its prevailing rules, for rehearing of denial of certiorari, or (ii) that Court denies his petition for rehearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 24th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) severed the trials of defendant and his co-indictee. The co-indictee was convicted of second degree murder and sentenced to life. By jury defendant was convicted of first degree murder, the armed robbery aggravator was found, and he was sentenced to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: A cabbie was found shot to death point blank in the back of the head and with some of his money missing. Co-indictee's fingerprints were found on the victim's scattered business cards. He was arrested and mentioned defendant. Defendant's girlfriend's sister called the police and said she heard defendant admit the shooting. The girlfriend said he said that the co-indictee did it. Defendant admitted being in the cab and blamed the co-indictee. At trial, the girlfriend changed her story to say defendant admitted being the shooter. The State argued that defendant's bloody clothes showed he was the shooter. The Louisiana Supreme Court found that no prejudice occurred to him as a result of the victim's mother's, a subpoenaed witness, presence during voir dire. The trial judge's reference to defendant in privately telling the jury about their hotel for the trial did not imply he was dangerous. A peremptorily-challenged veniremember who found specific intent and mitigating circumstances to be mutually exclusive was properly not excused for cause because she also said she could consider mitigators. Prohibition of impeachment of the sister on her juvenile record was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed, except that the judgment would not serve as a statutory condition precedent to execution until either (a) defendant failed to petition the United States Supreme Court timely for certiorari; or (b) that court denied his petition and either (i) he, having filed for and been denied it, failed to petition the court timely for rehearing of denial of certiorari, or (ii) that court denied him rehearing.

Cat's Meow, Inc. v. City of New Orleans ex rel. Department of Fin.


No. 98-CA-0601


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-0601 (La. 10/20/98); 720 So. 2d 1186; 1998 La. LEXIS 3039



October 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS, HONORABLE ROBIN M. GIARRUSSO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED AND CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, nightclubs and patron, filed an action against defendant city alleging that the city's amusement tax ordinances was unconstitutional. The Civil District Court for Orleans Parish (Louisiana) granted summary judgment in favor of the nightclubs and patron. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The nightclubs and patron alleged that the city's amusement tax ordinances violated the enabling legislation passed by the state, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:41-46, because the city's ordinances allowed for more exemptions than the enabling legislation. The city argued that the nightclubs lacked standing, that the city's home rule charter granted the authority for the additional exceptions, that the case had become moot because the amusement tax ordinance had been amended. The court found that the case had not become moot because the nightclubs and patron were not merely asking for prospective relief but damages for taxes already paid. The court also found that the trial court had acted prematurely when it granted summary judgment in favor of the nightclubs and patron and declared the city ordinance unconstitutional because the trial court should have ruled on the standing issue and the home rule charter issue. Either of these issues might have provided the trial court a means to resolve the dispute without ruling on the constitutionality of the ordinance. The trial court should have refrained from determining the constitutionality of the ordinance unless it was absolutely essential.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the nightclubs and patron and remanded for further proceedings.

 

21 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Crescent Towing & Salvage Co. v. Ormet Corp.


No. 97-C-1531


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-1531 (La. 09/09/98); 720 So. 2d 628; 1998 La. LEXIS 2487



September 9, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 23, 1998.
Certiorari Denied February 22, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1087.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.



DISPOSITION: The judgments of the lower courts are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant port commission, a public body, rented a marine cargo terminal to defendant lessee. Plaintiff tug companies brought suit against them, arguing that the lessee's exclusive employment of a competitor to provide tug service violated the Interstate Commerce Clause. They challenged the order of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit (Louisiana) affirming the trial court's denial of injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The lease provided that the lessee would use the terminal primarily for its own business; to the extent the terminal was not required for this purpose, it was to be made available to the public. In 1995, the lessee, believing that using its own tugs would be more cost-effective, entered into a contract with the competitor to provide tug service; previously, vessel owners had arranged for their own tugs. The court held that the commission's actions as a lessor of the terminal, acting in competition with other terminals, were those of a market participant, not as a market regulator, and that therefore there was no market regulation on which to base a Commerce Clause challenge. It held that the commission's acquiescence in the tug contract, by refusing to prohibit it, did not amount to state regulation for purposes of the Commerce Clause, writing that under U.S. Supreme Court precedent, when a private entity's decision was at most merely approved by or acquiesced in by the government, the private entity's action likely would not be characterized as state action. Here, it noted, the tug companies had not alleged that the commission compelled or encouraged the contract at issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision.

State v. Letulier


No. 97-KA-1360


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


750 So. 2d 784; 1998 La. LEXIS 2336



July 8, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 16TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARTIN, HONORABLE ANNE L. SIMON, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the 16th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Martin (Louisiana), for first degree murder and his death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder in the trial court and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court held that the trial court properly excused a potential juror pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 787 due to his knowledge of the case and his relationship with the family of one of the victims. The court determined that evidence of unadjudicated criminal conduct presented by the State did not inject an arbitrary factor into the penalty phase of defendant's trial by impermissibly shifting the jury's focus from his character and propensities to a determination of his guilt or innocence regarding the unrelated conduct. The court ruled that photographs of the victims were properly admitted because their probative value outweighed any prejudicial effect. The court held that evidence of violent acts by defendant was properly admitted to rebut evidence of his non-violent character. The court determined that defendant's death sentence was not constitutionally excessive or disproportionate considering his crimes and the evidence of his character.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder and his death sentence.

Conerly v. State


No. 97-C-0871


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


714 So. 2d 709; 1998 La. LEXIS 2338



July 8, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF OUACHITA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents brought medical malpractice, wrongful death, and survival actions against defendants, state hospital and employees. Judgment was for the parents but their recovery was capped pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39 of the Malpractice Liability for State Services Act. The Court of Appeal, Second Circuit (Louisiana) affirmed liability but allowed separate caps for the wrongful death and survival actions. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents' daughter was injured at birth and later died as a result of those injuries. On appeal, the state contended that the Malpractice Liability for State Services Act (MLSSA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39, limited the parents' recovery for their wrongful death and survival actions to a total recovery of $ 500,000. The supreme court found that the language of § 40:1299.39 was ambiguous. After a review of the legislative history and purpose of the MLSSA, the court determined that § 40:1299.39 provided a single cap applicable to the parents' wrongful death and survival actions resulting from the act of malpractice causing the death of their daughter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeal's holding that the cap applicable to the survival claim was separate from the wrongful death claims and reinstated the trial court's judgment capping the parents' total recoverable damages at $ 500,000.

 

24 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Fields v. State ex rel. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corrections


No. 98-C-0611


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


714 So. 2d 1244; 1998 La. LEXIS 2337



July 8, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 9, 1998. Case Final October 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Judge Robert Downing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Nineteenth Judicial District Court in the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) declared parts of 1997 La. Acts 1486, which authorized the impoundment of a vehicle when the operator failed to present statutorily required proof of insurance, to be unconstitutional. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff senators challenged the constitutionality of 1997 La. Acts 1486 which authorized an investigating officer to immediately impound a motor vehicle if the operator was unable to produce proof of statutorily mandated insurance. The trial court declared the law unconstitutional, and the state appealed. The court reversed and remanded. The senators' primary challenge was that the law violated motorists' rights under the Due Process Clause by not providing a hearing before their cars were impounded. Generally, before a person is deprived of a protected interest, he must be afforded some kind of hearing. However, there were circumstances involving a valid governmental interest which justified postponing the hearing until after the event. Three factors were evaluated and balanced to determine what process was due: (1) the private interest affected, (2) the risk of erroneous deprivation, and (3) the government's interest. The court held that the private interest affected here, ownership of a car, was only temporarily deprived and that deprivation was not final. There was also no great risk of error because motorists were presumed to know the law regarding proof of insurance.


OUTCOME: Judgment finding a legislative enactment that authorized the impoundment of a vehicle when the operator failed to present statutorily required proof of insurance to be unconstitutional was reversed and remanded.

Louisiana Seafood Mgmt. Council v. Louisiana Wildlife & Fisheries Comm'n


No. 97-CA-1367


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-1367 (La. 05/19/98); 715 So. 2d 387; 1998 La. LEXIS 1088



May 19, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE JANICE G. CLARK, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court, declaring La. Rev. Stat. 56:13.1 and La. Rev. Stat.56:305B(14)(a) unconstitutional and permanently enjoining the enforcement of those provisions, is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, seafood management council, commercial fishermen, wholesalers, and retailers, appealed a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which declared unconstitutional several portions of the Louisiana Marine Resources Conservation Act (Act), 1995 La. Acts 1316, and permanently enjoined the enforcement of those provisions by defendants, commission and department.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed a class action against defendants, asserting that the Act was unconstitutional in its entirety based on numerous violations of state and federal constitutional provisions. On appeal, the court concluded that construing the word "should" in the statute as permissive did not violate the title-object requirement. The court concluded further that former La. Rev. Stat. 56:640.3 was merely a hortatory provision directing that the legislature, as a policy matter, was to seek a recommendation from the department. The court found that the underlying premise for the district court's holding that plaintiffs possessed a vested incorporeal right to fish commercially was legally erroneous. Accordingly, the Act did not result in a taking of any property right--corporeal or incorporeal--possessed by plaintiffs. Given the mitigatory aim of the rod and reel provision of the statute in general, coupled with the specific pragmatic purpose of the requirement to restrict entry into the commercial fisheries market, the court concluded that the statutory classification had a rational basis and reversed the district court's finding of unconstitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment declaring portions of the Act unconstitutional and permanently enjoining the enforcement of those provisions.

Perfusion Servs. of Baxter Healthcare Corp. v. Foster


No. 98-CA-0056


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


98-0056 (La. 05/19/98); 711 So. 2d 695; 1998 La. LEXIS 1092



May 19, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE JEWEL "DUKE" WELCH, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant state challenged a judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, For The Parish Of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found that 1997 La. Acts 986, as codified in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:916(B)(1)(2)(3), was unconstitutional in prohibiting respondent corporation from receiving compensation for the "use" of products or equipment used in the performance of clinical perfusion services, and which granted a preliminary injunction.


OVERVIEW: The corporation sold and provided perfusion services, equipment, and supplies to hospitals and healthcare providers; it filed suit, seeking injunctive relief and a declaration that § 51:916 was unconstitutional. The trial court found that the statute was unconstitutional and unenforceable in prohibiting receipt of compensation for use of the corporation's products and equipment, but was otherwise constitutional. In order to provide for an orderly disengagement of contracts, the trial court enjoined enforcement of the constitutional portions of the statute for one year. On appeal, the court held that: 1) the trial court's finding of unconstitutionality was based on an incorrect interpretation of the word "use," as the statute was only intended to prevent the corporation from receiving compensation "from the sale or use" of equipment or services to a medical institution if it also provided perfusion services to that same institution; 2) the statute was not intended to prohibit perfusionists from being compensated for their services while using perfusion equipment; and 3) it was error to enjoin enforcement of a constitutional statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which found that a state statute prohibiting receipt of compensation for the "use" of products or equipment used in the performance of clinical perfusion services was unconstitutional. The court also reversed the trial court's one-year preliminary injunction against enforcement of the constitutional portion of the statute; and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

Ruiz v. Oniate


No. 97-C-2412


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-2412 (La. 05/19/98); 713 So. 2d 442; 1998 La. LEXIS 1093



May 19, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.



DISPOSITION: The court of appeal's finding that only employees with written employment contracts are covered "persons" under the MLSSA is reversed. With respect to all other arguments raised in Charity's application for certiorari, the writ is recalled and denied. We remand to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After plaintiff patient and various physicians settled a malpractice suit, the trial court rendered a judgment against defendant hospital. The Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) held that the statutory cap on damages set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39 did not apply to the hospital because its employees did not have a written contract with the state. The court granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The patient and the hospital tried the suit alleging malpractice as a result of the hospital's employees' failure to properly diagnose the patient. The patient and the hospital stipulated that the physicians were the hospital's employees. The trial court rendered a judgment in favor of the patient. The court of appeal held that the hospital was not entitled to the statutory cap on malpractice lawsuits set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39 because it did not prove that its employees had written contracts with the state. On appeal, the court held that the hospital's employees, for whom the hospital was vicariously liable, were covered persons under § 40:1299.39 as it existed. Therefore, the hospital was entitled to the benefit of the cap on malpractice damages, exclusive of future medical care and related benefits. The court reviewed the legislative history of the statute and concluded that when it was initially enacted it did not require a written contract. The purpose of the § 40:1299.39 was to provide protection to state health care workers by providing a cap on malpractice claims made against them even if they did not have a written contract.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeal's finding that only employees with written employment contracts were covered persons under the Malpractice Liability for State Services Act. The court remanded the case for further proceedings to address the patient's allegation that the cap on malpractice damages was unconstitutional. The court recalled and denied the writ on the other issues raised by the hospital.

Morgan v. ABC Mfr.


No. 97-C-0956


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-0956 (La. 05/01/98); 710 So. 2d 1077; 1998 La. LEXIS 1082



May 1, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 26, 1998. Released for Publication July 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIFTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED TO THE COURT OF APPEAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee filed an appeal on writ of certiorari from the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which affirmed the lower court's holding in favor of defendant general employer in the employee's negligence action.


OVERVIEW: An employee was injured by the negligent acts of a borrowed employee employed by a general employer but working under the supervision of the special employer. The employee filed suit and the trial court found for the general employer. The employee appealed and the lower court affirmed. On further appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case, holding that both the special and the general employers could be held liable for the torts of a "borrowed" employee. Where a general employer was in the business of hiring out its employees under the supervision of another employer, it remained liable for the torts of the "borrowed" employees. The court held that the labor provided by the general employer was its product, and the general employer should have borne the expenses and risks associated with its product, as well as reaping the benefits derived therefrom. The general employer's failure to exercise direct supervisory control over its employee should not have precluded its liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court in favor of the general employer and remanded the case.

Progressive Sec. Ins. Co. v. Foster

State v. Boyd


No. 97-KA-0579


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-0579 (La. 04/14/98); 710 So. 2d 1074; 1998 La. LEXIS 975



April 14, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF ORLEANS HON. PATRICK QUINLAN. ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Louisiana appealed a decision of the Criminal District Court, Parish of New Orleans (Louisiana), which quashed an indictment charging defendant with battery upon a police officer in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.2 because it was unconstitutionally vague under La. Const. art. V, § 5(D).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by indictment with battery upon a police officer, and he filed a motion to quash his indictment on the ground that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.2(B)(3) was unconstitutionally vague as to the language "injury that requires medical attention." The trial court quashed the indictment upon a finding that a portion of the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The State appealed, and the court reversed and remanded for a full trial on the merits. The court determined that the trial court's ruling was premature because the trial court quashed the indictment before any evidence was presented. The court concluded that the trial court could not have determined whether the statute was applied unconstitutionally against defendant without any facts before it. The court found that the clear and unambiguous wording of § 14:34.2(B)(3) meant that any battery of a police officer, which made it necessary for the officer to seek medical care primarily for the prevention of alleviation of an injury was required medical attention. The court concluded that even though the term might have been subjective in nature, it did not render § 14:34.2(B)(3) unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the district court's order quashing the indictment against defendant for battery upon a police officer.

 

31 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Langley


No. 95-KA-1489


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-1489 (La. 04/14/98); 711 So. 2d 651; 1998 La. LEXIS 982



April 14, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 19, 1998, Reported at: 1998 La. LEXIS 2092. Released for Publication June 19, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal From the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, For the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Honorable Fred Godwin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction and sentence of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which convicted him for murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for murdering a child and was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed his conviction on numerous grounds. The court rejected all of defendant's assignments of error. The defendant's desire to admit evidence of his attempt to plead guilty as remorse evidence was properly excluded as hearsay, as was a videotaped interview with a forsenic psychiatrist. Evidence of prior bad acts, consisting of diary entries detailing child molestation, was also admissible in light of the fact that defendant introduced them into evidence. Defendant's arrest on a Georgia parole violation that led to his confession was legal, as well as the confession itself, because there was no violation of due process in the delay in executing the warrant. The delay was reasonable based on defendant's flight from Georgia. The officers who arrested defendant did so under the authority of a valid warrant. Thus, their subjective intent to examine defendant about the murder was not significant. The exclusion of certain prospective jurors was not error where they indicated their opposition to the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence for murder.

Kimball v. Allstate Ins. Co.


97-CA-2885 c/w 97-CA-2956


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-2885 (La. 04/14/98); 712 So. 2d 46; 1998 La. LEXIS 983



April 14, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. HONORABLE ROBERT D. DOWNING, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two separate civil cases, the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105(C) to be a local or special law in violation of La. Const. art. III, § 12(A), and declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105(D) to be an unconstitutional delegation of the legislative authority to political subdivisions in violation of La. Const. art. XII, § 10(C).


OVERVIEW: The court stated that La. Rev. Stat. § 13:5105(C), which pertained to jury trials, concerned and affected not only an individual lawsuit, but, more egregiously, any and all lawsuits in which defendant City of Baton Rouge of the Parish of East Baton Rouge was made a party defendant. Consequently, § 13:5105(C) was a special law, which concerned civil actions and was unconstitutional under La. Const. art. III, § 12(A)(3), which prohibited the legislature from passing a local or special law concerning any civil or criminal actions. The court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105(D), which pertained to jury trials, did not contravene either La. Const. art. XII, § 10(C), which authorized the legislature to provide a procedure for lawsuits against public bodies, or any other constitutional provision argued and briefed by plaintiffs, two injured persons, associated individuals, and a vehicle driver, to the court. The court found that the district court did not rule on the retroactive application of either La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105(D) or Metropolitan Council of the City of Baton Rouge/Parish of East Baton Rouge, Res. 36859 (1996), which pertained to jury trials.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the judgment of the district court.

Caddo-Shreveport Sales v. Office of Motor Vehicles ex rel. The Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corrections


No. 97-CA-2233


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-2233 (La. 04/14/98); 710 So. 2d 776; 1998 La. LEXIS 978



April 14, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE JEWELL E. WELCH, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Louisiana Office of Motor Vehicles challenged an order from the Nineteenth Judicial District for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which was granted in favor of appellee parish tax collector and that declared La. Rev. Stat. § 47:303(B)(3)(a) and (b)(i) unconstitutional to the extent the Commissioner of the Louisiana State Office of Motor Vehicles was mandated to collect local sales and use taxes levied on motor vehicles.


OVERVIEW: Appellee filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment declaring La. Rev. Stat. § 47:303 unconstitutional. Appellee alleged that the statute unconstitutionally prohibited appellee from collecting locally levied sales and use taxes on motor vehicles. Appellee argued that La. Const. arts. VI, 29(A) and VII § 3(A) & (B) conferred upon the local governments the power to levy and collect all local sales and use taxes. The trial court declared La. Rev. Stat. § 47:303(B)(3)(a) and (b)(i) unconstitutional to the extent that it mandated the state Commissioner to collect local sales and use taxes levied on motor vehicles. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court held that the constitutional grant of authority to local governments to levy and collect local sales taxes prohibited the legislature from requiring local governments to agree that local taxes on motor vehicles would be collected by Office of Motor Vehicles. The court concluded that a statutory mandate that the local collector was required to agree to allow someone else to gather in the local taxes infringed on the intrinsic authority of the local collector conferred by the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that declared a statute unconstitutional and unenforceable to the extent that the state Commissioner was mandated to collect local sales and use taxes levied by political subdivisions on motor vehicles.

State v. Byrd


No. 96-KA-2302


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-2302 (La. 03/13/98); 708 So. 2d 401; 1998 La. LEXIS 251



March 13, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 24, 1998. Released for Publication April 24, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ACADIA, HONORABLE DON AARON, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Acadia (Louisiana), which quashed an indictment against defendants for violations of § 30:2183(G)(1) of the Louisiana Hazardous Waste Control Law (HWCL), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:2183(G)(1), on the ground that the provision was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted for violations of § 30:2183(G)(1), the "catch-all" provision of the HWCL. The State claimed that defendants knowingly stored hazardous waste at a facility without a permit. Defendants filed a motion to quash the indictment. The trial court granted the motion on the ground that § 30:2183(G)(1) was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings. The court held that the "catch-all" provision was not an unlawful legislative delegation of authority to the Louisiana Department of Environmental Quality because the HWCL contained a clear expression of legislative policy, prescribed sufficient standards to guide the department, and was accompanied by adequate safeguards. The court determined that § 30:2183(G)(1) was not unconstitutionally vague when considered within its regulatory context and that defendants had adequate notice of what conduct was prohibited. The court ruled that defendants failed to prove that they were not guilty as a matter of law of the crimes alleged in the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment quashing the indictment against defendants and holding that the "catch-all" provision of the HWCL was unconstitutionally vague. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

In re C.B.

State v. Muschkat


No. 96-KA-2922


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-2922 (La. 03/04/98); 706 So. 2d 429; 1998 La. LEXIS 245



March 4, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 4, 1998. Released for Publication March 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF CADDO, HONORABLE RAMONA EMANUEL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which found that the drug-traffic loitering statute, La. Rev. Stat. § 40:981.4, was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating the drug traffic loitering statute, La. Rev. Stat. § 40:98.4. Defendant filed a motion to quash the indictment alleging that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The trial court granted the motion to quash. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court held that the statute was vague because a person of reasonable intelligence could not know which conduct was prohibited and permissible and the statute delegated basic policy matters to the policemen, judges, and juries for resolution on an ad hod and subjective basis. The court found the statute could not be saved by reading into it a specific intent requirement where § 40:981.4 did not require specific intent in addition to an overt act because under La. Rev. Stat. § 40:981.4(D), intent was either shown by the overt act itself, or in certain instances, an overt act was not even required at all. The court concluded that § 40:981.4 was overbroad because it criminalized a substantial amount of constitutionally protected activities including standing on a public sidewalk or remaining in a public place.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that found the drug-traffic loitering statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.

State v. Johnson


No. 97-KK-1906


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-1906 (La. 03/04/98); 709 So. 2d 672; 1998 La. LEXIS 238



March 4, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 3, 1998. Released for Publication April 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED. REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The cause was before the court upon the grant of a writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) to review the trial court's downward departure from defendant's statutorily mandated sentence under the Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15.529.1, for possession of cocaine and marijuana.


OVERVIEW: The trial court noted that the mandatory minimum sentence for defendant, a fourth offender, was 20 years, but departed from this sentence and sentenced him to 30 months. The trial court stated that all of defendant's prior convictions were non-violent and that the instant crime was only possession of a residual amount of cocaine. The court held that although the trial court gave reasons for the sentence, it did not make a sufficient showing on the record that imposition of the statutorily mandated minimum sentence would be constitutionally excessive under these facts. The court did not find clear and convincing evidence to rebut the constitutionality of the mandatory minimum sentence in this case. In reviewing the statutorily mandated minimum sentence, the court found that the lack of prior violent crimes had been already factored into the minimum sentence, the possession of only a residue of cocaine or a crack pipe full of cocaine was insignificant under the law, and the 20-year sentence clearly contributed to the sentencing goals of punishment and deterrence.


OUTCOME: The sentence of the trial court was vacated and set aside. The cause was remanded to the trial court so that it could sentence defendant to the minimum required under the Habitual Offender Law, with a credit for time served.

State v. Robertson


97-KA-0177


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-0177 (La. 03/04/98); 712 So. 2d 8; 1998 La. LEXIS 244



March 4, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 3, 1998. Rehearing Denied April 3, 1998. Released for Publication April 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction and sentence are affirmed for all purposes, except that this judgment shall not serve as condition precedent to execution.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which convicted him upon a jury verdict of first degree murder, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30, and sentenced him to death. In his appeal, the defendant raised 37 assignments of error, implicating federal and state constitutional guarantees.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was indicted by a grand jury for two first degree murders, in violation of § 14:30. At an initial trial, the defendant was convicted as charged and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court reversed because the trial judge failed to sustain a particular challenge for cause by the defendant. On retrial, a jury again found the defendant guilty of the charges and recommended a sentence of death based upon a finding of aggravating circumstances. The second trial court subsequently entered the defendant's conviction and imposed the death penalty. On appeal from the second trial, the defendant raised 37 assignments of error, implicating federal and state constitutional guarantees. Upon review, the court affirmed both the conviction and the sentence, finding no reversible error. In particular, the court found no error in the jury selection at the second trial, in the trial court's admission of a confession where the defendant had not exercised his right to remain silent, in the state's use of prior crimes evidence during the penalty phase, or in the jury's finding of the "especially heinous" aggravating factor, given that ample evidence of torture had been presented.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction for first degree murder and his sentence of death. Specifically, the court rejected all of the defendant's assignments of error alleging violations of federal and state constitutional guarantees, including challenges to the jury selection, the admission of a confession, the state's use of prior crimes evidence during the penalty phase, and the jury's findings of aggravating circumstances.
