Soloco, Inc. v. Dupree


No. 97-CA-1256


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-1256 (La. 01/21/98); 707 So. 2d 12; 1998 La. LEXIS 4



January 21, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF LAFAYETTE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, horse owner and stabler, sought review of a judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:173.1 unconstitutional in actions brought by plaintiffs, employer and employee, against defendants for injuries and damages occurring when the owner's horse bolted onto a highway and collided with the employer's truck, which was driven by the employee.


OVERVIEW: The owner's horse was killed when it bolted onto a highway and collided with the employer's truck. The collision injured the employee and caused significant damage to the truck. Plaintiffs' actions against defendants were consolidated for trial. Defendants filed peremptory exceptions pursuant to § 4:173.1, which absolved a horse owner from liability for damages caused by his horse while in the custody of a third party except in cases of gross negligence. The trial court granted the employer's motion for declaratory judgment, holding that the statute was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that: 1) the law giving preference to race horse owners was rationally related to a legitimate state interest and, therefore, survived equal protection scrutiny; 2) because plaintiffs' cause of action never arose under state law, they were not deprived of a vested property right in violation of due process; and 3) although reasonable, the policy advanced by the district court was inconsistent with the policy determination already made by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which granted plaintiffs' motion for declaratory judgment in their personal injury action against defendants. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

In re Quirk


No. 97-O-1143


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-1143 (La. 12/12/97); 705 So. 2d 172; 1997 La. LEXIS 3359



December 12, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 26, 1997.



DISPOSITION: RECOMMENDATION REJECTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge challenged an order by the Judiciary Commission (Louisiana), which determined that he violated Canons 2A, 2B, 3A(1) and 3A(4) of the Code of Judicial Conduct, and engaged in willful misconduct relating to his official duty and public conduct prejudicial to the administration of justice.


OVERVIEW: The judge claimed that the Commission's findings should have been rejected because he was accused of sentencing defendants to church as part of their sentences. The court said that judicial independence was a cornerstone of the legal system. The judge also claimed that he was deprived of Due Process rights because he was not fairly apprised of the charges against him. The court agreed. It said that the judge was deprived of notice of the charges against him which arose not only from Louisiana court rules but also from basic principles of constitutional law. Procedural due process required fair notice of the charges. It was beyond dispute that procedural due process required that the judge be given fair notice before the formal hearing. Fair notice of the charge upon which the Commission sought to recommend discipline was a mandatory requirement. The court concluded that without such notice, the judge was unable to adequately prepare for or defend against the allegations of misconduct. The court also said that the judge had not violated the Cannons of the state.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the Commission's recommendation of discipline should be rejected.

Sudwischer v. Estate of Hoffpauir


No. 97-C-0785


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-0785 (La. 12/12/97); 705 So. 2d 724; 1997 La. LEXIS 3352



December 12, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ACADIA. JEFFREY P. VICTORY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant child sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit (Louisiana), which affirmed the trial court's judgment, finding that the child failed to prove filiation under the clear and convincing standard of La. Civ. Code Ann. art 209, which applied retroactively to the case and was not violative of the equal protection clause.


OVERVIEW: The child filed an action, seeking a portion of the deceased's estate, claiming to be the biological child of the deceased. The court held that La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 209, which required that the child prove filiation to the deceased by clear and convincing evidence while requiring that a child only prove filiation to a living parent by a preponderance of the evidence, was procedural and was to be applied retroactively. Based upon the record, the court held that the child failed to present evidence of actions by the deceased which were unequivocal and of sufficient frequency to constitute an informal acknowledgment under the clear and convincing standard of proof and that the DNA tests did not clearly and convincingly prove filiation. As to the equal protection challenge, the court held that the higher standard of proof where the alleged parent was deceased was substantially related to the state's interest in the orderly disposition of property at death because of the danger of fraud and the inability of the opponents to present evidence which might be available to the alleged parent if he were alive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court and held that the clear and convincing standard was retroactive and constitutional and that the child had not proven filiation by clear and convincing evidence.

Williams v. Department of Health & Hosps.

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-0055 (La. 12/2/97); 703 So. 2d 579; 1997 La. LEXIS 3351

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action by plaintiffs, the parents of patient, who was a minor, against defendants, a physician, a state hospital, and the State of Louisiana, the State appealed an order of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which on remand, held the State liable for damages in excess of the statutory cap imposed by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an action against defendants pursuant to the Malpractice Liability for State Services Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39 et seq., alleging that the patient, their son, was dependent on a drug used to treat his attention-deficit disorder. The court held that the abrogation of sovereign immunity demanded that governments be limited to the same defenses available to private citizens.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which held the State liable for damages in excess of a statutory cap. The court held that the statute imposing the cap on damages was not unconstitutional.

Livingston Downs Racing Ass'n v. State


No. 96-CA-2890


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-2890 (La. 12/2/97); 705 So. 2d 149; 1997 La. LEXIS 3342



December 2, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As amended. Rehearing Denied January 9, 1998. Dissenting Opinion Dated January 7, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, A. FOSTER SANDERS, III, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Louisiana sought review of a decision of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found in favor of plaintiff race track and determined that a portion of the Louisiana off track betting law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:211(5), was unconstitutional. The track claimed that the statute violated equal protection and that it was a prohibited local or special law.


OVERVIEW: The track owners were unable to conduct off-track betting at their establishment because they were not covered by the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:211(5). The track claimed that the statute benefited a special class of persons, namely those race tracks which were in operation during the 1986-87 racing season, without a compelling reason. The track argued that the law benefited a special class of persons and not the general public without a ration basis in violation of the equal protection clause contained at La. Const. art. 1, § 3. The court applied the rational basis test to determine whether the classification contained in the statute was rationally related to a legitimate government interest. The court held that it was designed to preserve the economic vitality of the race track industry which had been suffering from declining revenues. The court also held that the statute was not a local or special law prohibited by La. Const. art. 3, § 12 because it benefited the economy of the State as a whole by providing for a healthy horse racing industry.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and upheld the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:211(5).

Louisiana Associated Gen. Contr. v. New Orleans Aviation Bd.

DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant New Orleans Aviation Board (Board) appealed a decision of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff contractor and declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 38:2233.2 unconstitutional as violative of La. Const. art. I., § 3.


OVERVIEW: The Board established a program that set participation goals, preferences, and set asides on airport/heliport related contracts and procurements for firms owned by socially and economically disadvantaged persons. 48 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


No. 96-KA-1798


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-1798 (La. 10/21/97); 700 So. 2d 493; 1997 La. LEXIS 2867



October 21, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which granted defendant post-conviction relief and declared the statute under which he was convicted of driving while intoxicated, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98(A)(1)(b), unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for driving while intoxicated and was charged under § 14:98(A)(1)(b), which provided a lower blood alcohol level for persons under the age of 18. His sentence was deferred, he completed probation, and his conviction was set aside. He then filed an application for post-conviction relief under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 924, in which he challenged the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98(A)(1)(b) on equal protection grounds. The trial court declared the statute unconstitutional. On appeal, the court set aside the trial court's judgment and dismissed defendant's application for post-conviction relief. The court held that defendant was not entitled to seek relief under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 924 because he was not in custody at the time of filing his application. The speculative possibility that he might violate the law again and that the district attorney might use his prior conviction to enhance his future sentence or to serve as an element of the future crime was not sufficient to give defendant standing. Therefore, the court did not reach the issue of whether the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment declaring the statute unconstitutional and dismissed defendant's application for post-conviction relief.

 

49 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Albe v. Louisiana Workers' Compensation Corp.


No. 97-CC-0014 Consolidated with No. 97-CA-0581


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-0014 (La. 10/21/97); 700 So. 2d 824; 1997 La. LEXIS 2874



October 21, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Dissenting Opinion Dated December 12, 1997, Reported at: 1997 La. LEXIS 3358.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. ON APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKER"S COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION, DIVISION EIGHT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Louisiana Workers' Compensation Corporation, appealed the decision from the Office of Workers' Compensation Administration (Louisiana), which overruled the exception that a hearing officer did not have subject matter jurisdiction to decide constitutional questions in an action brought by plaintiff workers. Defendant employer appealed the decision that the denial of medical treatment to plaintiff employee was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The workers sought to declare certain statutes under the Worker's Compensation Act unconstitutional. The employee's benefits were terminated pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1201.4 when he was incarcerated. The hearing officer found that the denial of medical treatment and evaluation under the statute was unconstitutional. On appeal, the actions were consolidated and the court found that both decisions were incorrect. A hearing officer had no subject matter jurisdiction to decide constitutional matters. An administrative agency generally did not have the power to make constitutional decisions. Pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 16(A)(1) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.3(E), the Office of Worker's Compensation Administration was limited to deciding substantive claims. Judicial power to decide constitutional questions rested in the courts pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 1.


OUTCOME: The decisions of the hearing officers were both reversed and remanded. The hearing officers did not have subject matter jurisdiction to decide constitutional questions. Courts, not administrative agencies, decided constitutional issues.

 

50 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Reeder v. North


No. 97-C-0239


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


97-0239 (La. 10/21/97); 701 So. 2d 1291; 1997 La. LEXIS 2873



October 21, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated December 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIFTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT REINSTATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney sought certiorari review of a judgment from the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which reversed a decision from trial court and remanded the case for a trial on the merits. The trial court had found that plaintiff client's malpractice action was perempted under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605, and therefore dismissed client's suit.


OVERVIEW: The state supreme court granted the writ of certiorari to determine whether the court of appeal was correct in holding that § 9:5605 did not perempt client's legal malpractice suit even though client filed suit more than three years after the date of the alleged negligent act. After reviewing the record and the applicable law, the state supreme court held that the strict wording of § 9:5605 provided that client's legal malpractice suit was perempted. The state supreme court, however, remanded the case to the trial court to allow client to amend and to supplement his petition. Specifically, the state supreme court found that, under the clear wording of the statute, the court of appeal was wrong in holding that the peremptive period did not begin to run until the facts ripened into a viable cause of action sufficient to support a lawsuit, i.e., the date the U.S. Supreme Court denied certiorari. There was no doubt that the legislature intended that three years after the act, omission, or neglect, the cause of action was extinguished, regardless of when the negligence was discovered and regardless of whether a malpractice action might be brought within that three-year period.


OUTCOME: Accordingly, the judgment of the court of appeal was reversed and the judgment of the trial court, which sustained the exception of peremption was reinstated; however, the case was remanded to the trial court to allow client time to amend and to supplement his petition.

City of Baton Rouge v. Blakely


No. 96-KA-1742


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-1742 (La. 09/09/97); 699 So. 2d 1053; 1997 La. LEXIS 2476



September 9, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM BATON ROUGE CITY COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, JUDGE DONALD R. JOHNSON.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State appealed an order of the Baton Rouge City Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which granted in part defendant's motion to quash an indictment against defendant on grounds that the penalty exceeded the maximum penalty and amended the ordinance to provide a penalty not to exceed a fine of $ 200, imprisonment for 60 days, or both.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with misdemeanor theft, a violation of Baton Rouge, La., City Ordinances § 13:67, which carried a maximum penalty of six months in prison, a fine of $ 500, or both. OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's judgment granting in part defendant's motion to quash.

State v. Rome


No. 96-KA-0991


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-0991 (La. 07/01/97); 696 So. 2d 976; 1997 La. LEXIS 1712



July 1, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, SECTION D, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE SEET ASIDE, AND CASE REMANDED FOR RE-SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State challenged an order of the Criminal District Court, Section D, for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which sentenced defendant to five years at hard labor for vehicular homicide in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1, three of the five years suspended, and ordered the two remaining years served in home incarceration.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove a van into a group of people who were standing on the sidewalk watching a St. Patrick's Day Parade. While operating this van, defendant struck thirty-nine people, killing one person. Defendant was convicted of, among other charges not relevant, vehicular homicide in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1. The trial court sentenced defendant to five years at hard labor, three of the five years suspended, and ordered the two remaining years served in home incarceration. The State appealed. The court set aside defendant's sentence and remanded for resentencing, holding that under the clear language of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1 (B), the trial judge was required to sentence defendant to a minimum of two years imprisonment, of which, one year of that imprisonment was required to be without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence, that the trial judge was mandated to sentence the defendant to at least one year of imprisonment and did not have the option of suspending the defendant's sentence or placing the defendant on probation for at least one year, and that the sentence of home incarceration which was imposed in lieu of imprisonment was unlawful.


OUTCOME: The court set aside defendant's sentence and remanded the action for resentencing.

 

55 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Perschall v. State


No. 96-CC-0322


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-0322 (La. 07/01/97); 697 So. 2d 240; 1997 La. LEXIS 1713



July 1, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied. Released for Publication September 5, 1997.
Related proceeding at In re Office of Chief Justice, La. Supreme Court, 2012 La. LEXIS 1724 (La., June 13, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA.
Perschall v. State, 684 So. 2d 401, 1996 La. LEXIS 3162 (La., Nov. 8, 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, resident and registered voter of Orleans Parish, filed a declaratory judgment in state court that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:312.4 violated the state constitution, naming the state as defendant. It was removed to federal court and transferred to United States District Court for the Eastern District of Louisiana. After remand to state court, the court brought the case to it for argument and decision, ordering the lower courts bypassed.


OVERVIEW: The "Chisom" statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:312.4, passed to settle a federal voting rights claim regarding the state judiciary, created an additional seat on a court of appeal, and ordered the judge duly elected assigned to the supreme court as a justice. The court said it was faced with conflicting constitutional provisions regarding supreme court composition: (1) La. Const. art. V, § 3's limit of seven supreme court justices, and (2) La. Const. art. V, § 5(A)'s investiture in the supreme court of power to assign sitting or retired judges to any court. The court ruled that the statute was unconstitutional under La. Const. art. V, § 3, insofar as it effectively imposed an eighth justice on the supreme court, adding that the remaining portions of the statute were not severable; therefore, the entire statute was unconstitutional. However, the court ruled that the supreme court as it was currently composed should continue to function as a de jure court with its actions valid and effectual, and that the judge elected under the statute was not a usurper of an office, but rather, that judge's actions had been and would continue to be given de jure effect.


OUTCOME: The court declared the "Chisom" statute unconstitutional in its entirety. The court recognized the status quo would remain intact, and the court, as it was currently composed and operating, would continue to function as a de jure court.

City of Baton Rouge v. Knox


No. 95-KA-2850, 95-KA-3042


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2850 (La. 07/01/97); 697 So. 2d 262; 1997 La. LEXIS 1721



July 1, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant City of Baton Rouge sought review of two judgments from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which ruled in favor of defendants. Both judgments held that Baton Rouge, La., Code of Ordinance tit. 13:1019, was preempted by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1031 et seq. under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:143; and one also ruled that the ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city ordinance and the state statute both prohibited the distribution of drug paraphernalia. Defendants were charged with violation of the city ordinance, first offense. They filed motions to quash, which were granted. The court affirmed the trial courts' rulings on the nonconstitutional ground of preemption and did not consider defendants' constitutional arguments. The court rejected the City's argument that because the ordinance punished only first and second offenses, and under the state statute, only the third offense was a felony, the ordinance did not proscribe the "same offense" as did a state felony statute for purposes of double jeopardy, which was the established test for whether a municipal ordinance was preempted under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:143. The court noted that conduct that the municipality sought to prohibit was exactly the conduct proscribed by the state. Only the number of prior convictions distinguished between whether the conduct would be considered a misdemeanor or a felony; however, the conduct remained the same and it was this identity of conduct that impermissibly infringed on the state's right to define and punish felonies under state law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, on preemption grounds, the trial courts' judgments and did not reach the constitutional issues.

State v. Bourque

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-0842 (La. 07/01/97); 699 So. 2d 1; 1997 La. LEXIS 1717

Post-conviction relief dismissed at State ex rel. Bourque v. State, 760 So. 2d 308, 2000 La. LEXIS 970 (La., Mar. 17, 2000)
Post-conviction relief granted at State ex rel. Bourque v. Cain, 876 So. 2d 744, 2004 La. LEXIS 229 (La., Jan. 30, 2004)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by State v. Bourque, 2014 La. App. LEXIS 3149 (La.App. 3 Cir., Aug. 25, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 16TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ST. MARY, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE MICHAEL J. McNULTY, JR., JUDGE.
State v. Bourque, 622 So. 2d 198, 1993 La. LEXIS 2300 (La., 1993)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Mary (Louisiana), which, after he was convicted of first-degree murder, imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: At the sentencing hearing, the jury unanimously returned a verdict of death finding two aggravating circumstances: (1) that defendant knowingly created a risk of death or great bodily harm to more than one person; and (2) that defendant was engaged in the perpetration or attempted perpetration of aggravated burglary. The court affirmed the imposition of the death penalty, rejecting defendant's claims of error. The court held, inter alia, that the fact that the prosecutor told jurors during voir dire that they would be recommending, not inflicting, the death penalty was not reversible error, because given the entirety of the court's statements, no juror could have failed to appreciate the gravity of the jury's responsibility; given the prosecutor's use of strikes against both black and white prospective jurors and the number of black jurors actually seated on the jury, defendant did not establish that the State made discriminatory use of peremptory strikes; the jury instructions were proper; the capital sentencing scheme was constitutional; the sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive; and the sentence was not disproportionate to the sentences imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence for all purposes, except that the judgment should not serve as a condition precedent to execution until defendant failed to petition the United States Supreme Court timely for certiorari or the Supreme Court denied his petition for certiorari.

State v. Craig


No. 95-KA-2499


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2499 (La. 05/20/97); 699 So. 2d 865; 1997 La. LEXIS 1312

Writ of certiorari denied Craig v. Louisiana, 522 U.S. 935, 118 S. Ct. 343, 139 L. Ed. 2d 266, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6363 (1997)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Craig v. Cain, 750 So. 2d 176, 1999 La. LEXIS 2584 (La., Oct. 8, 1999)
Writ denied by, Sub nomine at State v. Maurer, 825 So. 2d 1186, 2002 La. LEXIS 2810 (La., Sept. 30, 2002)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Craig, 944 So. 2d 660, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2288 (La.App. 1 Cir., Oct. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE BONNIE JACKSON, JUDGE.
State v. Craig, 623 So. 2d 1341, 1993 La. LEXIS 2514 (La., 1993)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the 19th Judicial District Court (Louisiana) of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. This was a direct appeal from that conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and others stole a truck. After driving around with the owner for nearly an hour, defendant shot the victim several times at a secluded construction site. At trial, defendant initially pleaded not guilty, but later attempted to enter a guilty plea which the trial judge refused. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to enter a guilty plea, in failing to charge the jury that he was prevented from entering an unqualified plea of guilty, in denying his motion for mistrial, and in refusing to qualify a witness as an expert. As to sentencing, defendant contended that the jury's sentence was a result of passion, prejudice, arbitrariness, and caprice and that there was insufficient evidence of aggravating circumstances. After consideration, this court concluded that the court was correct in refusing to accept defendant's plea because it was not qualified, he was not entitled to the requested instruction, the state did not make impermissible closing arguments, and the witness was properly disqualified as an expert. In regards to the sentence, it was not the result of passion, it was proportionate, and there were aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Koon


No. 96-KA-1208


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-1208 (La. 05/20/97); 704 So. 2d 756; 1997 La. LEXIS 1318



May 20, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Limited Rehearing Granted June 30, 1997, Reported at: 1997 La. LEXIS 1711.
Rehearing granted by, in part, 06/30/1997
Adhered to, On rehearing at State v. Koon, 1997 La. LEXIS 1711 (La., July 2, 1997)
Writ of habeas corpus granted Koon v. Cain, 2008 U.S. App. LEXIS 9478 (5th Cir. La., May 1, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE MICHAEL R. ERWIN, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the 19th Judicial District Court, for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which convicted him of first degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30, and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 for killing his estranged wife and her parents, and was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed, finding no merit in any of defendant's assignments of error. The court determined that there was no reasonable possibility that defendant's statement to a detective and two detectives' comments about defendant's attitude could have contributed to a juror's decision to impose the death penalty. The court found that the record supported a conclusion that the jury understood that the weighing it was required to undertake was a qualitative, not quantitative, process. The court found that the state was entitled to the moral force of its evidence, and that postmortem photographs of murder victims were admissible to prove corpus delicti, to corroborate other evidence establishing cause of death, location, placement of wounds, as well as to provide positive identification of the victim. The court found that where defendant shot and killed three family members in cold blood, the death sentences were not disproportionate to the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a trial court's order convicting defendant of first degree murder and sentencing him to death, because there was no reasonable possibility that defendant's statement to a detective and two detectives' comments about defendant's attitude could have contributed to a juror's decision to impose the death penalty, and the death sentences were not disproportionate to the crime where defendant shot and killed three family members.

Dow Hydrocarbons & Resources v. Kennedy


No. 96-CA-2471


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-2471 (La. 05/20/97); 694 So. 2d 215; 1997 La. LEXIS 1309



May 20, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT CIVIL APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Secretary of the Department of Revenue and Taxation and the Attorney General of the State of Louisiana (collectively "state"), appealed a declaratory judgment from the 19th Judicial District Court of East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana) in favor of plaintiff, non-Louisiana corporations, that 1993 La. Acts § 690, which changed the corporate tax structure, violated La. Const. art. III, § 2(A).


OVERVIEW: The Louisiana legislature enacted 1993 La. Acts § 690 (Act). It amended provisions of Louisiana's corporate income tax law. The Act, inter alia, reclassified certain dividend income, with the result that a corporation not based in Louisiana but doing business in Louisiana had to pay income tax on dividends received from a controlled subsidiary that earned no income in Louisiana. The act also provided that a corporation based in Louisiana was not subject to corporate income tax on dividends received from a controlled subsidiary that earned no income in Louisiana.This increased taxes for non-Louisiana based corporations. The Louisiana Supreme Court ruled that because the Act increased taxes, at least for some corporations, it violated La. Const. art. III, § 2(A), which prohibited the enactment of tax increases during odd numbered years. The court rejected the state's suggestion that the court sever the offensive portion of the Act and leave the remainder intact. The court ruled that where the purpose of the statute was defeated by the unconstitutional portion, the entire act was void ab initio. The court ruled that it did not have authority for a judicial "line-item veto."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's declaration of unconstitutionality of 1993 La. Acts § 690 because it was a new tax increase enacted in an odd numbered year in violation of La. Const. art. III, § 2(A).

Jones v. Board of Ethics for Elected Officials


NUMBER 96-CC-2005


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-2005 (La. 05/09/97); 694 So. 2d 171; 1997 La. LEXIS 1207



May 9, 1997, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state senator sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, State of Louisiana, which held that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to issue a temporary restraining order against defendant Board of Ethics or to provide injunctive relief in a case concerning a challenge to the procedure of the Board of Ethics.


OVERVIEW: In response to a request from a state senator, the trial court granted a temporary restraining order, enjoining the Board of Ethics from proceeding with a public hearing on conflicts of interest charges brought against the state senator. The state senator sought injunctive relief, contending that the pre-hearing procedure of the board was fraught with due process violations and that the procedures to be used by the board were similarly flawed. The court of appeal vacated the temporary restraining order, finding that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to issue the temporary restraining order or to provide injunctive relief. On appeal, the court held that the trial court was vested with subject matter jurisdiction to decide a due process challenge to the procedure which the Board of Ethics utilized to determine an alleged violation of the Code of Governmental Ethics.

Safety Net for Abused Persons v. Segura


No. 96-CA-1978


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-1978 (La. 04/08/97); 692 So. 2d 1038; 1997 La. LEXIS 574



April 8, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 22, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE LOUISIANA COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF IBERIA, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the court of appeal declaring La. R.S. 13:1906 unconstitutional and vacating the writ of mandamus issued by the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant Safety Net for Abused Persons, Inc. sought review of a judgment of the Louisiana Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Iberia (Louisiana), that reversed the trial court's judgment and decreed in favor of respondent judges that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1906 (1992) violated the La. Const. art. VII, § 14 and unconstitutionally infringed on the powers of the judiciary in violation of the separation-of-powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court ruled that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1906 (1992) did not violate the La. Const. art. VII, § 14, but it also ruled that the imposition of a filing fee by § 13:1906 in all civil suits violated the right of access to the courts provided by the La. Const. art. I, § 22 and the separation-of-powers required by the La. Const. art. II, § 2; in addition, the court ruled that the imposition of a fee by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1906 (1992) in each criminal proceeding in which a fine, court costs, or a forfeiture was ordered violated separation of powers. The filing fee violated the right of access to the courts and separation of powers because its purpose, which was to fund domestic-abuse services, did not relate to the administration of justice. According to the court, domestic-abuse programs were worthy and necessary, but they were social-welfare programs that could not be funded by civil-suit filing fees collected by the courts pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1906.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the judges and against the corporation, the court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeal that declared the statute unconstitutional and that vacated the writ of mandamus issued by the trial court.

 

63 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Saizan


96-KA-1340


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-1340 (La. 04/08/97); 692 So. 2d 1045; 1997 La. LEXIS 577



April 8, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 22, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, which ruled that a portion of a Plan of Government of the City-Parish of Baton Rouge, depriving the parish attorney authority to nolle prosequi, was unconstitutional as a usurpation of the State's police power and violative of La. Const. art. VI, § 9(B).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested by the City police for violations of certain city ordinances. When the case was called for trial, the parish attorney realizing that he had excused his only witness moved to dismiss the charges against defendant without prejudice and indicated that he would re-file. The trial judge denied the motion to dismiss and the parish attorney announced that it would seek writs on the judge's ruling. However, the City never perfected its writ application and instead, the parish attorney dismissed the original affidavit and re-filed charges against defendant. In response, defendant filed a motion to quash, arguing that the City's failure to perfect its writ application resulted in a final judgment which dismissed the charges against him. The city court granted the motion to quash, the parish attorney sought review, the trial court reversed the ruling on the motion to quash and ruled that the parish attorney did not have the authority to nolle prosequi, and defendant sought review. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment, holding that there was no constitutional principle that prevented charges against defendant in several courts of concurrent jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the district court. The court remanded to the city court for further proceedings.

 

64 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Russell v. CSX Transp.


No. 96-CA-2151 c/w 96-CA-2362


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-2151 (La. 02/25/97); 689 So. 2d 1354; 1997 La. LEXIS 373



February 25, 1997, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiff employee, a non-resident, against defendant employer, alleging claims under the Federal Employers Liability Act, the employer sought review of an order of the Judicial District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which denied its motion to dismiss on the basis that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 123B, pertaining to forum non conveniens, violated the federal and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured in the employer's out-of-state facility. The employer filed a motion to dismiss for forum non conveniens because the employee resided out-of-state, all of the witnesses resided out of state, and the action involved only a federal cause of action. The trial court denied the motion, holding that La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 123B was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that the statute violated the Supremacy Clause of the U.S. Constitution because it discriminated against claims arising under federal law. The court found that the trial court did not have a valid excuse to refuse to enforce a federally created right when the parties were properly before the court because the statute did not fall within the valid excuse exception. The court held that because art. 123B contained no express provisions for the dismissal of state law causes of action and therefore, discriminated against federally created rights in violation of the Supremacy Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which denied the employer's motion to dismiss and held that the forum non conveniens statute unconstitutional.

 

65 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Gaspard v. Vanguard Acceptance Corp.


No. 96-CA-1177


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-1177 (La. 02/25/97); 689 So. 2d 1352; 1997 La. LEXIS 371



February 25, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL 15TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, purchasers of motor vehicles, sought review of a decision of the 15th Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which found in favor of defendant finance corporation and determined that the civil penalty provisions of the Motor Vehicle Sales Finance Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 6:960(C) were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After discovering that the corporation had been assigned hundreds of notes on cars purchased in Louisiana without a license, which was required under the statute, the Louisiana Motor Vehicle Commission imposed a fine on the corporation and the purchasers initiated a suit seeking civil penalties. The trial court found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 6:690(C) was unconstitutional and violative of due process because it contained an improper grant of judicial power to the executive branch and because it did not provide any guidelines to prevent arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement by the administrator of the Commission. The court found that the administrator's decision whether or not to impose a fine had no bearing on the purchasers' right to seek civil penalties under the statute. The trial court's finding of unconstitutionality had been erroneously based on its conclusion about the impact of the administrator's decision on the rights of civil litigants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded for further proceedings.

 

66 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Loyd


No. 96-KK-1805


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-1805 (La. 02/13/97); 689 So. 2d 1321; 1997 La. LEXIS 370



February 13, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI FROM THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIFTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of St. John the Baptist (Louisiana), which vacated the trial court's decision, based on constitutional grounds, to not give the commutation jury instruction mandated by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.2(B) at defendant's third penalty phase trial after his conviction for first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Before defendant's penalty phase trial on a conviction for first degree murder, the trial court issued an order refusing to give the jury instruction mandated by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.2(B) regarding the governor's power to commute a criminal sentence. On appeal by the State, the intermediate appellate court reversed. On defendant's further appeal, he argued that art. 905.2(B) could not be applied retroactively to his offense committed before its enactment. In affirming, the court ruled that art. 905.2(B) was authorized by La. Const. art. I, § 16, did not change the definition of first degree murder or deprive defendant of any defenses, and had only an attenuated relationship to any increase in punishment. The court held, therefore, that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.2(B) was not an ex post facto law. The court also ruled that the Due Process Clause did not prohibit the jury instruction and that defendant had the right to offer evidence regarding the frequency and extent of gubernatorial commutations. The court held that the jury instruction was a neutral statement of the law and did not materially affect the balance between mitigating and aggravating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

 

67 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Succession of Gilbert


No. 96-C-0949


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-0949 (La. 02/07/97); 689 So. 2d 1314; 1997 La. LEXIS 368



February 7, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Dissenting Opinion Dated February 13, 1997.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both plaintiff heirs and spouse sought review of an order from the trial court (Louisiana), which ruled that none of the donations inter vivos made by the decedent to the heirs and to the spouse should be included in the mass estate in determining the legitime. The court of appeal reversed that part of the judgment of the trial court that exempted the donations inter vivos to the spouse from the action for reduction.


OVERVIEW: This was an action by the heirs, who were the decedent's daughters of his first marriage, against the decedent's surviving spouse for reduction of the decedent's mortis causa and inter vivos donations to the spouse that were alleged to be in excess of the disposable portion. The principal issue was whether the decedent's two sets of inter vivos donations to his daughters, each set made in equal amounts in the same calendar year, must be added back fictitiously into La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1505's compilation of the mass estate for the purpose of calculating the legitime, or whether the donations fall within the exemption of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1502. The critical issue in the present case was the legislative intent of the exemption in the second paragraph of art. 1502. The court found that the equal gifts in the same year to all descendants by roots were not subject to reduction, but unequal gifts in one year or gifts made in different years were reducible and were to be included in the calculation of the legitime because the art. 1502 exemption did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal insofar as it exempted the donations inter vivos to the heirs from inclusion in the mass estate and the calculation of the legitime.

 

68 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hart


No. 96-KA-0599


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-0599 (La. 01/14/97); 687 So. 2d 94; 1997 La. LEXIS 7



January 14, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF WASHINGTON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE PATRICIA HEDGES, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: The motion to quash is reversed and the case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from the judgment of the 22nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Washington (Louisiana), which on a motion to reconsider granted defendant's motion to quash the indictment for malfeasance in office on the grounds that the phrase "any other sexual conduct" contained in the statute, La. Rev. Stat. § 14:134.1, was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant prison guard was indicted for malfeasance in office in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:134.1. Specifically, he was charged with having sexual intercourse with a female prisoner and engaging in sexual conduct by facilitating two male prisoners to have sexual intercourse with two female prisoners. The court reversed the trial court's judgment granting his motion to quash because the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The term "any other sexual conduct" was not vague because it was sufficiently specific enough to alert a person as to what conduct was proscribed. The legislature intended to make the statute as broad as possible to prohibit any and all conduct that might be interpreted as sexual --given the nature of the relationship between prisoners and those who exercised direct authority over them while incarcerated. Despite the changes that could occur in sexual standards in the general population, it was clear that any and all conduct of a sexual nature between those persons designated in § 14:134.1 and an inmate was intended to be illegal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which granted defendant's motion to quash.

 

69 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Cameron Parish Sch. Bd. v. Acands, Inc.


No. 96-CA-0895


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-0895 (La. 01/14/97); 687 So. 2d 84; 1997 La. LEXIS 11



January 14, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring in Part and Dissenting in Part Opinion Dated January 31, 1997. Rehearing Denied February 21, 1997. Released for Publication February 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 38th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CAMERON, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: RULING OF UNCONSTITUTIONALITY VACATED; EXCEPTION OF PRESCRIPTION GRANTED; DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school board appealed the judgment of the 38th Judicial District Court, Parish of Cameron (Louisiana), which held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5644 was unconstitutional as a violation of due process insofar as it purported to revive the school board's prescribed cause of action against defendant asbestos manufacturer.


OVERVIEW: The school board filed an action against several parties, including the asbestos manufacturer, in which the school board sought recovery of costs for the removal of asbestos material used in the construction of three school buildings. The asbestos manufacturer filed a peremptory exception of prescription which, after a hearing, was granted by the trial court. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5644, relative to prescription of actions involving asbestos abatement, was declared unconstitutional by the trial court insofar as it purported to revive already prescribed causes of action. Pursuant to La. Const. art. 5, § 5(D), the school board brought a direct appeal to the court. The court affirmed the trial court's decision that the claim was prescribed under the law existing prior to the enactment of § 9:5644 and found that § 9:5644 did not contain the required clear and unequivocal expression of intent by the legislature to retroactively apply the statute so as to revive prescribed causes of action. The court vacated the constitutional ruling because it was not necessary to the resolution of the claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the asbestos manufacturer's exception of prescription to the school board's cause of action and vacated the trial court's ruling of the unconstitutionality of the asbestos prescription statute.

 

70 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


City of Baton Rouge v. Goings


No. 95-KA-2542


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2542 (La. 12/13/96); 684 So. 2d 396; 1996 La. LEXIS 3352



December 13, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 27, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL BATON ROUGE CITY COURT PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city appealed from a judgment of the Baton Rouge City Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), that found that a city ordinance was preempted by the federal act. Appellant claimed that the court had jurisdiction under La. Const. art. 5, 5(D).


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that a city ordinance was preempted by a federal act and the city appealed under La. Const. art. 5, § 5(D). The court held that it lacked jurisdiction and transferred the case to the appropriate court of appeal. Under art. 5, § 5(D), a case is appealable if an ordinance is declared unconstitutional. The court held that the finding by the trial court that the ordinance was preempted by a federal law was not a declaration of unconstitutionality, and as such, jurisdiction was not proper. The court concluded that a finding that this court lacks jurisdiction under La. Const. art. 5, § 5(D) where a trial court finds that an ordinance has been preempted by a federal statute is consistent with the view that this court lacks jurisdiction when a trial court finds that an ordinance has been preempted by a state law.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the case to a court of appeals.

 

71 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilson


No. 96-KA-1392 consolidated with No. 96-KA-2076


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-1392 (La. 12/13/96); 685 So. 2d 1063; 1996 La. LEXIS 3351



December 13, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Rehearing Denied December 30, 1996. Released for Publication December 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT PARISH OF OUACHITA. APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF ORLEANS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state sought review of two judgments from the Fourth Judicial District Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), and from the Criminal District Court Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which granted defendants' motions to quash the indictments of aggravated rape of girls under the age of 12.


OVERVIEW: In two different cases, the lower courts granted defendants' motions to quash indictments that charged defendants with aggravated rape of girls under the age of 12. The issue before the court was whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42(C), which authorized the death penalty for offenders who raped a victim under the age of 12, was constitutional. The court disagreed with the lower courts and found § 14:42(C) constitutional. Defendants argued that death was a disproportionate penalty for the crime of rape because no life had been taken. However, given the appalling nature of the crime, the severity of the harm inflicted upon the victim, and the harm imposed on society, the death penalty was not excessive for the crime of rape when the victim was under 12 years old. Also, the class of defendants eligible for the death penalty was sufficiently narrow so as not to lead to arbitrary and capricious application. Finally, the court gave great deference to the legislature in its determination of the appropriateness of a death penalty in cases of rape of a child under 12 years old. The court reversed the motions to quash the indictments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower courts' judgments, which granted defendants' motions to quash the indictments of aggravated rape of girls under the age of 12, because the statute that authorized the death penalty for offenders who raped a victim under the age of 12 was constitutional.

Whitnell v. Silverman


No. 95-C-0112 Consolidated with 95-C-0259


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-0112 (La. 12/06/96); 686 So. 2d 23; 1996 La. LEXIS 3350



December 6, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated December 16, 1996. Rehearing Denied December 30, 1996. Released for Publication December 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA.

ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient and spouse filed a medical malpractice action against defendant physicians. The physicians sought review of a judgment by the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which held that the statute of limitations provision in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 was unconstitutional as applied to the patient and to causes of action for diseases with a latency period of over three years.


OVERVIEW: The patient and spouse filed a medical malpractice suit against the patient's physicians. The patient and spouse asserted that a pathology report diagnosed a pre-cancerous lesion, which had a high likelihood of developing into bladder cancer, and that the physicians failed to disclose the information. The physicians filed an exception of prescription on the basis that the action was filed after the three-year statutory limitation as provided in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. The court held that the claim was barred under § 9:5628 because: (1) the patient's condition was discoverable within the three-year limitation period, (2) the patient had no standing to challenge § 9:5628 in its application to individuals with diseases that had latency periods in excess of three years, (3) the court was without power to render judgment over hypothetical third parties with diseases with latency periods in excess of three years, (4) evidence regarding diseases with latency periods in excess of three years was irrelevant, and (5) the patient had no standing to raise an equal protection challenge because she did not fit within a class of individuals disadvantaged by a statutory classification.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeal judgment, which held that a statute of limitations was unconstitutional as applied to the patient and spouse in a medical malpractice action against physicians. The court also reversed the ruling that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to diseases with latency periods longer than three years.

Med Express Ambulance Serv. v. Evangeline Parish Police Jury


No. 96-CA-0543


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-0543 (La. 11/25/96); 684 So. 2d 359; 1996 La. LEXIS 3224



November 25, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE THIRTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EVANGELINE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant parish policy jury sought direct appeal of a judgment from the Thirtieth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana), which, in a suit brought by respondent ambulance service, held that Evangeline Parish, La., Code art. II, §§ 24-20 through 24-32 were unduly vague and violative of the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of both the U.S. and Louisiana Constitutions, and stuck down the ordinances.


OVERVIEW: The ordinances regulated parish-wide ambulance services and required that any service wishing to operate within the parish obtain a permit from the police jury president or his designee. The ambulance service was denied a permit after a determination was made that there was no need for additional ambulance services on a parish wide basis, and it sought injunctive relief as well as a declaration that the ordinances were unconstitutional. The trial court granted the relief requested. On review, the court reversed. The court found that, applying the rational relationship test, the ordinances did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV's Equal Protection and Due Process Clauses. The court further found that the health, safety, and welfare of citizens were appropriate government interests, and the ordinances furthered those interests. Therefore, the ordinances did not violate La. Const. art. I, § 3. Similarly, because the ordinances did not affect a fundamental right and were rationally related to a legitimate government interest, they did not violate La. Const. art. I, § 2's due process protections. Finally, the court held that the ordinances were not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the ruling of the district court that declared the ordinances unconstitutional. The court reversed the judgment granting the ambulance service a preliminary injunction and ordering the police jury to issue a permit to the ambulance service and dismissed the ambulance service's action.

Shell Oil Co. v. Secretary, Revenue & Taxation


No. 96-C-0929


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-0929 (La. 11/25/96); 683 So. 2d 1204; 1996 La. LEXIS 3229



November 25, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certiorari to review a judgment from the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which affirmed a district court judgment reversing a judgment of the Board of Tax Appeals. The Board had ruled that applicant oil company did not have to pay severance taxes assessed by respondent State Department of Revenue and Taxation on oil and gas produced under mineral leases granted by the U.S. Department of Interior.


OVERVIEW: The mineral leases covered land within the confines of an air force base. The taxes were assessed for 1980-1986. Initially, the oil company took the position that the imposition of the taxes for any period violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 17. On review, the oil company abandoned that argument and argued that collection of the taxes was not authorized under state law until the effective date, in 1982, of an amendment to La. Rev .Stat. Ann. § 52:1, which clearly authorized the collection of the taxes. The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment, holding that the taxes were collectible for the entire period. The court noted that in a 1954 case, it had held that neither the federal constitution nor La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 52:1 prohibited the imposition of the taxes. However, since the date of that decision, the U.S. Court of Appeals for the Fifth Circuit, claiming to be basing its judgment on a decision of the U.S. Supreme Court, had held to the contrary. The court concluded that the Supreme Court decision had not decided the precise issue presented, that the Fifth Circuit's reliance had been misplaced, and that the court was not bound to follow the Fifth Circuit judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

State v. Cousan


No. 94-KA-2503


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-2503 (La. 11/25/96); 684 So. 2d 382; 1996 La. LEXIS 3233



November 25, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE EIGHTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF WINN.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Parish of Winn (Louisiana), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of shooting a police officer while trying to escape from apprehension. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding, inter alia, that a statement made by defendant to a police officer, that he had shot the victim but that the shooting was accidental, was voluntarily made even though defendant had not been informed that the victim had died, and that claims of error relating to the guilt stage of the proceeding were not preserved for review absent a contemporaneous objection in the trial court. However, the court held that the trial court erred at the penalty phase of the trial by instructing the jury on the governor's clemency power in accordance with the 1993 version of La. Code Crim. A later constitutional amendment, which provided constitutional authority for the enactment of a statute that would require trial courts to inform the jury of the governor's clemency power, did not apply retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but vacated the sentence and remanded the case to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing.

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2307 (La. 11/25/96); 684 So. 2d 350; 1996 La. LEXIS 3226

Stat. Ann. § 51:712(A)(2) and § 51:721(A), (B) were unconstitutional.

State v. Strickland


No. 94-KA-0025


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-0025 (La. 11/01/96); 683 So. 2d 218; 1996 La. LEXIS 2871



November 1, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied December 13, 1996. Released for Publication December 13, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF VERNON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE TED R. BROYLES, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: FIRST DEGREE MURDER CONVICTION AFFIRMED; DEATH SENTENCE CONDITIONALLY AFFIRMED; REMANDED TO THE DISTRICT COURT FOR EVIDENTIARY HEARING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Thirtieth Judicial District Court, Parish of Vernon (Louisiana), which found him guilty of first degree murder, armed robbery, and conspiracy to commit the armed robbery and sentenced him to death, claiming that the trial court failed to sever the charges, failed to suppress illegal evidence, improperly conducted voir dire, and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed and shot an assistance manager outside of a bank, who was making a night deposit. Defendant was charged and convicted of first degree murder, armed robbery, and conspiracy to commit the armed robbery. Defendant was sentenced to death, and challenged his conviction and sentence. The court held that defendant failed to show prejudice in being tried on all three counts, and therefore the trial court did not err in not severing the indictment. The court also determined that evidence introduced at trial was not illegally obtained, because the police had consent and probable cause to search the trailer was defendant was hiding. The court further stated that the trial court correctly conducted voir dire, and did not improperly exclude jurors who were biased against the death penalty. In addition, the court was not able to find that the prosecutor's comments during opening arguments were improper or prejudicial. Finally, the court concluded that the evidence was inconclusive to prove ineffective assistance of counsel, and remanded back to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing on defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, and held that defendant was properly convicted of first degree murder, armed robbery, and conspiracy to commit the armed robbery. However, the court remanded back to the trial court to conduct an evidentiary hearing on defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim.

Triangle Marine v. Savoie


Nos. 95-C-2873, 95-C-2885, 95-C-2899, 95-C-2904


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2873 (La. 10/15/96); 681 So. 2d 937; 1996 La. LEXIS 2618



October 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiff taxpayers against defendant parish to determine the legality of ad valorem taxes, the taxpayers challenged a judgment from the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit (Louisiana), affirming the grant of summary judgment that dismissed the taxpayers' suit as premature.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers brought suit against the parish alleging that the ad valorem taxes on the taxpayers' vessels were unconstitutional. The taxpayers alleged that they were engaged in international trade and that their vessels were exempt under La. Const. art. 7, § 18. The court of appeal found that the challenge was to the validity of the ad valorem tax and was not a constitutional challenge. The court dismissed the suit for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. On appeal to the supreme court, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that a challenge to the validity of a tax on exempt property was a challenge to the legality, not the correctness, of the tax. A tax assessment on exempt property was illegal. Instituting suit directly in the district court pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2110 was the appropriate method for challenging a tax levy on exempt property. The court concluded that the challenge was not a challenge to such issues as over-valuation and mis-description.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

Miller v. Oubre


No. 96-CA-2022


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-2022 (La. 10/15/96); 682 So. 2d 231; 1996 La. LEXIS 2619



October 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEAL, FIFTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: St. Charles Parish sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of St. Charles (Louisiana), which found in favor of plaintiffs, two justices of the peace and a constable, and determined that ward and precinct lines which were redraw pursuant to an ordinance adopted by the Parish council were unconstitutional. The court enjoined the conduct of elections except in accordance with districts established in 1991.


OVERVIEW: The crux of this case was the Parish's argument that as a post-1974 Home Rule government it had power concurrent with the state Legislature to enact justice of the peace and constable redistricting ordinances. The Parish sought to exercise this function by enacting an ordinance with created seven districts where there had previously only been six. The court found that under La. Const. arts. V and VI as well as under the St. Charles Parish Home Rule Charter that the state legislature was vested with the sole authority to affect redistricting in the Parish. The court concluded that district lines drawn in 1982, 1991, and 1996 were all constitutionally infirm but the court declined to remove any elected officials from office. The court called upon the Legislature to rectify the problem in its next session by providing for new districts and provided that the parties could apply for a rehearing if the Legislature failed to act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court.

 

81 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Teel v. DOT & Dev.


No. 96-CA-0592


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-0592 (La. 10/15/96); 681 So. 2d 340; 1996 La. LEXIS 2691



October 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 15, 1996. Released for Publication November 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: DECLARATION OF UNCONSTITUTIONALITY VACATED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development sought review of a judgment of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans, State of Louisiana, which held the department 50 percent liable in plaintiff driver's negligence and strict liability action. The district court further decided that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800 violated La. Const. art. XII, § 10(A).


OVERVIEW: The driver's van was traveling on a state highway when he saw the vehicle in front of him hydroplane on heavy roadway water. While assisting that distressed motorist he was struck by a third vehicle that had come into contact with the same water accumulation and hydroplaned. The driver suffered the loss of his left leg. He sought damages from the department alleging negligence and strict liability. The district court held the department partly liable and declared that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800 was unconstitutional because it was a vestige of sovereign immunity in violation of La. Const. art. XII, § 10(A). The department sought review. On appeal, the court vacated the declaration of unconstitutionality because a court should not pass on the constitutionality of legislation unless it was essential to the decision of the case or controversy. The court held that it was not essential to the case to decide constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800 because where a trial court found negligence on the part of the department, the court need not resort to strict liability under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2317 to find liability on the part of the department.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the declaration of unconstitutionality, declined to address the constitutionality of the legislation, and remanded to the appellate court to consider the remaining issues raised by the parties.

 

82 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State ex rel. Department of Pub. Safety & Corrections, La. Gaming Control Bd.


No. 96-CA-2204


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-2204 (La. 10/15/96); 680 So. 2d 1179; 1996 La. LEXIS 2692



October 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied October 18, 1996, Reported at: 1996 La. LEXIS 3727.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. INJUNCTION ISSUED. REHEARING DELAY LIMITED TO FORTY-EIGHT HOURS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State of Louisiana, through the Department of Public Safety and Corrections and the Louisiana Gaming Control Board, sought review of a judgment from the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana in favor of plaintiff, a video gaming licensee, declaring La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 27:13(C)(6) unconstitutional insofar as it restricted contributions to committees supporting or opposing issues.


OVERVIEW: The video gaming licensee wished to contribute to an advertising fund promoting video poker. He sought a declaration that § 27:13(C)(6) was unconstitutional insofar as it restricted contributions to committees supporting or opposing issues. The trial court rendered judgment in his favor and issued a preliminary injunction. On appeal, the court affirmed. Because the statute regulated U.S. Const. amend I rights, the court applied strict scrutiny. Although gambling activity was strictly regulated, the State could not ban commercial speech simply because it could regulate the underlying conduct. The State could not restrict contributions to a political committee organized to communicate ideas. The court held that the statute was unconstitutional insofar as it prohibited contributions to committees supporting or opposing ballot measures. It enjoined the State and the Board from enforcing § 27:13(C)(6) and from enforcing the Board's Emergency Rule 107 insofar as they prohibited contributions, expenditures, and loans to independent committees unconnected with candidates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and enjoined defendants from enforcing the statute and an implementing rule insofar as they prohibited contributions to committees supporting or opposing issues.

State v. Roy


No. 95-KA-0638


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-0638 (La. 10/04/96); 681 So. 2d 1230; 1996 La. LEXIS 2469



October 4, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 15, 1996. Released for Publication November 15, 1996. Certiorari Denied April 21, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2584.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, Honorable Alfred A. Mansour, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana),which convicted defendant of two counts of first degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant broke into the home of his former girlfriend, stabbed her husband to death, robbed her of $ 50.00, tied her and the children up, slit their throats, then stabbed her 75-year-old aunt to death. The girlfriend and children survived and testified. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court held that challenges for cause were properly denied for two venirepersons, one who initially said she would automatically vote for the death penalty if she found defendant guilty and another who said he could not consider intoxication in mitigation, when they both later agreed they could follow the law. The court found that the prosecutor's improper statements that defendant was presumed "to intend the natural consequences of his actions" did not require reversal when the trial judge correctly instructed the jury. The court found no abuse of discretion in disallowing voir dire on race, when the crime was not interracial. The court noted that an aggravating circumstance was clearly established by the murder of more than one person, thus, the failure of any of the other aggravating circumstances found by the jury would not invalidate the death penalty verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court judgment.

 

84 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


In re Succession of Villarrubia


No. 95-C-2610


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2610 (La. 09/05/96); 680 So. 2d 1147; 1996 La. LEXIS 2087



September 5, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Rehearing Denied October 11, 1996. Released for Publication October 11, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI. FOURTH CIRCUIT COURT OF APPEAL.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent executor sought a writ of certiorari, seeking to overrule an order of the Court of Appeals (Louisiana), which found that petitioner heir had not waived his right to bring a motion to re-open succession after signing a receipt for legacy.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner heir's father predeceased petitioner's grandmother. When the grandmother died, petitioner considered bringing an action against his uncles for a greater share of the estate, but, instead signed a receipt for legacy consenting to a judgment of possession. Days after signing the receipt, petitioner learned that the state supreme court had declared a state statute limiting forced heirship unconstitutional and had decreed that "no law shall abolish forced heirship." Petitioner then sought to re-open the succession. The trial court denied the motion, finding that petitioner had waived his right to bring suit by acquiescing to the judgment. The lower court reversed, finding that because there were no forced heir rights when the judgment was signed, petitioner could not have waived such a right. The court reversed, holding that, pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 3393B, an error in law was not a valid reason to re-open a succession, nor was an assertion of forced heirship rights. The evidence demonstrated that petitioner knew the law was in limbo regarding forced heirship at the time he signed the judgment.


OUTCOME: Petition for writ of certiorari was granted because the lower court erred in ruling that petitioner heir was entitled to re-open a succession. The law clearly prohibited such re-opening for assertion of forced heirship rights or an error in law.
