State v. Sandifer


No. 95-KA-2226


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-2226 (La. 09/05/96); 679 So. 2d 1324; 1996 La. LEXIS 2095



September 5, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 19, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the trial court on Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which found in favor of defendant and concluded that as applied to the facts of this case, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95(E) violated the double jeopardy clause and was unconstitutionally overbroad, and quashed the bill of information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested by officers who discovered him in his car with three marijuana cigarettes, some cocaine, and two firearms. He pled guilty to a misdemeanor marijuana charge and the trial court dismissed the bill of information against him which charged him with violating La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95. This statute provided that it was illegal to possess firearms and illegal drugs at the same time. Although the trial court reasoned that double jeopardy attached because defendant had already pled guilty to the marijuana charge, the court found that the cocaine charge was still pending and held that the State should be afforded an opportunity to amend its bill of information and avoid that attachment of double jeopardy. The court held that the statute was not vague because the work possess could be given its ordinary meaning. Defendant raised various scenarios where the statute could be overbroad or where it could be applied to abridge equal protection, but the court concluded that the trial court erred in finding the statute overbroad on the basis of a hypothetical scenario.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case.

 

86 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


McAlpine v. McAlpine


No. 94-C-1594


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1594 (La. 09/05/96); 679 So. 2d 85; 1996 La. LEXIS 2257



September 5, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion of February 9, 1995, Reported at: 1995 La. LEXIS 600.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband appealed the decision of the Fourth Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana), which reversed the trial court's ruling in part. The court of appeal held that the antenuptial agreement was void but affirmed the trial court's decision with respect to the automobile.


OVERVIEW: The husband and the wife signed an antenuptial agreement. The wife filed a rule to show cause why she should not be awarded permanent alimony pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 112 and why she should not have a car returned to her, claiming it was a gift from the husband. The trial court held the antenuptial agreement was enforceable, that the car was not a gift, and dismissed the wife's rule. The court of appeal reversed the trial court's ruling in part, holding the antenuptial agreement was against public policy and therefore void. The court granted the husband's writ of certiorari and originally affirmed. The court then reversed its original opinion holding that (1) permanent alimony was not a law enacted for the public interest but to protect individuals and therefore the prohibition found in La. Civ. Code art. 7 did not apply; (2) antenuptial agreements were enforceable, but were subject to the same grounds for rescission as other contracts; (3) the wife entered into the antenuptial agreement freely and voluntarily and not under undue duress; and (4) the trial court was not manifestly erroneous in finding that the car was not a gift to the wife.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal, reversing the trial court's dismissal of the wife's claim for permanent alimony. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court holding that the car was not a gift to the wife.

 

87 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Milstead v. Diamond M Offshore


No. 95-C-2446


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2446 (La. 07/02/96); 676 So. 2d 89; 1996 La. LEXIS 1699; 1996 AMC 2431



July 2, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI THIRD CIRCUIT COURT OF APPEAL.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applying Louisiana's manifest error standard of appellate review in examining plaintiff employee's state court suit against defendant employer under the Jones Act and general maritime law, the Third Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana) affirmed a judgment for plaintiff employee as amended and affirmed the award of prejudgment interest on all of damages, past and future. The employer sought certiorari review therefrom.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that federal principles of appellate review were not binding upon Louisiana courts in the exercise of concurrent maritime jurisdiction, and that Louisiana's manifest error standard of review controlled. Further, the court held that federal law precluded the award of prejudgment interest on future damages. Standards of appellate review were not characteristic features of general maritime law, and application of Louisiana's state standards of appellate review did not interfere with the proper harmony and uniformity of general maritime law. Thus, Louisiana appellate courts applied the state manifest error standard of review in general maritime and Jones Act cases. The court, however, agreed with the employer's argument that the trial court erred in awarding prejudgment interest on the Jones Act award. The trial court had discretion to grant prejudgment interest on the sums awarded as past damages in the employee's general maritime and Jones Act claims. However, the trial court lacked authority to grant interest on the general maritime and Jones Act awards for future damages, whether future lost earnings or future pain and suffering.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court for recalculation of the damages but affirmed the judgment for the employee in all other respects.

Manuel v. State


No. 95-CA-2189


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2189 (La. 07/02/96); 677 So. 2d 116; 1996 La. LEXIS 1693



July 2, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring Opinion Dated July 12, 1996. Released for Publication July 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EVANGELINE, STATE OF LOUISIANA.

Original Opinion of March 8, 1996, Reported at: 1996 La. LEXIS 597.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is reversed, and plaintiffs' action is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, class of purchasers and retailers, brought suit against the state challenging the constitutionality of the statutes imposing penalties for selling alcoholic beverages to persons under 21. The Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline, State of Louisiana granted a preliminary injunction prohibiting the state from enforcing any of the prohibitions.


OVERVIEW: The class of purchasers and retailers (the class) challenged the constitutionality of Act 639 of 1995 and seeking both declaratory and injunctive relief. The trial judge granted a temporary restraining order, prohibiting the state from enforcing any prohibition against the purchase, possession, service or sale of alcoholic beverages to persons between the ages of 18 and 21. After the hearing on the preliminary injunction, the trial judge granted the class declaratory relief, ruling that Act 639 of 1995 constituted arbitrary age discrimination in violation of La. Const. art. I, § 3 and also granted injunctive relief, prohibiting enforcement of the unconstitutional statutes. The state appealed. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and dismissed the action. The court held that the purpose of the statute was to curtail the ready availability of alcohol to inexperienced drivers and drinkers in the age group. The court found that the exceptions to the statute were reviewed in accordance with the division of control between the state and parents and the statutory exceptions did not undermine the statute's furtherance of the governmental purpose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and dismissed the class' action.

Smith v. Department of Health & Hosps.


No. 95-C-0038


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-0038 (La. 06/25/96); 676 So. 2d 543; 1996 La. LEXIS 1609



June 25, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 3, 1996. Released for Publication September 3, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF OUACHITA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff medical malpractice claimants sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana). Claimants wanted the court to address the method of valuation of the damages recoverable for the loss of a chance of survival in a medical malpractice case.


OVERVIEW: Claimant's husband had gone into the hospital for routine foot surgery. His hospitalization had included a routine chest x-ray which the staff radiologist reported as showing a mediastinal mass. He was discharged from the hospital without any information about the mass in his chest. When he returned 15 months later, he was diagnosed with lung cancer from which he died 19 months after the initial x-ray. Claimant then filed the instant medical malpractice action. The court of appeals had rejected claimants' contention that they were entitled to full damages for the death, noting that claimants had failed to prove, more probably than not, that decedent would have survived but for the malpractice. The court disagreed and stated that allowing recovery for the loss of a chance of survival was a recognition of the loss of a chance of survival as a distinct compensable injury caused by the defendant's negligence, to be distinguished from the loss of life in wrongful death cases, and there was no variance from the usual burden in proving that distinct loss.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeal was set aside, and the case was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

Plaquemines Parish Gov't v. Getty Oil Co.


No. 95-C-2452


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2452 (La. 05/21/96); 673 So. 2d 1002; 1996 La. LEXIS 1044



May 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1996. Released for Publication June 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF PLAQUEMINES, STATE OF LOUISIANA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parish government sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of Plaquemines (Louisiana), which affirmed a trial court judgment holding that a mineral lease remained in full force and effect and denied the parish government's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: A parish government filed suit asking the court to declare that mineral servitudes on compromise lands and the lease with which the servitudes were burdened were expired. The parish government also sought an accounting from an oil company for the production from the expired servitude areas since the dates they allegedly reverted to the parish. A group of heirs intervened to protect their interests and filed a motion for summary judgment seeking to have their lease recognized as binding on 100 percent of the compromise lands. The trial judge concluded that the heirs' lease remained in full force and effect as to the full 100 percent mineral interest in the expired servitude area and therefore denied the parish government's motion for summary judgment. The court of appeal affirmed and the parish government sought further review. The court noted that the heirs' lease, granted in 1928, survived a 1930 consent decree and was granted by a landowner, not a mineral servitude owner. The court therefore affirmed the court of appeal's judgment because it held that the termination of other servitudes had no effect on the validity of the lease and that the lease remained valid and binding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeal in favor of the heirs.

Rhodes v. State ex rel. DOT & Dev.


No. 95-CA-1848


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-1848 (La. 05/21/96); 674 So. 2d 239; 1996 La. LEXIS 1046



May 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF REVIEW TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, 1ST CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: DECLARATION OF UNCONSTITUTIONALITY VACATED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development (state), sought review of a judgment de novo of the Court of Appeal (Louisiana), which (1) held that the notice provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800 were unconstitutional, and (2) granted a judgment in favor of appellees, the motorists #1 and #2, on their strict liability claims for damages after a car accident that resulted from a malfunctioning traffic light.


OVERVIEW: Motorist #1 and motorist #2 brought actions, alleging negligence and strict liability against the Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development (DOTD) and the Louisiana Department of Public Safety and Corrections (DPSC) arising out of an automobile accident when a traffic light malfunctioned. The trial court granted judgment for defendants. Upon review, the court of appeal determined that the notice provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800, which required that defendants have actual or constructive notice of the defective traffic signal, were unconstitutional, and held that the DOTD was liable for damages under strict liability principles. The DOTD filed a writ to review. The court ruled that that it was not necessary for the court of appeal to determine the constitutionality of the notice provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800, because it had to first evaluate the negligence claim brought by the motorists. The court held that that only if the court of appeal determined that the motorists failed to prove their negligence claim should the court of appeal determine the constitutionality of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the court of appeal's judgment, which declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800 unconstitutional and remanded the case.

Blanchard v. State ex rel. Parks & Rec. Comm'n

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-0053 (La. 05/21/96); 673 So. 2d 1000; 1996 La. LEXIS 1048

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARTIN, HONORABLE MICHAEL J. MCNULTY PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State, through the Parks and Recreation Commission, appealed from an order of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Martin (Louisiana), which declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's estate filed suit against the State, claiming that the decedent was killed at a park due to inadequate shelter from a lightening storm. The State filed an exception of no cause of action under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1, which provided immunity to the State under certain circumstances. The trial court overruled the exception. The decedent's estate then filed a motion in limine, seeking a declaration that the statute was unconstitutional as a resurrection of the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The trial court granted the motion. The court reversed. The trial court erred in ruling on the constitutionality of the statute before determining whether the statute applied at all. The fact that the trial court overruled the State's exception under the statute was not a definitive ruling by the trial court that the statute was inapplicable. The trial court should have proceeded to trial on the merits instead of addressing prematurely the constitutionality of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order.

Louisiana Republican Party v. Foster


No. 96-CA-0314


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


96-0314 (La. 05/21/96); 674 So. 2d 225; 1996 La. LEXIS 1161



May 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART. The Republican Party is given 15 days from the date of finality of this judgment in which to file its plan with the Secretary of State under R.S. 18:443.1.B. as it was amended by Act 949 of 1992.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which declared that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 18:443.1.B, 18:443.2(7), and 18:443.1.A, as applied to the Louisiana Republican Party, were unconstitutional. The State obtained a direct appeal to the court pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 5(D).


OVERVIEW: The Louisiana Republican Party filed suit challenging the constitutionality of 1995 amendments to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 18:443.1.B. and 18:443.2(7) as well as the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:443.1.A. The suit sought an injunction of the enforcement of the statutes and a declaration that the statutes were unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV and La. Const. art. I, §§ 7 and 9 (1974). The trial judge issued a temporary restraining order and declared that the three statutes, as applied to the party, were unconstitutional. On appeal, the State argued that it had an interest in insuring the application of the one-person, one-vote principle. The court held that the principle was not applicable in the context of an election of members to the Republican Party State Central Committee and could not justify the state's infringement on the party's freedom of association. The court found that §§ 18:443.1.B. and 18:443.2(7), as amended, unconstitutionally violated the party's right of freedom of association and affirmed the judgment as to those statutes. The court vacated the portion of the judgment that declared § 18:443.1.A. to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment insofar as it declared two amended statutes unconstitutional. The court vacated the trial court's declaration that a third statute was unconstitutional.

State v. Jackson

March 22, 1996, Decided

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State, claiming a constitutional question, appealed from the judgment of the Parish of Orleans Criminal District Court, Division "E" (Louisiana), which reduced defendant's bail and ordered him released on two unsecured personal surety bonds.


OVERVIEW: The State invoked the court's appellate jurisdiction pursuant to La. Const. Art. V, § 5(D), claiming that the district court had declared La. Code Crim. Proc. V, § 10, but such an appeal was moot because the State had dismissed the charges against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court treated the state's appeal as an application for supervisory writs and denied the application as moot.

 

95 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Campbell


No. 95-K-1409


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-1409 (La. 03/22/96); 670 So. 2d 1212; 1996 La. LEXIS 602



March 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari to the Third Circuit Court of Appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certiorari to review a judgment from the Third Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana), which held that a jury's return of a non-responsive verdict of attempted jury tampering, an error invited by the trial court's incorrect listing of responsive verdicts, operated as an implicit acquittal of jury tampering, the charged offense; and that double jeopardy barred defendants' retrial.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with three counts of jury tampering. The jury returned verdicts of attempted jury tampering on all counts and the trial court sentenced defendants to two years at hard labor. On appeal, the appellate court held that the verdicts returned by the jury were not responsive to the charged offense and vacated defendants' convictions and sentences. The appellate court further held that the jury's verdicts had nevertheless acquitted defendants of the charged offense and that double jeopardy principles thus precluded their retrial for jury tampering on double jeopardy grounds. The court ordered defendants discharged from further prosecution. On review, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court agreed that the unresponsive verdicts of attempted jury tampering constituted a patent error, which required reversal of the convictions. However, because, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:129, attempted jury tampering was jury tampering and not a lesser-included offense, the court could not say that the jury meant to acquit defendants of any material element of the charged crimes. Therefore, the court held that a retrial would not constitute double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the appellate court's decision reversing defendants' convictions and sentences, vacated the appellate court's order discharging defendants from custody, and remanded the case to the district court for further proceedings in accordance with the law.

State v. Powell


No. 96-KD-0282

97 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Manuel v. State


No. 95-CA-2189


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2189 (La. 03/08/96); 692 So. 2d 320; 1996 La. LEXIS 597



March 8, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted July 2, 1996, Reported at: 1996 La. LEXIS 1693.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EVANGELINE, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state and officials (collectively, state), challenged a decision of the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana), which held that statutes that prohibited the purchase by, sale to, or purchase on behalf of, alcoholic beverages by persons under 21years old, and which provided sanctions for those actions, were unconstitutional under La. Const. art. I, § 3.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, adults under 21 years of age and purveyors of alcohol, challenged the constitutionality of legislation rendering illegal the sale of alcohol to adults under 21. The challenged statutes were La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:93.10 - 14:93.14, 26:90, and 26:286. The evidence showed that in Louisiana, 18- to 20-year-olds were not the group responsible for the greatest number of alcohol-related accidents. The court held that the state's objective of increased highway safety was neither directly implicated nor substantially furthered by the discriminatory classification of those under 21. The court noted that there were several non-discriminatory alternatives available. The court held that the classification contained in the challenged statutes undercut countervailing interests of the state. Although the state's objective of continued receipt of its full share of federal highway funds was an understandable and desirable goal, it was, nevertheless, not legitimate. The state's inability to obtain certain discretionary federal funds did not suffice as a legitimate reason for the presumptively unconstitutional discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's declaration that the challenged statutes unconstitutionally discriminated on the basis of age.

 

98 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Louisiana Associated Gen. Contrs. v. State ex rel. Div. of Admin., Office of State Purchasing


No. 95-CA-2105


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2105 (La. 03/08/96); 669 So. 2d 1185; 1996 La. LEXIS 598; 64 U.S.L.W. 2608



March 8, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state and its agencies and officials, appealed from the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which entered an order temporarily enjoining defendant state health agency from treating a construction project as a minority set aside under the Louisiana Minority and Women's Business Enterprise Act (Act), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 39:1951 et seq., and granted plaintiff association's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court determined that association had standing because the interests it sought to protect were germane to its organizational purposes. In addition, the individual members had a real and actual interest in the case. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because it determined that under the Act certified minority businesses were able to bid on approximately 100 percent of the public works and procurement contracts let by the state, while non-minority businesses were only able to bid equally on approximately 90 percent of such contracts put out to bid by state agencies. The court found that the act violated La. Const. art. III, § 3, which prohibited the state from denying any person the equal protection of its laws and which also prohibited state laws from discriminating against a person because of race. The court determined that the wording of Louisiana's guarantee of equal protection was clear and unambiguous and that it had to be applied as written. The section on its face absolutely prohibited any state law which discriminated on the basis of race regardless of whether the intent of the law was to rectify past discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

99 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. RLCC Technologies


No. 95-CA-2621


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2621 (La. 02/28/96); 668 So. 2d 1135; 1996 La. LEXIS 608



February 28, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 14, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALDWELL, HON. RONALD L. LEWELLLYAN, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the judgment of the trial court declaring La. Rev. Stat. 23:1032 and La. Rev. Stat. 23:1061 unconstitutional is reversed. This case is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, employer and employees, appealed the decision of the Thirty-Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Caldwell (Louisiana), which declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 23:1032's grant of tort immunity to a principal or statutory employer of an injured employee of the direct employer unconstitutional in the declaratory judgment action of plaintiff decedent's wife arising out of her husband's wrongful death.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff decedent's wife filed a complaint for wrongful death. Defendants, employer and employees, asserted a grant of immunity pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 23:1032. Plaintiff amended her complaint to include a request for a declaratory judgment that § 1032 was unconstitutional. At trial, § 1032 was found to be unconstitutional and defendants appealed. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court. The court found that the discrimination alleged was not expressly prohibited by La. Const. art. I, § 3. Thus, the classification of statutory employees and direct employees was presumed constitutional, and the burden of proving unconstitutionality was placed on plaintiff as the party seeking to invalidate the provision. Plaintiff failed to show that the classification created by § 1032 did not suitably further any appropriate state interest. Section 1032 was found not to violate La. Const. art. I, § 22, because access to the judicial process was not essential to the exercise of a fundamental constitutional right. Thus, the legislature was free to allow access to the courts in any system or classification that was not totally arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which declared the exclusivity provision of the Louisiana Workers' Compensation Act unconstitutional. The court found that plaintiff decedent's wife failed to prove that the provision did not further any appropriate government interest. The provision had been invoked for immunity purposes by defendants, employer and employees, at trial.

Deumite v. State


No. 95-CA-1263


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-1263 (La. 02/28/96); 668 So. 2d 727; 1996 La. LEXIS 610



February 28, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 14, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT CIVIL APPEAL FROM 18TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, POINTE COUPEE PARISH.



DISPOSITION: DECLARATION OF UNCONSTITUTIONALLY VACATED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Department of Wildlife and Fisheries, challenged a judgment of the 18th Judicial District, Pointe Coupee Parish (Louisiana), which declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2795(E) to be an unconstitutional grant of sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother brought an action on behalf of the teenage son seeking damages based upon theories of negligence and strict liability against the Department of Wildlife and Fisheries (DWF) when their son sustained spinal injuries when he dove off a boat into a lake bottom. The DWF asserted immunity under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2795(E). The trial court rejected the immunity defense and awarded the father and mother $ 7,654,425 in damages plus medical expenses and loss of consortium. The trial court held that the statute was an unconstitutional grant of sovereign immunity, and improperly treated the DWF and private landowners differently. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that it was unnecessary for the court to rule on the constitutionality of the statute, because, under the circumstances, where the son was using the lake for recreational purposes at the time of the accident, the trial court could apply the same recreational use standards imposed upon private landowners in determining the DWF's liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's declaration of unconstitutionality, finding that the declaration was not essential to the resolution of the case.

 

101 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tart


No. 93-KA-0772


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-0772 (La. 02/09/96); 672 So. 2d 116; 1996 La. LEXIS 388



February 9, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 10, 1996. Rehearing Denied May 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISHES OF OUACHITA AND MOREHOUSE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE MICHAEL S. INGRAM, PRESIDING JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parishes of Ouachita and Morehouse (Louisiana) convicted defendant of murder and sentenced him to death. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly stabbed the elderly owners of a jewelry store to death for at least 15 to 30 minutes, cutting their carotid arteries, jugular veins, and larynxes. He was discovered in possession of some of the stolen jewels and arrested. A cellmate testified that defendant confessed to the homicides, and defendant later made the same confession to police. The reviewing court upheld the conviction and sentence. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the state to remove for cause a juror who expressed "mixed feelings" about the death penalty. Defendant's counsel did not have an actual conflict of interest because he never cross-examined a state's witness who had been a former client, so defendant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel. His confession to police was voluntary because he only invoked his right to counsel when questioned earlier on stolen property charges. He did waive this right days later when questioned on the murder charge, so his Miranda rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The conviction and death sentence were affirmed.

State v. Kelly


No. 95-K-2335


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-2335 (La. 02/02/96); 666 So. 2d 1082; 1996 La. LEXIS 310



February 2, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] IN RE: State of Louisiana; - Plaintiff(s); Applying for Writ of Certiorari and/or Review; to the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Number 95KA-0861; Parish of Orleans Criminal District Court Div. "H" Number 373-298.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State applied for a writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, which affirmed defendant's conviction of simple burglary and his sentence to 28 months at hard labor, which was below the statutory minimum of six years mandated for a second offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of simple burglary and adjudged a second offender. The trial court sentenced him to serve 28 months at hard labor, which was less then the minimum sentence of six years mandated by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. The court of appeal affirmed. The court granted the State's application for review and vacated the sentence. The court determined that that the trial court failed to make a proper finding that the imposition of the statutorily mandated sentence would have been excessive.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the court of appeal's judgment, and remanded the case to the trial court to justify its deviation from the statutorily mandated minimum sentence.

Williams v. Department of Health & Hosps.


No. 95-CA-0713


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-0713 (La. 01/26/96); 671 So. 2d 899; 1996 La. LEXIS 260



January 26, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State appealed from a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which determined that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39 was unconstitutional. The statute established a $ 500,000 limitation on the state's liability in medical malpractice cases. Plaintiff parents brought this malpractice action against the state after their son was hospitalized for Ritalin dependency.


OVERVIEW: Parents brought a medical malpractice action against the state after their son, who had been diagnosed as hyperactive, was hospitalized for Ritalin dependency and a possible overdose. The trial court found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39, which limited the amount of liability that could be assessed against the state in a medical malpractice action to $ 500,000, was unconstitutional and awarded the parents in excess of $ 2 million. On review, the court held that before it could determine whether the statute was unconstitutional, it first had to decide whether the issue of constitutionality was properly raised below. The parents claimed that they gave the state formal notice in the form of a letter, and the state failed to raise any objections. The court found, however, that the challenge was not raised in the form of a formal pleading as required by law. The court held that the issue had to be specifically pleaded, and the parties had to be allowed sufficient time to brief and prepare arguments regarding their position on the constitutionality issue. The issue was remanded to the trial court for hearing.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter so that both sides could present arguments as to the constitutionality of the statute that limited the amount of liability that could be assessed against the state in a medical malpractice action.

 

104 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Board of Comm'rs v. Board of Comm'rs


No. 95-CA-1353


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-1353 (La. 01/16/96); 666 So. 2d 636; 1996 La. LEXIS 178



January 16, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 16, 1996. Released for Publication February 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT CIVIL APPEAL FROM THE EIGHTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF WEST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff board commissioners of the North Lafourche Conservation, Levee, and Drainage District appealed a judgment of the Eighteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of West Baton Rouge (Louisiana), made in favor of defendant board commissioners of the Atchafalaya Basin Levee District by ruling that 1992 La. Acts 876 was unconstitutional, inter alia, in that it authorized taxation above the maximum set out in the La. Const. art. VI, § 39(A).


OVERVIEW: 1992 La. Acts 876 created the North Lafourche Conservation, Levee, and Drainage District (NLD) so as to overlap two previously existing levee districts: one of which was the Atchafalaya Basin Levee District (ABD). The court ruled that the legislature had violated the La. Const. art. VI, § 38 (1974) by creating the NLD geographically on top of two previously existing levee districts, which included the ABD, already serving the same purposes. Section 38 provided that the legislature could mandate by law the consolidation, division, or reorganization of existing levee districts or could create new levee districts.The court ruled that there had not been a consolidation, division, or reorganization of existing levee districts by the formation of the NLD. The court also ruled that the creation of the NLD did not fall within the legislature's power to create new levee districts; the court held that this power clearly implied that there only be one levee district per geographical area.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the Atchafalaya Basin board commissioners and against the North Lafourche Conservation board commissioners, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Manuel v. Louisiana Sheriff's Risk Management Fund


No. 95-C-0406


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-0406 (La. 11/27/95); 664 So. 2d 81; 1995 La. LEXIS 2885



November 27, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 11, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF IBERVILLE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant insurer filed a writ of certiorari seeking review of the decision of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of Iberville (Louisiana), which reversed the trial court's decision that sustained a peremptory exception of no cause of action in an action for damages by respondents, husband and wife, for the alleged violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1220(B)(2).


OVERVIEW: The husband was severely injured when his car was struck by the insured's car. The insurer settled with the husband and wife. The insurer paid the settlement funds 68 days after the settlement was reduced to writing. The husband and wife brought a damages action for failure to pay the settlement funds within 30 days, as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1220(B)(2). Section 22:1220(B)(2) became effective subsequent to the date that the insurance policy was issued and after the date that the accident occurred. However, § 22:1220(B)(2) was in effect when the settlement was reduced to writing. The trial court sustained the insurer's peremptory exception of no cause of action. The appellate court reversed the trial court's decision. The court affirmed the appellate court's decision and held that the subject matter of § 22:1220(B)(2) was unrelated to that of the insurance policy. Insurance policies were invulnerable to charges that they impaired contractual obligations. Retroactivity was not an issue because the conduct that granted the husband and wife a cause of action was the failure to pay the settlement within 30 days, and it happened after the enactment of § 22:1220(B)(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court, which reversed the trial court's decision, and held that the application of a statute to conduct occurring after the statute's enactment was prospective in nature, in favor of the husband and the wife in their damages action against the insurer for late payment. The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Matherne v. Gray Ins. Co.


No. 95-CA-0975


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-0975 (La. 10/16/95); 661 So. 2d 432; 1995 La. LEXIS 2540



October 16, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 30, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 17th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFOURCHE. HONORABLE JEROME J. BARBERA, III, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party defendant Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development sought review of a judgment of the 17th Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafourche (Louisiana), which declared that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800B was unconstitutional as a violation of La. Const. art. XII, § 10(A) in an action brought by third-party plaintiffs, an insurer and another.


OVERVIEW: La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800B limited the department's public entity liability. A tort action was brought against third-party plaintiffs after a car accident on a state highway. Third-party plaintiffs alleged that the fault and negligence of the department caused the accident. The department denied liability, contending that negligent driving caused the accident. Alternatively, the department argued that if it was found that the highway and its shoulder were defective, then the department asserted that it did not have notice of the defect or a reasonable period of time in which to correct the defect. Third-party plaintiffs then filed a motion asking the district court to "strike" the notice requirement of § 9:2800B because the department failed to plead the defense timely or alternatively to have the statute declared unconstitutional. Ruling on this motion, the district judge declared § 9:2800B unconstitutional. The department sought review. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. The court held that until the circumstances surrounding the department's knowledge of the defect in the road were determined, it was premature to pass on the constitutional issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court and remanded for further proceedings.

Bellard v. Louisiana Correctional & Indus. Sch.


No. 95-C-0157


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-0157 (La. 10/16/95); 661 So. 2d 430; 1995 La. LEXIS 2542



October 16, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 30, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF REVIEW TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate challenged by writ of review a judgment from the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, State of Louisiana, which affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing with prejudice the inmate's action against defendants, the State, a prison, and its warden, citing the inmate's failure to timely pursue his administrative remedies under the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed he injured his knee falling from his top bunk at the prison, then re-injured it entering a prison van. The inmate filed an action against defendants seeking monetary damages for negligently failing to protect him from injury. After the case was transferred to the trial court defendants responded with exceptions of improper venue, lack of subject matter jurisdiction, no right or cause of action, and abandonment. The trial court dismissed the action, holding that the inmate had forfeited his prisoner tort grievance by not timely pursuing administrative remedies. The appellate court affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed. The trial court erred in failing to maintain the exception of improper venue and to transfer the remaining issues to a court of proper venue. The Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure was the inmate's exclusive remedy for his tort claim. Venue for appeal of an adverse decision under that act lay exclusively in the 19th Judicial District Court. The inmate's action was remanded for transfer to the 19th Judicial District Court. The remaining exceptions could then be acted upon in the trial court of proper venue in the interests of justice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the inmate's action against defendants. The court remanded the inmate's action to the trial court with an order that the action be transferred to the 19th Judicial District Court for further proceedings.

City of Baton Rouge v. Williams


No. 95-KA-0308


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


95-0308 (La. 10/16/95); 661 So. 2d 445; 1995 La. LEXIS 2546



October 16, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 30, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE BATON ROUGE CITY COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a ruling of the Baton Rouge City Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which held that it was within the court's discretion to allow the hearing of a motion to quash a citation charging defendant with disturbing the peace on the ground that the city ordinance under which the offense was charged was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was cited for disturbing the peace in violation of Baton Rouge, La. Ordinance 13:103. After pleading guilty, defendant withdrew his plea and filed a motion to quash the citation on the ground that the ordinance was unconstitutional in that it imposed a penalty in excess of that imposed by the state for the same offense and it violated the Equal Protection Clause because it subjected defendant to the possibility of a different punishment for the same offense under state law. The prosecutor objected to the motion on the ground that it was not timely filed before trial. The trial court trial court ruled that it was within its discretion to allow the hearing of the motion and granted the motion. On appeal, the city argued that the trial court erred in its ruling because the ordinance violated no statutory or constitutional principles. The court reversed the trial court's decision because it held that the ordinance did not constitute an abridgement of the police power of the State of Louisiana and did not violate the constitutional guarantee of equal protection. The court also noted that the penalty did not exceed the limit set by the city's home rule charter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

109 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Prejean v. Dixie Lloyds Ins. Co.


No. 94-CA-2979


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-2979 (La. 09/15/95); 660 So. 2d 836; 1995 La. LEXIS 2372



September 15, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion of May 22, 1995, Reported at: 1995 La. LEXIS 1375.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurance guaranty association sought review of a decision of the trial court (Louisiana) that found it responsible for all court costs attributable to the tortfeasor's liability insurer, whether they arose prior to or after the liability insurer's insolvency. The suit was filed by plaintiff to recover injuries he sustained in an automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was injured in an automobile accident in 1989. The tortfeasor's liability insurer was declared insolvent on May 17, 1993. On the date of the accident, there was no statutory provision that limited the insurance guaranty association's exposure for court costs. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1379(3)(d), became effective on September 7, 1990 and a determination was made that § 22:1379(3)(d) was substantive in nature and could only be applied prospectively. Subsequently, the insurance guaranty association was held responsible for all court costs attributable to tortfeasor's liability insurer, whether they arose prior to or after its insolvency. In reversing the decision, the court held that the law in effect on the date of the insurer's insolvency, rather than the law in effect on the date of the accident, should have been used to determine the insurance guaranty association's liability for court costs. Plaintiff acquired the right to sue the liability insurer, but not the insurance guaranty association, on the date of the accident. Plaintiff's cause of action against the insurance guaranty association did not exist until tortfeasor's liability insurer was declared insolvent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that ordered the insurance guaranty association to pay the outstanding court costs originally assessed to the tortfeasor's liability insurer and ruled that the statute in question applied prospectively to exempt the insurance guaranty association from liability for the preinsolvency court costs incurred by the tortfeasor's liability insurer.

 

110 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Glover v. State


No. 93-KH-2330 Consolidated with No. 94-KH-2101 Consolidated with No. 94-KH-2197


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-2330 (La. 09/05/95); 660 So. 2d 1189; 1995 La. LEXIS 1950



September 5, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Glover v. Cain, 128 F.3d 900, 1997 U.S. App. LEXIS 33076 (5th Cir. La., 1997)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Gallow v. State, 999 So. 2d 1144, 2009 La. LEXIS 1188 (La., 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Gallow v. Rader, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 112253 (W.D. La., Nov. 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL FOURTH CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA Consolidated with ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL SECOND CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA Consolidated with ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL SECOND CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA.
State ex. rel. Glover v. State, 646 So. 2d 363, 1994 La. LEXIS 2753 (La., Nov. 18, 1994)
State v. Young, 646 So. 2d 362, 1994 La. LEXIS 2754 (La., Nov. 18, 1994)
State v. Wright, 641 So. 2d 631, 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2209 (La.App. 2 Cir., July 21, 1994)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted of different crimes and filed their applications for post-conviction relief. All defendants' applications were denied as untimely. Three cases were consolidated for review to determine the constitutionality of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8 which limited the time in which a criminal defendant may file an application for post-conviction relief to three years after his conviction and sentence became final.


OVERVIEW: Article 930.8 provided that, subject to listed exceptions, petitions for post conviction relief would not be considered if filed more than three years after the judgment of conviction and sentence became final. The court held that art. 930.8 1) did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment or federal habeas corpus rights because they did not apply to actions of the states; 2) did not suspend the state writ of habeas corpus in violation of La. Const. art. I, § 21 because habeas corpus relief was not available to a defendant who was entitled to file an application for post conviction relief; 3) did not violate the Louisiana Due Process Clause, La. Const. art. I, § 2, because art. 930.8 provided a reasonable amount of time within which to file an application; 4) did not violate the La. Const. of 1974, art. I, § 22 right to access to courts because access to the courts was available when a timely application was filed; and 5) was not an ex post facto law in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and La. Const. art. I, § 23 because art. 930.8 did not relate to an offense or punishment.


OUTCOME: The judgments denying defendants' applications for post-conviction relief were affirmed. Article 930.8 was constitutional.

 

111 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Marshall


No. 81-KA-3115 c/w 94-KH-0461


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


81-3115 (La. 09/05/95); 660 So. 2d 819; 1995 La. LEXIS 1956



September 5, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, HONORABLE ALVIN V. OSER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Criminal District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which entered judgment on a jury verdict, convicting defendant of armed robbery and attempted first degree murder and sentenced defendant to consecutive terms of 99 years imprisonment for armed robbery and 50 years imprisonment for attempted first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of armed robbery and attempted first degree murder. The trial judge denied a motion for new trial and sentenced defendant to consecutive terms of 99 years imprisonment for armed robbery and 50 years imprisonment for attempted first degree murder. Although defendant's appeal was originally placed on the Court's 1983 docket, action on a motion for evidentiary hearing and motion for new trial disrupted the appeal schedule. The district court held an evidentiary hearing ordered by the court, but failed to rule on the motion for new trial. In 1993, when defendant appealed the denial of a motion to correct an illegal sentence, his appeal's limbo status was revealed. The court vacated in part defendant's sentence for attempted first degree murder and affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for armed robbery, holding that because defendant received the maximum sentence for both convictions, it was clear the trial judge did not structure a scheme of interdependent sentences and that a 99 year sentence for an armed robbery where the victim was seriously wounded was not excessive or grossly disproportionate to the seriousness of the crime.


OUTCOME: The court vacated in part defendant's sentence for attempted first degree murder and affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for armed robbery.

 

112 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Guichard Drilling Co. v. Alpine Energy Servs.


No. 94-C-1275


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1275 (La. 07/03/95); 657 So. 2d 1307; 1995 La. LEXIS 1874



July 3, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated July 18, 1995.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff drilling company appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Louisiana), which reversed a grant of summary judgment in favor of the drilling company in its suit to enforce its lien rights against certain property, including a mineral lease in which intervenor oil companies had an interest, holding that the drilling company did not properly preserve its lien and its lien rights were therefore preempted.


OVERVIEW: A drilling company was hired as a subcontractor to drill a well for an oil company. It filed its affidavit asserting a lien against the oil and gas lease, filed suit against the contractor to enforce its lien, filed a notice of lis pendens, and notified the oil companies. After obtaining judgment, it filed suit to make that judgment executory, and garnished funds held for the oil companies. The court of appeals reversed the judgment in favor of the drilling company, holding that the drilling company failed to institute an action on the lien within one year after recording its lien affidavit. On application for certiorari, the court reversed, holding that the drilling company timely complied with the statutory requirements for preservation of its lien by filing a lien affidavit in the mortgage records of the parish where the drilling services were performed. The court remanded for a determination of the effect of one of the oil company's bankruptcy proceedings and whether the drilling company seized proceeds to which it was not entitled.


OUTCOME: The judgment reversing the grant of summary judgment in favor of the drilling company was reversed because the drilling company properly preserved and enforced its lien. Because the trial court did not address the effect of one oil company's bankruptcy proceedings and there were factual issues regarding the claims that the drilling company garnished proceeds not covered by its lien, the district court's grant of summary judgment was reversed.

 

113 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Prejean v. Dixie Lloyds Ins. Co.


No. 94-CA-2979


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-2979 (La. 5/22/95); 655 So. 2d 303; 1995 La. LEXIS 1375



May 22, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Granted September 15, 1995, Reported at: 1995 La. LEXIS 2372.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant, the Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association (LIGA), appealed the judgment from the trial court (Louisiana), which found that 1993 La. Acts 651 and 958, which amended La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4521(A) by exempting LIGA from the prepayment of court costs, was unconstitutional, and which granted the rule of respondent, an insured, by ordering LIGA to pay an insurer's pre-insolvency court costs.


OVERVIEW: At the conclusion of the litigation in three consolidated cases arising from a car accident, LIGA was ordered to share the court costs with an insurer. The insurer became insolvent, and one insured filed a rule seeking an order compelling LIGA to pay the LIGA'a pre-insolvency court costs. The trial court held that 1993 La. Acts 651 and 958 were unconstitutional and entered judgment in favor of the insured. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment finding that the Acts were unconstitutional, but affirmed the judgment ordering LIGA to pay the court costs. The Acts, which amended La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4521(A) by exempting LIGA from the pre-payment of court costs, served a valid state interest by protecting LIGA's insolvency. Although La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1379(3)(d) exempted LIGA from paying the pre-insolvency obligations of the insurer, § 22:1379(3)(d) was a substantive law and did not expressly state that it was retroactive. Thus, under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 6 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 1:2, LIGA had to pay the insurer's pre-insolvency court costs, because the car accident occurred before the effective date of La Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1379(3)(d).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment declaring unconstitutional the acts which amended a statute by exempting LIGA from the prepayment of court costs. The court affirmed the judgment which granted the rule of an insured by ordering LIGA to pay an insurer's pre-insolvency court costs.

State v. Baxley


94-KA-2982


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-2982 (La. 05/22/95); 656 So. 2d 973; 1995 La. LEXIS 1441



May 22, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concur in Part/Dissent in Part Dated May 23, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE CALVIN JOHNSON, PRESIDING JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision of the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which granted defendant's motion to quash a bill of information charging defendant of soliciting an undercover police officer with the intent to engage in oral copulation in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89, finding that the statute violated defendant's state constitutional right to privacy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by information of soliciting an undercover police officer with the intent to engage in oral copulation for $ 20 pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89. Defendant filed a motion to quash the bill of information, claiming the statute was unconstitutional contending that the statute was applied discriminatorily against homosexuals and mandated greater punishment than the prostitution statute. The statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89, punished engaging in unnatural carnal copulation and/or solicitation of another with the intent to engage in unnatural carnal copulation for compensation. The trial court granted defendant's motion to quash ruling that the statute violated defendant's state constitutional right to privacy. The court reversed, holding that the legislature was entitled to deem one form of conduct more offensive to the public's morals than another, and to punish that conduct more severely. The statute proscribed the same behavior regardless of the actor's sexual orientation, thus was facially neutral. Defendant failed to prove a discriminatory purpose for the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of defendant's motion to quash the a bill of information charging him with soliciting an undercover police officer with the intent to engage in oral copulation.

City of Baton Rouge v. Ross


No. 94-KA-0695


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-0695 (La. 04/28/95); 654 So. 2d 1311; 1995 La. LEXIS 1142



April 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 12, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE CITY COURT OF BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by plaintiff city with drug traffic loitering under Baton Rouge, La., Code of Ordinances § 13:1055. The City Court of Baton Rouge (Louisiana) invalidated the ordinance. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: Baton Rouge, La., Code of Ordinances § 13:1055 made drug traffic loitering an offense. The court affirmed the decision to invalidate the ordinance because under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:143, the ordinance was preempted by a state statute that made the same offense a crime. The ordinance and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 14:28, 40:9766-971.1 defined the same offense as defined by the same elements. Because the city and state constituted a single sovereignty, a conviction or acquittal by the city under the ordinance barred prosecution by the state for the same offense. Therefore, § 14:143 was designed to prevent the city from passing a criminal ordinance, which was the same offense proscribed by a state felony statute. Section 14:143 was a constitutional exercise of the Legislature's police power because it did not impermissibly infringe on city affairs as a home rule government.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision for defendant invalidating the city's ordinance.

 

117 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Larson


No. 94-KA-1237


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1237 (La. 04/10/95); 653 So. 2d 1158; 1995 La. LEXIS 967



April 10, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication April 24, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 16TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARY, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state sought review of a decision of the 16th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Mary (Louisiana), which declared as unconstitutional, the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:90(A)(13) and (D)(3), which prohibited lewd dancing on licensed premises, and dismissed criminal charges against defendant, the owner of a bar that exhibited nude dancing.


OVERVIEW: Undercover police observed nude dancing in a bar and violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:90(A)(13) and (D)(3), which prohibited lewd dancing on premises licensed to serve alcohol. The nude dancers repeatedly exposed various private body parts. Defendant, the owner of the bar, was arrested and charged under § 26:90(A)(13) and (D)(3). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss, contending that the statutes in question failed to set forth a scienter requirement, thus improperly permitted a prosecution without a showing of criminal intent or culpable knowledge. The trial court declared the statutes in question unconstitutional because of the lack of specificity as to intent. The state sought direct review to the Louisiana Supreme Court. The court reversed and remanded, holding that under the 21st Amendment, a state had the absolute power to prohibit totally the sale of liquor within its boundaries and to regulate the sale of liquor. No constitutional violation was invoked simply because the statute would cause a bar owner to prevent others from exercising their First Amendment right to dance nude at his establishment. There was no mens rea requirement for public welfare laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the ruling declaring the sections of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law, which prohibited lewd dancing on licensed premises, unconstitutional and the dismissal of the charges against defendant under those sections.

Marler v. Petty


94-CP-1851


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1851 (La. 4/10/95); 653 So. 2d 1167; 1995 La. LEXIS 977



April 10, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA. PARISH OF WASHINGTON.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a prisoner, applied for a writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, State of Louisiana. Parish of Washington, which affirmed the trial court's judgment that sustained the motion of defendants, prison and state officials, to dismiss the prisoner's suit for improper venue under the Louisiana Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171 et seq.


OVERVIEW: A prisoner was attacked by another inmate and sued the inmate and prison and state officials. The trial court sustained the officials' motion to dismiss the suit without prejudice for improper venue, and the appellate court affirmed. On a writ of certiorari, the court affirmed the judgment that venue was improper, but reversed the dismissal of the suit and remanded the case for transfer to the proper venue. The prisoner's tort suit was governed by the Louisiana Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure, La. Rev. § 15:1171 et seq. Thus, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1177, the prisoner had to file his suit against the inmate as well as against the officials in the Nineteenth Judicial District Court. Because the prisoner did not knowingly file his suit in the wrong district court, the prisoner was entitled to have his case transferred pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 121 and 932 to the Nineteenth Judicial District Court. Because the trial court did not rule on the officials' claim that the prisoner did not exhaust his administrative remedies, the appellate court improperly ruled in favor of the officials on that issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment affirming a trial court's judgment that a prisoner's tort suit against an inmate and against prison and state officials was filed in the wrong suit. The court reversed the judgment affirming the dismissal of the prisoner's suit and remanded the case to transfer the suit to the Nineteenth Judicial District Court as required by the Louisiana Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure.

 

119 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Columbia Gulf Transmission Co. v. Broussard


No. 94-C-1650


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1650 (La. 04/10/95); 653 So. 2d 522; 1995 La. LEXIS 974



April 10, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] ON WRIT OF REVIEW TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State successfully applied for a writ of review to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit (Louisiana), which affirmed the summary judgment of the trial court that favored plaintiff, an oil transmission company. The company sought to recover use taxes it had paid under protest for transporting natural gas from offshore Louisiana to Kentucky through underground interstate pipelines.


OVERVIEW: The primary issue was whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305E(1) or the United States Constitution's Commerce Clause prohibited a Louisiana use tax on compressor fuel. Compressor fuel was natural gas that was diverted from an interstate pipeline to power the compressors that propel the natural gas through the pipeline. The court found that the natural gas compressor fuel was consumed, it came to rest, and it became a part of the state's property. The gas production was a substantial nexus with the State of Louisiana. There was no discrimination against interstate commerce. The tax was applied equally to intrastate and interstate pipelines. Gas in interstate commerce was taxed equally with intrastate gas when both were consumed within the state. The court further found that the tax was fairly apportioned because it was imposed only on gas actually consumed in Louisiana's compressor stations. The gas was measured as it was removed and consumed. The court further found that because private counsel was retained by the state, the state was entitled to a 10 percent surcharge for attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment that favored the oil transmission company that was rendered by the trial court and affirmed below and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Neisler


Nos. 94-KK-1384 and 94-KK-1540


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1384 (La. 3/9/95); 655 So. 2d 252; 1995 La. LEXIS 664



March 9, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended March 16, 1995. Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL. FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEAL JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought a writ of certiorari in the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit (Louisiana) to review a finding of no expectation of privacy in a cordless telephone usage and the reversal of an order suppressing wiretap evidence from their trial on drug charges. They urged that the failure to present an informant violated Louisiana Electronic Surveillance Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15-1301 et seq. and the "search" violated La. Const. art I, § 5.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with various drug offenses and sought to suppress evidence obtained from intercepting their cordless telephone conversations. They alleged that the wiretap order issued under Louisiana Electronic Surveillance Act (the Act), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1301 et seq., was flawed because the State failed to present the informant to the issuing judge. The appellate court reversed the order suppressing the evidence, but found no reasonable expectation of privacy in cordless telephone communications. Defendant sought a writ of certiorari and the court affirmed, in part, holding that given the widespread presence of cordless telephones, there was no expectation of privacy in their use. It reversed, in part, ruling that the State's failure to present the informant, as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1310(B)(1) mandated the suppression of all evidence obtained from the tainted wiretap order according to the exclusionary rule of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1310(H)(1), 15:1307. It held that cordless telephone conversations were not "oral" communications under the Act. The interception of defendants' telephone broadcasts was not a constitutionally protected "search."


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court, suppressing evidence obtained pursuant to the execution of a wiretap order from defendants' trial for drug offenses. The State's failure to comply with the presentation requirements of the electronic surveillance act fatally flawed the wiretap order and mandated that all evidence obtained as a result of that order be suppressed.

Board of Comm'rs v. Connick


No. 94-CA-3161


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-3161 (La. 03/09/95); 654 So. 2d 1073; 1995 La. LEXIS 663



March 9, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 23, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: DISTRICT COURT'S ORDER DECLARING LSA-R.S. 14:90(D) UNCONSTITUTIONAL VACATED; JUDGMENT DENYING PLAINTIFF INJUNCTIVE RELIEF AFFIRMED; EXCEPTION OF NO CAUSE OF ACTION SUSTAINED, AND CASE DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Board of Commissioners of the New Orleans Levee District sought review of a decision of the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which denied its motion for an injunction against defendant district attorney and declared that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:90(D) represented an unconstitutional intrusion into the constitutionally defined power of the district attorney, pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 26(B).


OVERVIEW: The Board initiated this action against the district attorney. The Board sought to enjoin him from investigating riverboat gambling activities which the district attorney claimed were a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:525(B)(1)(a). The district attorney claimed that the riverboat was conducting gambling activities at the dock, which removed the casino operators from the protective scope of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:90(D). The trial judge declined to grant the Board's motion for an injunction and, on sua sponte, declared that § 14:90(D) unconstitutionally interfered with the district attorney's power in the area of riverboat gambling. The court found that the trial court erred in reaching the constitutionality of the statute because it was not necessary for the disposition of the case. The court found that a district attorney's investigation could only be enjoined prior to prosecution when a statute was manifestly unconstitutional or when it was a bad faith investigation amounting to an abridgement of a protected right. Neither of these was applicable in this case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order declaring the statute to be unconstitutional, affirmed its denial of the Board's motion for injunctive relief, and sustained the district attorney's exception of no cause of action.

Twin Parish Port Comm'n v. Berry Bros.


No. 94-CA-2594


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-2594 (La. 2/20/95); 650 So. 2d 748; 1995 La. LEXIS 594



February 20, 1995, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant port commission challenged a judgment of the district court (Louisiana) denying his motion for an injunction and declaratory judgment preventing appellees from constructing a natural gas storage facility on Lake Peigneur. The commission contended that the trial court erred by finding that the commission's Ordinance No. 10 was unconstitutional under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:4.1 - :13.


OVERVIEW: The commission sought an injunction and declaratory judgment preventing the construction of a pipeline Lake Peigneur on the basis that any disruption of the water bottom of the lake was prohibited under Twin Parish Port Commission, Ordinances 10, and 3. The trial court denied the commission's motion allegedly on the basis that Ordinance 10 was unconstitutional and that Ordinance 3 was preempted by Louisiana's Department of Environmental Quality statutes and regulations. The commission appealed, contending that the ordinances had been declared unconstitutional and appellate jurisdiction existed under La. Const. art. V, § 5(D). The court held that Ordinance 10 was declared only in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:4.1 et seq., the Open Meeting Laws and therefore the court lacked jurisdiction. The court also held that because no independent jurisdictional basis existed under art. V, § 5(F) relative to Ordinance 3, the court was without jurisdiction over that portion of the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court held that the record failed to show a declaration that any ordinance was unconstitutional, the court did not have appellate jurisdiction, and the case was transferred to the Third Circuit Court of Appeals with orders to vacate any injunctive relief unless nonconstitutional grounds for any injunction existed.

Wooden v. Louisiana Tax Comm'n


No. 94-CA-2481


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-2481 (La. 2/20/95); 650 So. 2d 1157; 1995 La. LEXIS 596



February 20, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. HONORABLE WILLIAM H. BROWN, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the judgment of the trial court declaring La. Rev. Stat. 9:2948 unconstitutional is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Louisiana Tax Commission appealed a judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which, in a declaratory judgment action brought by plaintiff Tax Assessor of Morehouse Parish, ruled that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2948 was an unconstitutional legislative enactment in contravention of La. Const. of 1974, art. VII, § 21. The court first considered whether the tax assessor lacked standing.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to § 9:2948, a buyer under a bond for deed contract was deemed, for purposes of the homestead exemption, to own immovable property he purchased and was occupying under the bond for deed. The assessor argued that affording the homestead exemption to a non-owner violated the constitution. On appeal, the court held that the assessor had a significant real and actual interest in maximizing the collection of ad valorem taxes on all taxable property in the parish. Because § 9:2948 operated to reduce the ad valorem taxes collected, the assessor had standing to bring the action. Read together, La. Const. art. VII, §§ 20(A) and 21 provided that the only properties exempt from ad valorem taxation were those subject to the homestead exemption provided in La. Const. art. VII, § 20(A) and the properties listed in art. VII, § 21, which did not include immovable property subject to a bond for deed contract. Article VII, § 21 denied the legislature the power to enact, directly or indirectly, any other exceptions from ad valorem taxation. Therefore, the district court correctly declared § 9:2948 unconstitutional as violative of La. Const. art. VII, §§ 20 and 21.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.
