BP Oil Co. v. Plaquemines Parish Gov't


No. 93-CA-1109


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-1109 (La. 01/27/95); 651 So. 2d 1322; 1995 La. LEXIS 196



January 27, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 10, 1995. Reported at: 651 So. 2d 1322 at 1336.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of September 6, 1994, Reported at: 1994 La. LEXIS 1940.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to an application for rehearing, plaintiff taxpayer asked the court to review that part of its decision on original hearing in which the court had held that the legislative suspension of certain exemptions from state sales and use taxes also applied to suspend a proportionate amount of exemptions from local sales taxes, including sales taxes imposed by defendant parish.


OVERVIEW: The legislature suspended a portion of various state sales and use tax exemptions. Taking the position that the suspension applied equally to local governmental subdivisions, the parish demanded that the taxpayer pay use taxes on all refinery gas and coke-on-catalyst used at its refinery. The taxpayer paid the taxes under protest and filed suits seeking refunds. The trial court held that La. Const. art. VI, § 29(D), required application of the legislative suspensions equally to governmental subdivisions. On the taxpayer's application for a rehearing of the court's original decision on appeal from the trial court judgment, the court held that it did not need to decide the implications of art. VI, § 29(D) because the legislation at issue only involved the suspension of a law. Suspension of a law was governed by La. Const. art. III, § 20, which limited suspensions to one year and applied only to state sales and use taxes. Accordingly, the exemptions at issue did not apply to governmental subdivisions. The court also held that the method used by the parish to value coke-on-coal was invalid and directed that it be value on remand pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:306-318.


OUTCOME: The court amended it judgment on original hearing (1) to hold that the valuation method used by the parish was invalid and to direct the trial court on remand to value coke-on-catalyst in accordance with the court's opinion, and (2) to reverse that portion of the trial court judgment that decreed that the legislative suspension of state sales and use taxes applied equally to exemptions from local taxes.

St. Charles Gaming Co. v. Riverboat Gaming Comm'n

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-2697 (La. 01/17/95); 648 So. 2d 1310; 1995 La. LEXIS 185



January 17, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 31, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.



DISPOSITION: For the reasons assigned, the declaration of unconstitutionality is reversed and the judgment ordering a preliminary injunction to issue is vacated. The case is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parish president challenged a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which declared a parish ordinance unconstitutional and ordered a preliminary injunction to issue in favor of appellee gaming company in an action concerning land zoning for riverboat gaming facilities.


OVERVIEW: An ordinance of the parish limited the location for docking riverboat casinos. The gaming company requested that the parish rezone a docking site so that it could proceed with plans to develop the site for a riverboat casino. The parish refused the request. The trial court granted the gaming company a preliminary injunction and declared the ordinance unconstitutional. The parish president appealed the grant of the injunction and sought an emergency stay of the injunction pending the appeal's outcome. The court reversed the trial court's declaration of unconstitutionality and the order for the preliminary injunction. The court found that La. Const. art. XII, § 6(B), and the Louisiana Riverboat Economic Development and Gaming Control Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:501 et seq. (1994) (Riverboat Gaming Act), did not deny home rule powers as to non arbitrary zoning ordinance like the ordinance at issue. The court also found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:552(B) (1994) of the Riverboat Gaming Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:501 et seq. (1994), only prohibited local governing authorities from licensing or regulating riverboats and their gaming operations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the declaration of unconstitutionality and vacated the judgment that ordered the preliminary injunction. The court remanded the action for adjudication on whether the gaming company was entitled to injunctive relief.

Police Ass'n v. City of New Orleans


No. 94-C-1078


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1078 (La. 01/17/95); 649 So. 2d 951; 1995 La. LEXIS 189



January 17, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] WRIT TREATED AS AN APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, IN PART, REVERSED, IN PART, AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city brought a writ application seeking review of the finding by the Court of Appeals, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans, State of Louisiana that New Orleans, La., Municipal Ordinance 15298, as amended by New Orleans, La., Municipal Ordinance 15420 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The New Orleans City council passed an ordinance which required all city employees to be domiciled in the city, but excepted from that requirement all employees who were domiciled outside the city on December 10, 1990, as long as they maintained the same out-of-city domicile, and with the further proviso that certain non-domiciliary employees who did not have permission to live outside of the city, had to establish a domicile within the city in order to accept a promotion. Plaintiffs challenged the constitutionality of the statute. The court declared unconstitutional, only those provisions of New Orleans, La., Municipal Ordinance 15298, as amended by New Orleans, La., Municipal Ordinance 15420, imposing upon the class of non-domiciliary employees hired between August 27, 1973 and December 10, 1990 who did not get specific permission from the Chief Administrative Officer to maintain out-of-city domiciles, the requirement that they establish a domicile within the city in order to accept a promotion. Such provisions were severed from the valid portions of the ordinance leaving the balance of the ordinance and the grandfather clause intact.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, finding that the grandfather clause of the residency requirement ordinance violated the equal protection clause of the Louisiana constitution, and it struck those parts of the ordinance as unconstitutional. But finding those provisions severable and the ordinance otherwise valid, it upheld the validity of the balance of the ordinance, and amended the court of appeals judgment accordingly.

 

128 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


No. 94-KA-1290


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1290 (La. 01/17/95); 648 So. 2d 872; 1995 La. LEXIS 192



January 17, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Rehearing Denied March 23, 1995, Reported at: 1995 La. LEXIS 757.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: For the reasons assigned, the judgment of the trial court declaring La. R.S. 40:981.3 unconstitutional is reversed. The judgment sustaining the motion to quash is reversed and set aside. The case is remanded to the district court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State of Louisiana sought review by writ of certiorari, pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 5, from the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana). Defendants were charged by bill of information with violating La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3. They filed a motion to quash the bill of information, alleging that § 40:981.3 was unconstitutional. The district court upheld the motion and declared § 40:981.3 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were arrested and charged, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3, with possession with the intent to distribute heroin within 1,000 feet of a schoolyard. They filed a motion to quash the bill of information. The district court held that the lack of a "knowledge" requirement did not invalidate the statute, nor did it violate defendants' due process rights. The district court also found that the penal provisions of § 40:981.3 were not excessive. However, the district court upheld the motion to quash on grounds that § 40:981.3 was overbroad, as it encompassed too much area. The court reversed the judgment of the district court. The court opined, inter alia, that § 40:981.3 was not unconstitutionally vague, as it was clearly and readily understandable, gave adequate notice of what conduct was proscribed, and provided adequate standards for determining guilt or innocence of the accused. Any reasonable person could understand that the statute proscribed possessing and trafficking controlled dangerous substances while within 1,000 feet of school property. Nor did the statute violate substantive due process, as it was rationally related to a legitimate state purpose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court, which had declared the statute, under which defendants were charged, unconstitutional. Further, the court reversed and set aside the judgment, sustaining the motion to quash the bill of information, and remanded the case to the district court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

129 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Baker v. MacLay Properties Co.


No. 94-CA-1529


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1529 (La. 01/17/95); 648 So. 2d 888; 1995 La. LEXIS 194



January 17, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 31, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: SUMMARY JUDGEMENT AFFIRMED; REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant, a Louisiana real estate broker, filed suit against respondent, an out-of-state real estate brokerage corporation, to recover commissions allegedly due to him under the parties' cooperating brokerage agreement. The 19th Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) held that the agreement was null and entered summary judgment for the corporation. The broker appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parties entered into the brokerage agreement because former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 37:1437(A) and a former Louisiana Real Estate Commission regulation established a residency requirement for Louisiana real estate brokers' licenses. Out-of-state brokers desiring to do Louisiana business were required to cooperate with Louisiana brokers and give a resident broker at least 50 percent of any fees or commissions. The trial court held that the statute and regulation violated the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the Constitution, and then dismissed the broker's demands as unenforceable. First, the court held that the statute and regulation were indeed unconstitutional and that the parties' contract based upon them was null. In particular, persons could not by their juridical acts derogate from laws enacted for the protection of the public interest. Second, a real estate broker is not entitled to payment, even on a quantum meruit basis, when he has no express or implied contract with the party from whom he seeks a commission. Nevertheless, the trial court erred in dismissing all of the broker's claims against the corporation since he stated a viable claim for unjust enrichment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment finding that the former Louisiana statute and regulation were unconstitutional, as well as the finding that the parties' contract was unenforceable. However, the court remanded the matter for further proceedings to determine whether the broker was entitled to damages for unjust enrichment.

Pace v. State ex rel. Louisiana State Employees Retirement Sys.


No. 94-CA-1027


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1027 (La. 01/17/95); 648 So. 2d 1302; 1995 La. LEXIS 183; 18 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2833



January 17, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 31, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED TO THE TRIAL COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Louisiana State Employee's Retirement System sought review of a decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found in favor of plaintiff tutrix and determined that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:543(19) violated equal protection guarantees insofar as it denied benefits to the illegitimate children of male members who did not obtain judgments of paternity.


OVERVIEW: Although the statute awarded benefits to legitimate children of unmarried members of the public retirement system and to the illegitimate children of female members, it denied benefits to the illegitimate children of male members who failed to obtain judgments of paternity or filiation during the lifetime of the male member. The tutrix filed suit on behalf of two children who were denied benefits under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:543(19). On appeal, the court held that the statute violated the equal protection principals contained at La. Const. art. 1, § 3. The court found that a myriad of social and economic pressures operated to prevent actions from being filed against the fathers of illegitimate children and concluded that they prevented illegitimate children from having a reasonable opportunity to assert their rights. The court found that the state had no interest in providing for the orderly distribution of retirement benefits in the same way that it did for the distribution of property because the same amount of retirement benefits was paid no matter how many survivors a decedent left. Additonally, recent technology made it easier to prove paternity than ever before.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding the statute unconstitutional and remanded for further proceedings.

Lafourche Parish Council v. Autin


No. 94-CA-0985


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-0985 (La. 12/09/94); 648 So. 2d 343; 1994 La. LEXIS 2954



December 9, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFOURCHE, STATE OF LOUISIANA


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the town of Golden Meadow and its mayor, sought review of a decision of the Seventeenth Judicial District Court, Parish of LaFourche (Louisiana), which found in favor of plaintiff LaFourche Parish Council, declared that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:1415(G) was unconstitutional, and enjoined its implementation by the town and its mayor.


OVERVIEW: Section 33:1415(G) permitted towns located within parishes to appoint members to parish boards and commissions. The parish council claimed that this statute represented an unconstitutional change affecting the structure and organization of the powers and function of a parish which was operated under a home rule charter adopted pursuant to La. Const. art. VI, § 5. Upon review, the court found that the statute was not facially unconstitutional because the scope of La. Const. art. VI, § 6, which banned the legislature from enacting any law which changed or affected the structure of a home rule parish, did not include those parishes which were not operated under a home rule charter. However, the court did find that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to the parish in this case. The court held that the statute effected the parish's administrative authority over its own boards and commissions and affected the distribution of powers and functions within the parish. The court determined that the statute was not an exercise of police power and that the provisions of La. Const. art. VI, § 9(B), did not protect the statute from the prohibitions of La. Const. art. VI, § 6.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment of the trial court, finding that the statute was unconstitutional only in its application to home rule charter parish governments, and otherwise affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

134 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanders


No. 93-KA-0001


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-0001 (La. 11/30/94); 648 So. 2d 1272; 1994 La. LEXIS 2882



November 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring Opinion Dated December 1, 1994. Certiorari Granted June 10, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 3772.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF TERREBONNE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions of two counts of first degree murder and the attending death sentence imposed by the 32nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of aggravated murder and was sentenced to death. He appealed his convictions and sentence. The court held that his convictions were appropriate and affirmed them. However, the court held that defendant was denied the adequate assistance of counsel in the penalty phase of his trial, reversed the death sentence and remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing. In the sentencing phase of the trial, counsel failed entirely to object to the presentation of the state's case-in-chief. Failure to object to the hearsay testimony not only showed defendant to have violated the terms of probation and to be a felon in the possession of firearms, but also exposed the jury to the arguably unduly prejudicial effects of what the prosecutor called the shocking array of weapons themselves, which timely objection could have prevented. Counsel's own case, consisted of the testimony of defendant and defendant's ex-wife, neither of whom gave any sign of being prepared to take the stand, did little more than give the state the opportunity to cross-examine them, with devastating results. Finally, defense counsel did not make a closing argument at the penalty phase.


OUTCOME: The court found that defendant suffered prejudice during the penalty phase of his trial due to inadequate representation of counsel. Therefore, because of ineffective assistance of counsel and the admission of improper evidence at the penalty phase, the court set aside defendant's sentence of death and remanded the case to the district court for a new sentencing hearing.

Louisiana Paddlewheels v. Louisiana Riverboat Gaming Comm'n


No. 94-CA-2015


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-2015 (La. 11/30/94); 646 So. 2d 885; 1994 La. LEXIS 2883



November 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Louisiana Riverboat Gaming Commission, sought review of a decision of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which declared as unconstitutional La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 4:537 and 4:537.1, which prohibited the issuance of a license for a riverboat gambling operation in Calcasieu and Ouachita Parishes without the approval of a majority of the electors.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, an applicant for a riverboat gaming license, was denied a license by the Commission. The denial was based on La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 4:537 and 4:537.1, which prohibited the issuance of a license for a riverboat gambling operation in Calcasieu and Ouachita Parishes without the approval of a majority of the electors. The applicant filed a declaratory judgment action seeking a declaration that the statutes in question were unconstitutional. The facts at trial indicated that other parishes were not under the same restrictions imposed on the Calcasieu and Ouachita parishes. The trial court declared the statutes unconstitutional. The court affirmed holding that certain types of local or special laws that operated solely in certain parishes were prohibited by La. Const. art. III, § 12(A)(1). The Louisiana constitution did not prohibit all local or special laws, but because the statutes in question involved the conducting of elections, §§ 4:537 and 4:537.1 were constitutionally invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that sections of the Louisiana Riverboat Economic Development and Gaming Control Act were unconstitutional.

State v. Schirmer


No. 93-KA-2631


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-2631 (La. 11/30/94); 646 So. 2d 890; 1994 La. LEXIS 2885



November 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring Opinion Dated March 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE DISTRICT COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed from the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which granted defendant's motion to quash upon determining that La. Rev. Stat. §§ 18:1462(A)(3), (4) were unconstitutionally overboard. Plaintiff also appealed the trial court's determination that La. Rev. Stat. § 1462(A)(2) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a drive to force a recall election and went to a polling site, set up a table, and began gathering signatures for the recall petition. Defendant was placed under arrest for violating La. Rev. Stat. §§ 18:1462(A)(2), (3), (4). Cases were pending in both federal and state courts. The federal court found the statutes constitutional, whereas the state court found them unconstitutional. The court affirmed the quashing of defendant's information in his criminal prosecution and affirmed the determination that the statutes were unconstitutional. Defendant's actions were political speech, which triggered strict scrutiny analysis. Although some restricted speech was necessary in order to serve the States' compelling interest in preventing voter intimidation and election fraud, §§ 18:1462(A)(3), (4) significantly impinged upon defendant's First Amendment freedoms. When the prohibition on political speech was extended to 600 feet, the difference was of a constitutional dimension. The court also found § 18:1462(A)(2) unconstitutionally vague, as it offered no guidelines regarding when it was proper to instruct a person to leave the vicinity of the polling site.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that the statutes in question were unconstitutionally overbroad or unconstitutionally vague.

Midboe v. Commission on Ethics for Pub. Employees


No. 94-CA-2270


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-2270 (La. 11/30/94); 646 So. 2d 351; 1994 La. LEXIS 2887



November 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA HONORABLE J. MICHAEL McDONALD, PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: REVERSED: ETHICS COMMISSION OPINION REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant Commission on Ethics for Public Employees sought review of a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court (Louisiana). The judgment was for respondent attorney and declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:1121 of the Code of Governmental Ethics unconstitutional as applied to respondent because it conflicted with La. State Bar R. Prof. Conduct, art. XVI, Rule 1.11 and infringed on the Louisiana Supreme Court's exclusive and plenary power.


OVERVIEW: Respondent attorney filed a petition for declaratory judgment and injunction against applicant Commission on Ethics for Public Employees and sought an order declaring the Code of Governmental Ethics, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:1101 et seq., unconstitutional in its application to respondent. The trial court ruled in favor of respondent, and the court reversed the decision. The court held that the district court, not applicant, had jurisdiction to rule on the constitutionality of the statutes and that respondent did not have to first raise his constitutional challenge before applicant. The court found that respondent had a real interest in obtaining a declaratory judgment to clarify his employment options because if he proceeded without such a declaration, he might subject himself and his future employer to administrative sanctions. The court held that respondent's request for injunctive relief was a proper method of demanding "further relief" pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. art. 1871. The court found that the application of the ethics code's prohibitions did not prevent respondent from practicing law and that the legislature was not attempting to regulate the practice of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment that ruled against applicant Commission on Ethics for Public Employees and that declared an ethics law unconstitutional as it applied to respondent attorney because it conflicted with a State Bar professional rule. The court held that the ethics code provisions did not impede or frustrate the court's authority to regulate the practice of law.

Vallo v. Gayle Oil Co.


94-CA-1238


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1238 (La. 11/30/94); 646 So. 2d 859; 1994 La. LEXIS 2888



November 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF VERMILLION, LOUISIANA


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employers appealed the decision from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Vermillion (Louisiana) that found for plaintiff employee and determined that a provision of the Worker's Compensation Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1203(A), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee challenged the constitutionality of a provision of the Worker's Compensation Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1203(A), in his pre-trial memorandum declaring that, if the statute was applicable, it was unconstitutional because it violated the Commerce Clause. Defendant employers did not defend the constitutional attack, the attorney general was not alerted by plaintiff that the constitutionality of § 23:1203(A) was under attack, and the parties did not contest the constitutionality of the statute in open court. The trial court found for plaintiff and a few weeks later declared the statute unconstitutional in a minute entry without written reasons. On appeal, the court vacated the minute entry and remanded. The court noted the attorney general did not file briefs or participate in oral argument. The court found that the claim of unconstitutionality of the statute was not specially pleaded in an appropriate pleading, the attorney general was not served a copy of the pleading, and the record did not contain a transcript of a contradictory hearing. The case was not in a proper posture to review the trial court's ruling of unconstitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the minute entry which adjudged the statute unconstitutional and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Cinel


No. 94-KA-0942


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-0942 (La. 11/30/94); 646 So. 2d 309; 1994 La. LEXIS 2891



November 30, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Criminal District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which declared the pornography involving juveniles statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.1, unconstitutional in its entirety and granted a motion to quash an information against defendant pursuant to the statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a former Roman Catholic priest, was charged with violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.1, the pornography involving juveniles statute. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute, contending that subsection 81.1D improperly excluded lack of knowledge of the performer's age as a defense and improperly infringed on free speech rights protected by the First Amendment. The trial court found that subsection 81.1D was unconstitutional and improperly eliminated the scienter requirement, and ruled that the entire statute was invalid on its face and dismissed the information against defendant pursuant to the statute, by granting defendant's motion to quash. The court reversed and remanded, holding that subsection 81.1D was severable from the remainder of the statute, thus it was improper to invalidated the entire statute. A statute was not to be struck down on its face if it was severable, and only the unconstitutional portion was to be invalidated. A child pornography statute was required to contain an element of scienter as to a defendant, however, a state was authorized to prohibit the simple possession of child pornography.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the grant of defendant's motion to quash the information pursuant to the pornography involving juveniles statute.

Habeney v. Bellow


No. 94-C-1600


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-1600 (La. 10/28/94); 645 So. 2d 624; 1994 La. LEXIS 2538



October 28, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] IN RE: Schoenberger, Stephanie G.; - Plaintiff(s); Applying for Writ of Certiorari and/or Review; Parish of Orleans Civil District Court Div. "D" Number 90-17329; to the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Number 93CA-0554


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certiorari to review a decision of the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit (Louisiana), that reversed and set aside the judgment of the district court below granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff insured and against defendant insurer. The lower court held that the 1990 and 1992 amendments to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1836(a) did not apply retroactively to bar the insured's claim.


OVERVIEW: The court granted the insured's application for review of the appellate court's judgment dismissing her claim based on amendments to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1836(a). The court reversed the appellate court and held that the amendments did not bar the insured's claim. The amendment changed the law and foreclosed on the insured's right to proceed against the insurer under the insolvent insurer's policy. The amendment was adopted after the insured's accident and if applied retroactively, the insured would have lost previously vested substantive rights. The court concluded that the insured settled her claim against the uninsured motorist insurer and reserved her right to pursue a claim against the insurer based upon the law as it existed at that time. As such, the appellate court's judgment applying the amendment retroactively was in error and the court reversed the judgment and reinstated the district court's decision in favor of the insured.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and reinstated the district court's decision in favor of the insured.

State v. Pollard


No. 93-KA-0660


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-0660 (La. 10/20/94); 644 So. 2d 370; 1994 La. LEXIS 2474



October 20, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Criminal District Court Parish of Orleans Hon. Leon J. Cannizzaro, Judge



DISPOSITION: RULING VACATED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) that quashed a multiple offender bill of information. The court stated that it would treat the appeal as an application for supervisory review under La. Sup. Ct. R. 1, § 11.


OVERVIEW: The court granted an application for supervisory review of the district court's judgment quashing a multiple offender bill of information. The court remanded the case for resumption of the multiple bill proceedings. The court held that the penalties provided by the multiple offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, were not unconstitutional on their face and did not provide grounds for quashing a multiple bill. The district court, however, did have authority to reduce any of the mandatory minimum sentences provided by the multiple offender statute for a particular offense and offender status if it would violate defendant's constitutional protection against excessive punishment. The court ordered the district court on remand to make the factual determination of offender status required by the evidence presented at the multiple offender hearing and to determine on the record whether the mandatory minimum sentence for the offender status was unconstitutionally excessive as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the district court for a factual determination of the offender status and to determine whether the mandatory minimum sentence provided for the offender status was unconstitutionally excessive.

In the Interest of A.C.


No. 93-CA-1125


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-1125 (La. 10/17/94); 643 So. 2d 743; 1994 La. LEXIS 2406



October 17, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 31, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE JUVENILE COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON

Original Opinion of January 27, 1994, Reported at: 1994 La. LEXIS 280.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted a petition for a rehearing to reconsider whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:364D was unconstitutional because it prohibited all visitation and contact between a parent and child for a specified period after a court had found by a mere preponderance of the evidence that the parent sexually abused the child. The Juvenile Court (Louisiana) had declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 9:364D and 367 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The mother and father of a minor child were divorced, and joint custody was ordered with the mother as the domiciliary parent and the father awarded visitation. The mother subsequently alleged that the father had sexually abused the child and sought to modify the father's visitation. The trial court denied the mother's request. The trial court further ruled that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:364D, which terminated the alleged abuser's visitation and contact in such situations, was unconstitutional, because it gave greater weight to the testimony of the mental health professional than other witnesses. On rehearing, the court ruled that the statute's failure to require proof of sexual abuse of the child by the parent in a factfinding hearing by clear and convincing evidence rendered the statute unconstitutional as violative of the parent's procedural due process rights. The court ruled that an elevated standard of proof in the factfinding stage was constitutionally required because the total and partially permanent loss of the parent's right to visitation and contact with his or her child was significantly more serious than the private interest involved in the ordinary civil case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

BP Oil Co. v. Plaquemines Parish Gov't


No. 93-CA-1109


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-1109 (La. 09/06/94); 651 So. 2d 1322; 1994 La. LEXIS 1940



September 6, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Granted January 27, 1995, Reported at: 1995 La. LEXIS 196.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF PLAQUEMINES
BP Oil Co. v. Plaquemines Parish Gov't, 642 So. 2d 1230, 1994 La. LEXIS 3105 (La., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed the decision of the Twenty-Fifth Judicial District Court, Parish of Plaquemines (Louisiana), which declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305D(1)(h) unconstitutional and dismissed the taxpayer's action against defendant parish for refunds of overpayments of local use taxes on refinery gas and coke-on-catalyst used in the taxpayer's petroleum refinery.


OVERVIEW: The parish assessed local use taxes against the taxpayer on the taxpayer's use of refinery gas and coke-on-catalyst created during the taxpayer's refining process. The taxpayer paid the assessments under protest and filed four actions for refunds pursuant to § 47:305D(1)(h). The trial court declared § 47:305D(1)(h) unconstitutional and dismissed the refund claims. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that § 47:305D(1)(h) was not in conflict with La. Const. art. VI, § 29, which granted the parish the authority to levy sales and use taxes, without legislative authorization, as long as the total sales and use taxes did not exceed three percent, because the parish's use tax could not go beyond the taxing limits set by the legislature, including the exemption for petroleum refinery products set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305D(1)(h). The court also held that the retail sale exemption of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:301(10)(c) did not apply because the refinery gas and coke-on-catalyst, once separated from the raw material, were not further processed into an end product for sale at retail. The court also remanded for consideration of various interest and penalty provisions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which had declared unconstitutional the petroleum refinery products' exemption to the parish's local use tax and had dismissed the taxpayer's claims for refunds for taxes paid under protest.

 

144 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Descant v. Administrators of the Tulane Educ. Fund


No. 93-C-3098


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-3098 (La. 7/5/94); 639 So. 2d 246; 1994 La. LEXIS 1865



July 5, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sued defendants physician, hospital, and its liability insurer, to recover damages for injuries sustained by their daughter during her birth. The court of appeal affirmed the trial court's finding that plaintiffs had no cause of action, and plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendants physician, hospital, and its liability insurer, to recover damages for injuries sustained by their daughter during her birth. Defendant hospital was a self-insured qualified health care provider under the Medical Malpractice Act, with liability is limited to $ 100,000.00 per claim. The court of appeal affirmed the trial court's finding that plaintiffs had no cause of action against defendant liability insurer, and plaintiffs appealed. The court affirmed, holding that because the Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. § 40:1299.41 et seq. eliminated the cause of action against defendant hospital for amounts in excess of $ 100,000.00, there was no remaining cause of action against defendant insurer. It further held that, even assuming that there were a cause of action against the hospital for claims above the statutory limit, and therefore against its insurer, defendant insurer could assert the limitation of liability of the Medical Malpractice Act as a defense to defeat plaintiff's right of action against it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that because the Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. § 40:1299.41 et seq. eliminated the cause of action against defendant hospital for amounts in excess of $ 100,000.00, there was no remaining cause of action against defendant insurer. It further held that, even assuming a cause of action, defendant insurer could assert the limitation of liability of the Act as a defense to defeat plaintiff's right of action.

 

145 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


City of New Orleans v. Board of Comm'rs


No. 93-C-0690


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-C-0690 (La. 7/5/94); 640 So. 2d 237; 1994 La. LEXIS 1866



July 5, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED TO THE TRIAL COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city brought an action against defendant state agency for declaratory judgment and an injunction to restrain the agency's violation of the city's ordinances. The trial court granted an exception for failure to state a cause of action in the agency's favor. The Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) affirmed the judgment. The court granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The agency began to build a marina and related developments for commercial profit on state owned land inside the city without complying with the municipal zoning and building ordinances. The city alleged that its regulations required a developer of such a project to obtain special approval as a conditional use from the city. The agency began construction of the marina without obtaining approval. The city contended that its power of the home rule government included the power to initiate, adopt, and enforce zoning and building ordinances within its boundaries. It claimed that it was constitutionally immune from the power of the legislature to withdraw, preempt, or deny the city's power to enact and enforce those ordinances. The court concluded that the agency's exception should have been overruled. The allegations demonstrated that the city had a valid cause of action. The enactment and enforcement of the ordinances to regulate the agency's use and development of land within the city were consistent with the state's constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the lower courts, which sustained and affirmed the agency's exception of no cause of action, were reversed. The exception was overruled. The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings according to law and consistent with the court's opinion.

 

146 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. All Pro Paint & Body Shop


No. 93-KA-1316


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-1316 (La. 7/5/94); 639 So. 2d 707; 1994 La. LEXIS 1869



July 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal From the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, State of Louisiana



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from the judgment of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit (Louisiana), which reversed the trial court's judgment and granted the motion to quash the indictment entered by defendants, owner and corporation, thereby reversing their convictions for illegal transportation and disposal of hazardous waste in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:2183(G)(2) and declaring the statute unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted for illegally transporting and disposing hazardous waste. The court reversed the vacation of defendants' convictions, holding that the statute was not a delegation to the executive branch of legislative authority to define a felony -- a power that could not be delegated. The appellate court erred in determining that the three-prong test was inapplicable. Upon applying the proper test, it was clear that the statute was constitutional. The Hazardous Waste Control Law (HWCL), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 30:2171-2207, contained a clear expression of legislative policy as it established a reasonable and definite policy warranting the exercise of the State's police power to protect the public health, safety, and welfare by regulating hazardous waste. The HWCL provided sufficient standards to guide the execution of the statute's declared policy. Finally, the HWCL was accompanied by adequate procedural safeguards to protect against abuse of discretion by the Department of Environmental Quality (DEQ), as the DEQ was required to promulgate regulations after public hearing in accordance with the Administrative Procedure Act and provided for legislative review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment, which found the statute unconstitutional, and reinstated the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendants for illegally transporting and disposing of hazardous waste.

 

147 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Lakeside Imports v. State


No. 94-C-0191


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-0191 (La. 7/5/94); 639 So. 2d 253; 1994 La. LEXIS 1870



July 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari and/or Review to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car dealer applied for a writ of certiorari to review the judgment from the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the dealer's suit against the State for a judgment declaring that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:193, which prohibited Sunday sales of vehicles, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:193 prohibited a car dealer from selling new or used cars on Sundays, and the dealer sued the State to have § 51:193 declared unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the dealer's suit, and the appellate court affirmed. On a writ of certiorari, the court affirmed the judgment and held that § 51:193 affected all people throughout the state, thus it was not a special law under La. Const. art. III, § 13. Although the dealer had a property right to conduct his business, that right was subject under La. Const. art. I, § 4 to the reasonable exercise of the State's police power. The State proved that it had three legitimate interests in prohibiting the Sunday sales: to protect small rural dealerships from unfair competition by large dealerships, to protect consumers from the higher prices brought by a higher overhead from Sunday sales, and to protect the welfare of commissioned salespersons. Defendant did not prove by clear and convincing evidence that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:193 did not bear a rational relationship to these objectives. Thus, defendant's due process rights were not violated and § 51:193 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment affirming the dismissal of defendant's suit for a judgment declaring unconstitutional a law that prohibited the Sunday sales of vehicles.

State v. Jones


No. 94-KK-0459


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


94-0459 (La. 7/5/94); 639 So. 2d 1144; 1994 La. LEXIS 1863



July 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 19, 1994. As Corrected.
Writ denied by State v. Jones, 642 So. 2d 1272, 1994 La. LEXIS 1973 (La., Aug. 26, 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS STATE OF LOUISIANA
State v. Jones, 634 So. 2d 845, 1994 La. LEXIS 700 (La., Mar. 18, 1994)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applied for a writ from the decision of the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which denied defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.2(B), the clemency instruction added to the state's capital sentencing provisions, under La. Const. art. 1, § 2, the state's due process clause, and La. Const. art. 1, § 20, the state's right to humane treatment clause.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for the first-degree murder of a British tourist during the perpetration or attempted perpetration of an armed robbery. OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's application for a writ from the decision of the intermediate appellate court, which had denied defendant's application for a writ to have the state's death penalty phase clemency instruction declared unconstitutional, and reversed the decision of the district court, which denied defendant's motion in limine on the same issue.

 

149 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


W. Jefferson Levee Dist. v. Coast Quality Constr. Corp.


No. 93-C-1718


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-C-1718 (La. 5/23/94); 640 So. 2d 1258; 1994 La. LEXIS 1316



May 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated August 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIFTH CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under La. Stat. Ann. § 38.301 et seq., plaintiff landowners sought compensation for the expropriation of their property by defendant levee district, which sought to construct a hurricane levee. The Fifth Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana) affirmed the amount of damages awarded by the trial court. The district appealed, arguing that the land had only a nominal wetlands value and that the award of severance and delay damages was improper.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the landowners' inability to develop their land was caused not by the district, but by the federal government, which was developing a national park in the area. Noting that the landowners contended that the highest and best use of the land was as residential subdivisions, the court found that the record indicated that the landowners could not have obtained in the reasonably foreseeable future the permits necessary to develop the land in that manner. Moreover, it held, they could not show that their inability to obtain the permits was caused by the district. Thus, it concluded, the property was to be valued according to its fair market value as nonpermitted wetlands. It held that the landowners were not entitled to severance damages, stating that the expropriation did not result in a diminution of value to that land which was not expropriated. It held that they were not entitled to delay damages, stating that during the delay between the district's obtaining a permit for the construction of the levee and its filing the expropriation suits the landowners were already prohibited from developing the land by the federal government.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decision, remanding the case to the trial court for computation of the total amount due to the landowners.

 

150 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Craig


Nos. 93-KK-2515, 93-KK-2654


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-2515 (La. 5/23/94); 637 So. 2d 437; 1994 La. LEXIS 1321



May 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE
State v. Harris, 631 So. 2d 432, 1994 La. LEXIS 65 (La., Jan. 7, 1994)
State v. Craig, 631 So. 2d 431, 1994 La. LEXIS 62 (La., Jan. 7, 1994)
State v. Craig, 631 So. 2d 431, 1994 La. LEXIS 66 (La., Jan. 7, 1994)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant Office of the Public Defender (OPD) sought writs to review an order of the First Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana), which reversed a trial court ruling that had required respondent city-parish to cover the expenses of an investigator to assist counsel for defendants in two capital murder cases. The city-parish sought writs to review an order requiring it to fund defendants' expenses for a psychologist and mitigation expert.


OVERVIEW: After holding a contradictory hearing in two cases involving prosecutions for capital murder, the trial court found that defendants' counsel were each entitled to the assistance of an investigator, psychologist, and mitigation expert, and held that the city-parish was responsible for providing the funds to pay the cost of that assistance. The court of appeal affirmed the ruling as to the psychologists and mitigation experts, but reversed as to the investigators. The court held that, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.11, the city-parish, through its "criminal court fund," was responsible for funding expenses associated with the defense of indigent criminals, and there was no basis for distinguishing between an investigator and an expert, where each was required for an effective defense. The court further held that the city-parish could not avoid this responsibility by failing to establish a "criminal court fund." In the absence of such a fund the monies had to come from the city-parish's general fund, pursuant to the city-parish's general responsibility, provided for in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:304, to fund the expenses of criminal proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order requiring the city-parish to pay for a psychologist and mitigation expert, reversed the order relieving the city-parish of responsibility for paying the expenses of an investigator, reinstated the trial court order requiring the city-parish to provide funding for those expenses, ruled that the funds were to come first from the city-parish Criminal Court Fund, and then from the city-parish general fund, and remanded.

State v. Davis

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


92-1623 (La. 5/23/94); 637 So. 2d 1012; 1994 La. LEXIS 1327

OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from fatal shootings in two robberies. In the first, there was no eyewitness, but in the second, defendant appeared on a security tape. Defendant's distinctive car was at both scenes, and his pistol was used for both shootings. Defendant was arrested when his car was stopped and his pistol was taken from a passenger. Defendant confessed to the second shooting, and admitted continuous possession of the car and pistol. Defendant's guilty plea after his arrest to an armed robbery that occurred before the incidents charged, and evidence of another unadjudicated robbery/shooting 45 minutes after the first murder, were admitted in the sentencing phase. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the circumstantial evidence of the first murder met the Jackson standard. The court ruled that suppression of the confession and pistol were properly denied, and the unadjudicated robbery under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 904.2. The court reasoned that even if the first murder was erroneously found to be "especially heinous," it could affirm because the guilty plea was properly found to be an aggravating circumstance under art 905.4.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court judgment.

Branch v. Willis-Knighton Medical Ctr.


No. 92-CC-3086


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


92-3086 (La. 4/28/94); 636 So. 2d 211; 1994 La. LEXIS 1020



April 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari to the Second Circuit Court of Appeal, Parish of Caddo



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient filed a strict tort products liability action against appellee hospital for damage sustained by the patient, who contracted hepatitis from contaminated blood sold to him by the hospital. The Louisiana Court of Appeals reversed the trial court and held that the action was barred by the three year limitation period of the special statute of limitations applicable to medical malpractice actions, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial and appellate courts were correct in concluding that the patient acquired a valid cause of action in strict tort products liability against the hospital arising from the sale of a product in a defective condition unreasonably dangerous to the user or consumer. However, the court held that the court of appeals erred in applying the statute of limitations for medical malpractice action to the patients' claim. Section 9:5628 did not apply to strict tort products liability actions arising out of the sale of blood in a defective condition unreasonably dangerous to the user or consumer and did not contain any provision that expressly or implicitly referred to strict liability or products liability. Because the patient's strict tort product liability action was not subject to the special rule of prescription applicable to medical malpractice actions, § 9:5628, it was therefore subject to the general one year prescription applicable to delictual actions. La. Civ. Code arts. 3536-37 (1870) and was timely filed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals' judgment and reinstated the trial court's judgment.

Louisiana Ins. Guar. Ass'n v. Gegenheimer


No. 93-CA-3021


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-3021 (La. 4/21/94); 636 So. 2d 209; 1994 La. LEXIS 1093



April 21, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Clerk of Court for the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) demanded prepayment of court costs in an action from appellant Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association (LIGA). The trial court denied the Association's writ of mandamus to compel compliance with the exemption contained in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4521(A) (1993), holding that it was unconstitutional. LIGA sought review.


OVERVIEW: When the clerk of court demanded payment of court costs, LIGA sought a writ of mandamus compelling the clerk to defer payment of costs under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4521(A) (1993). On review from an adverse decision, the court found that as a state created association, LIGA served a valid state purpose in paying claims to policyholders of insolvent insurers and that it was entitled to deferment of court costs to alleviate any financial burden litigation costs might have on it. The court reasoned that the meaning of "temporarily deferred" meant that after the litigation was concluded, costs in a fixed amount could be awarded against LIGA or any other state agency under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5112(A) and (B). The court held the statute constitutional and remanded the case with directions to issue the writ.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter with directions to the trial court to issue the writ of mandamus directed to the clerk of court.

State v. Stowe

Doherty v. Calcasieu Parish Sch. Bd.


No. 93 CA 3017


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-3017 (La. 4/11/94); 634 So. 2d 1172; 1994 La. LEXIS 990



April 11, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 25, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF CALCASIEU, STATE OF LOUISIANA HONORABLE WILLIAM L. McLEOD, JR., PRESIDING JUDGE



DISPOSITION: DISTRICT COURT JUDGMENT HOLDING R.S. 17:81.5 UNCONSTITUTIONAL REVERSED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful termination case against defendant school board, plaintiff employees appealed an order from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), finding that 1987 La. Sess. Law. Serv. 631 (Act) was unconstitutional and the school board was not required to implement procedures for the dismissal of non-tenured employees.


OVERVIEW: The employees initiated suit after their employment was terminated. The employees alleged that the school board failed to comply with the Act by implementing procedures for the dismissal of non-tenured employees. The school board alleged that the Act was unconstitutional. The district court found that the Act violated the title provision of La. Const. art. III, § 15 (1974). On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. The court held that the title of an act was to be liberally construed to effectuate the legislative purpose of the statute. The title need only express the general terms of its object. It was only when the variance in the act was palpable and totally irreconcilable with the object expressed in the title that the indicative title requirement was deemed violated. The object of the Act was to have school boards put in place and implement dismissal procedures for non-tenured employees. The body of the Act contained nothing that was unrelated to accomplishment of the stated purpose of having the school boards implement a dismissal system for non-tenured employees. In addition, the Act did not violate the one subject rule.


OUTCOME: The court reversed.

Chance v. American Honda Motor Co.


No. 93-CC-2582


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-2582 (La. 4/11/94); 635 So. 2d 177; 1994 La. LEXIS 991



April 11, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 25, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF CATAHOULA, STATE OF LOUISIANA


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to recover for personal injuries, plaintiffs, parents and minor child, challenged an order from the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Catahoula, State of Louisiana, granting defendant manufacturer's application for prescription.


OVERVIEW: The minor child was injured while riding a three-wheeled all terrain vehicle. The parents and the minor child brought suit some five years after the injury seeking to recover for personal injuries sustained by the minor child. The manufacturer filed an exception of prescription. The trial court denied the motion. The appeals court granted the prescription. On appeal to the supreme court, the court affirmed. The court held that the 1992 amendment to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3492 did not intend to revive prescribed causes of action. The amendment provided that the one year statute of limitation period did not apply to claims by minors or interdicts in actions involving permanent disability brought pursuant to products liability law or state law governing product liability. The court held that the language used did not contain any reference to retroactive application, much less revival of prescribed claims. The one year limitation period applied to the minor child, as her injury was prior to the amendment of article 3492.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Louisiana Health Serv. & Indem. Co. v. Tarver

The trial court found in favor of the State. The insurance company appealed, asserting that the statute constituted an unlawful taking. The court disagreed and found that after a five-year period, the State became the constructive "holder" of the monies and that the statute did not amount to an unconstitutional taking.

DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff principal sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Plaquemines (Louisiana), which reversed a decision of the trial court that issued a writ of mandamus directing defendant school board to negotiate and offer to the principal a new promotional contract for his position upon the expiration of his existing promotional contract.

The court held that the retroactive application of Act 779 to the principal's contract did not unconstitutionally impair the board's contractual rights. The court ruled that board as an agency of the state was aware of the legislature's broad power to regulate public education.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and reinstated the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Baxley


No. 93-KA-2159


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-KA-2159 (La. 2/28/94); 633 So. 2d 142; 1994 La. LEXIS 547



February 28, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS, NO. 356-945, SECTION E. THE HONORABLE CALVIN JOHNSON, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Prosecution sought review of an order from the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans Section E (Louisiana), which held that the crime against nature statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89, was an unconstitutional invasion of a citizen's right to privacy under La. Const. art. I, § 5.


OVERVIEW: After a hearing, the trial court decided the defendant had standing to challenge the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89(A)(1) and that the statute violated the state constitutional right to privacy. A direct appeal was taken to the court pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 5 (D)(1). The court found that the trial court erred in finding that the defendant had standing to contest the constitutionality of the statute. The trial court's judgment that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89(A)(1) violated a citizen's right to privacy under La. Const. art. I, § 5, was premature. Sections 14:89(A)(1) and 14:89(A)(2) described two different ways in which a person could commit a crime against nature. These two subparts describing the prohibited actions did not depend on each other for an understanding of their meaning. Defendant was not charged with conduct that violated § 14:89(A)(1), nor was he subject to any responsive verdict that would put him in jeopardy of a conviction under § 14:89(A)(1). Since the application of § 14:89(A)(1) could not adversely affect defendant, he did not have standing to contest its constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and found that defendant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute.

 

160 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Kelty v. Brumfield


No. 93-C-1142


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-1142 (La. 2/25/94); 633 So. 2d 1210; 1994 La. LEXIS 508



February 25, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring (In Part) and Dissenting (In Part) Opinion of March 1, 1994. Dissenting Opinion Revised March 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: IN RE: Beaucoudray, Lynn; Kelty, James Edward Jr.; - Plaintiff(s); Applying for Writ of Certiorari and/or Review; to the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Number 92CA-0904; Parish of Orleans Civil District Court Div. "E" Number 83-10059.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Certiorari was granted to review an order of the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit (Louisiana), which ruled in favor of defendant, the Patient's Compensation Fund, in plaintiff parents' action for a certification that their child was a patient in need of future medical care and related benefits under § 43, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.43, of the Medical Malpractice Act (MMA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The parents of a child injured by medical malpractice recovered the maximum amount allowed under the MMA and tried three times to have the child certified as a "patient in need of future medical care" from the Patients' Compensation Fund, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.43. The parents' first motion for certification was rejected by the district court. The second motion was granted by the district court but reversed by the appellate court. The third motion was denied by the district court, and the appellate court affirmed. The court granted certiorari, and held that the judgments of the previous courts were invalid because the statute that created the special remedial claim vested exclusive original subject matter jurisdiction of the initial disposition of those claims in the state agencies having authority to pay, reject, settle, and monitor the claims and administer the agency's funds. Because the stipulation of the parties and the original judgment of the district court amounted to a declaration that the child was a patient in need, she was entitled to compensation under § 43.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the appellate court.

Ly v. State

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


92-CA-2312 (La. 2/25/94); 633 So. 2d 1223; 1994 La. LEXIS 548

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.

State ex rel. A.C.


No. 93-CA-1125


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-CA-1125 (La. 1/27/94); 643 So. 2d 719; 1994 La. LEXIS 2899



January 27, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for the Parish of Jefferson.

Previously Reported at: 631 So. 2d 407 and Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee father was suspected of sexually abusing his daughter. The Juvenile Court for Jefferson Parish (Louisiana) gave appellant mother custody over the child and allowed the father to have supervised visits with the child. The mother filed a motion for modification of the judgment to prohibit any visitation. The juvenile court denied the motion but found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 9:364(D), 9.367 were unconstitutional. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile court found that § 9:364(D) was unconstitutional because it deprived the offending parent of parental rights without due process of law and hindered the offending parent's access to the courts. The court also noted that the statute was a legislative encroachment upon the responsibilities of the judicial branch. In addition, the juvenile court held that the portion of § 9:367 that taxed the "perpetrator" of the violence with all costs incurred was both unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. Finally, the juvenile court found that the portion of § 9.634(D) that gave "greater weight" to the testimony of the child's treating therapist on issues relating to visitation threatened the separation of powers scheme as established in La. Const. art. II and was unconstitutional. The court held that § 9:364(D) did not violate the constitutional proscription against deprivations of fundamental liberty interests without due process of law and that § 9:367 was not vague and overbroad. However, the court found that the finding that the portion of § 9.634(D) that gave "greater weight" to the testimony of the child's treating therapist on certain issues was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the order that denied the mother's motion for modification and determined that two laws related to the adjudication of parental rights were unconstitutional. The court, however, affirmed the finding that one portion of the state law that required the juvenile court to give the testimony of the child's treating therapist greater weight was unconstitutional.

Radiofone v. City of New Orleans


No. 93-WA-0962


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-WA-0962 (La. 1/14/94); 630 So. 2d 694; 1994 La. LEXIS 179



January 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 28, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suspensive Appeal Granted April 30, 1993.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeal (Louisiana), which reversed a decision of the trial court that granted the city's motion for summary judgment in plaintiff telecommunications services company's action to declare a city tax unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the city's tax violated La. Const. art. VI, § 28.


OVERVIEW: The city imposed a tax on the privilege of engaging in a telecommunications business greater than any such state tax without approval of the prescribed legislative supermajority. The company sought to have the tax declared unconstitutional. The trial court rejected the company's challenge and the company sought review. The appellate court reversed, holding that the city's tax violated art. VI, § 28 because it was an occupational license tax imposed by a local government in excess of any state occupational license tax without authorization by law enacted by the required legislative supermajority. The city sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the tax was unconstitutional because the city's home rule power to authorize an occupational license tax in excess of that approved by two-thirds of the elected members of each house of the legislature was in conflict with the restriction and the accommodation of interests provided for by art. VI, § 28 and had to yield to that provision. The court found that the power of the state to tax was unlimited except as restricted by constitutional provisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the appellate court.

Rick v. Department of Transp. & Dev.


No. 93-C-1776 c/w No. 93-C-1784


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-C-1776 (La. 1/14/94); 630 So. 2d 1271; 1994 La. LEXIS 180



January 14, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Review to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, State of Louisiana.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; TRIAL COURT JUDGEMENT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development (DOTD) sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, State of Louisiana, which affirmed a trial court's judgment finding the DOTD 50 percent at fault in an accident which killed the decedent. Plaintiffs, decedent's widower and children, sought review of the appellate court's reduction of the general damages award and the prejudgment interest rate.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the DOTD argued that it had no duty to upgrade the railroad crossing at which the decedent was killed, that its failure to upgrade the crossing was not a cause in fact of the death, that it was shielded by the discretionary function exception in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1, and that the trial court erroneously admitted evidence. The supreme court held that: (1) the DOTD was liable for negligence where it assumed a duty to upgrade the crossing; (2) it was impossible to say that the jury was clearly wrong in finding that the crossing's condition was a cause in fact of the death; (3) whether a particular crossing was selected for upgrade was a discretionary matter protected by § 9:2798.1, but failure to formulate an accurate hazard index for the crossing or to ask the railroad about the upgrade's status was operational negligence for which the DOTD was liable; (4) evidence of accident reports, traffic counts, and other raw data collected by the DOTD was discoverable and admissible; (5) the appellate court erred in failing to give deference to the trial court's assessment of general damages; and (6) the appellate court's reduction of the interest rate was error.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment on the liability issue, reversed the appellate court's judgment insofar as it reduced the award of general damages and the interest rate, and reinstated the judgment of the trial court.

Hillman v. Akins


No. 93-C-0631


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-C-0631 (La. 1/14/94); 631 So. 2d 1; 1994 La. LEXIS 184



January 14, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On plaintiff patients' application in consolidated malpractice cases, the court granted writs to review a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Calcasieu, Louisiana, which affirmed trial court orders sustaining peremptory exceptions of prescription filed by defendants, surgeons and hospitals, and which rejected the patients' claim that the doctrine of contra non valentem interrupted the running of the prescriptive period.


OVERVIEW: The patients challenged the court of appeal's affirmance of the trial court's judgment that sustained defendants' peremptory exceptions of prescription and dismissed the patients' medical malpractice action. Both the court of appeal and the trial court rejected the patients' assertion that because the doctors and hospitals knew but failed to disclose that a medical device that was used in the patients' surgeries was not federally approved, the doctrine of contra non valentem interrupted the running of the prescriptive period. The court affirmed, noting that each of the patients exceeded the prescriptive period provided by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. The patients argued that they were unable to bring their actions in time because defendants failed to disclose material information regarding their surgeries. The court held that there was no evidence that defendants knew that the use of the device had not been approved by the relevant federal agency. The court noted that the doctors acquired the information regarding the lack of approval after the surgery and contacted the manufacture of the inserted plate to ascertain whether they should continue to utilize the device.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeal.

Segura v. Frank


No. 93-C-1271 c/w No. 93-C-1401


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-C-1271 (La. 1/14/94); 630 So. 2d 714; 1994 La. LEXIS 185



January 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 28, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit. On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Writ of certiorari was granted with respect to plaintiff injured parties' and defendant insurers' cross-appeals of judgments from the Courts of Appeal for the Third and Fifth Circuit (Louisiana), which reached opposite determinations as to whether amendments to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386, the "nonduplication of recovery" statute, applied to claims arising from accidents occurring prior to the amendments' effective dates.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court initially noted that as the retroactive application of the amendment in 1992 La. Acts 237 to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386 would disturb insurers' vested rights, the amendment was substantive, rather than procedural or interpretation. The court thus determined that although retroactive application of La. Rev. Stat. § 22:1386 as amended by would impair insurers' contractual obligations under the uninsured motorist policies by making them primary liable for injured parties' claims against the insolvent carrier, the adjustment of insurers' rights and responsibilities was based upon reasonable conditions and was of a character appropriate to the public purpose justifying the legislative adoption. The court therefore held that under the appropriate Contracts Clause standard, retroactive application of 1992 La. Acts 237 was permissible, as it would violate neither the federal nor the state constitutional prohibitions against impairment of contractual relations. Accordingly, the court concluded that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386, as amended, applied to each injured party's pending claim.


OUTCOME: Although it disagreed with the reasoning of the lower court in its decision to apply the nonduplication of recovery statute to the claims at issue, the reviewing court affirmed that judgment. In addition, the court reversed the judgment of the lower court that had refused to apply the statute and remanded the matter for further proceedings.
