In re Pitre


No. 93-CA-2322


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


93-CA-2322 (La. 1/14/94); 630 So. 2d 700; 1994 La. LEXIS 191



January 14, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Eighteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberville, State of Louisiana.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant company sought review of a judgment from the Eighteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberville (Louisiana), which held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:130.18 unconstitutionally granted the company a tax exemption in derogation of those exemptions enumerated in La. Const. art. 7, § 21 (1974).


OVERVIEW: A waterworks district approved a bond issue for a water system. The company paid additional millage servicing the bonds under protest claiming an exemption under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:130.18. The trial court declared § 33:130.18 an unconstitutional violation of La. Const. art. 7, § 21 (1974) because the article listed the only property exempt from ad valorem taxation. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:130.18 was enacted under the 1921 Louisiana Constitution. The court also found that La. Const. art. 14, § 18(B) (1974) provided that laws that were in conflict with the 1974 Louisiana Constitution ceased upon its effective date. Thus, the court concluded that any validity that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:130.18 might have had prior the effective date of the 1974 Louisiana Constitution ceased when that constitution came into force because both the constitutions allowed only for listed exemptions. Because § 33:130.18 provided an exemption from ad valorem taxation in derogation of La. Const. art. 7, § 21 (1974), the exemption for new or increased taxes in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:130.18 ceased on the effective date of 1974 Louisiana Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which held that a statute unconstitutionally granted a tax exemption.

State v. McHugh


No. 92-KK-1852


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


92-KK-1852 (La. 1/6/94); 630 So. 2d 1259; 1994 La. LEXIS 89



January 6, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari to the First Circuit Court of Appeal



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment of the First Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana), which reversed a ruling of the trial court that denied defendants' motion to suppress. The appellate court ordered the evidence and defendants' statements suppressed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, who were deer hunters, were leaving a wildlife habitat during hunting season. Two wildlife law enforcement officers stopped defendants and demanded to see their hunting licenses. After defendants complied with this request, an officer asked them if they had any ducks. When they replied in the negative, the officer inquired if they had any other game in their possession. Defendants responded that one of them had killed a deer and pointed to carcass. The officer obtained permission to come aboard to examine the deer. Upon observing that there were no visible tags on the deer meat, the officer issued summonses charging defendants with violating La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:125. Defendants brought a motion to suppress. The trial court denied the motion, the appellate court revered the denial, and the State sought review. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. The court held that the motion to suppress should be denied because a game agent's stop of a hunter in or departing from a wildlife habitat in open season and detention of him for the limited purposes of a license check and requests for game information and inspection did not violate the state or federal constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Richardson v. Louisiana Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corrections


93-KD-0476


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


627 So. 2d 635; 1993 La. LEXIS 3388



November 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF REVIEW TO THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parole board sought certiorari review of the decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) that held illegal the mandatory life sentence imposed upon defendant pursuant to her conviction of possession and distribution of heroin in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(B).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession and distribution of heroin in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(B), and a mandatory life sentence was imposed according to the statute. Defendant claimed the sentence could not be imposed because "without benefit of parole" was not found in the statute and the sentence was unconstitutionally excessive. Defendant filed a petition for mandamus relief, which was granted by a commissioner and adopted by the trial court. The parole board sought certiorari review. The court held that the silence of § 40:966(B) regarding parole did not indicate that a sentence without eligibility of parole could not be imposed. In reversing the judgment, the court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4(B) applied, and dictated that a life sentence imposed pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966 could not be considered for parole eligibility until the sentence was commuted to a term of years. The court held that a mandatory life term was not cruel and unusual, excessive or disproportionate even for first drug offenders.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

American Waste & Pollution Control Co. v. St. Martin Parish Police Jury


93-CA-1348


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


627 So. 2d 158; 1993 La. LEXIS 3392



November 29, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARTIN, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: VACATED, RENDERED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant parish appealed a judgment from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Martin (Louisiana), which ruled in favor of plaintiff waste management company and held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:1236.16 was unconstitutional and continued its permanent injunction enjoining the parish from enacting any zoning or land use ordinances until it had appropriate constitutional authority to do so.


OVERVIEW: The parish petitioned for a declaratory judgment on the constitutionality of § 33:1236.16, which authorized it to provide for zoning and siting for the disposal of solid waste within the parish and for the lifting of the permanent injunction. The court found that the petition for declaratory relief lacked a justiciable controversy. Although the parish's petition claimed to seek a declaration of a right, in actuality it sought an advisory opinion on the constitutionality of § 33:1236.16. The question was not a real controversy because it was not asserted by an interested party. Furthermore, the statute was being challenged in the abstract. Being a permissive statute, action by the parish was necessary to render it operative. Therefore, contesting the statute's constitutionality was premature. The court also found that the trial court should have revoked the permanent injunction. The trial court should have considered the parish's request to lift the injunction as a rule to show cause why the injunction should not have been revoked. Thereafter, upon proof that the legislature had enacted § 33:1236.16, the trial court was constrained to revoke the injunction.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the trial court declaring the statute unconstitutional, dismissed that portion of the parish's petition seeking declaratory relief, revoked the permanent injunction against the parish, and remanded the case to the trial court.

Bosworth v. Whitley


93-CA-1829


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


627 So. 2d 629; 1993 La. LEXIS 3396



November 29, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor State sought review of a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4(B) (1992) was unconstitutional and held that plaintiff inmates were eligible for immediate parole consideration. The inmates were all sentenced to serve life sentences while the former capital punishment statute was still in effect.


OVERVIEW: After Louisiana's capital punishment statute was declared unconstitutional by the U.S. Supreme Court, the Louisiana Supreme Court ordered that the inmates sentenced under that statute be resentenced to life imprisonment. Section § 15:574.4(B) (1992) provided that no prisoner serving a life sentence shall be eligible for parole consideration until that sentence has been commuted to a fixed number of years. The trial court found § 15:574.4 to be unconstitutional. In reversing, the court held that the statute did not violate the separation of powers clause of the state constitution. The court found that although the authority to grant parole was delegated to the executive branch, the eligibility for parole was closely regulated by the legislature. The court found that the statute did not violate due process rights because the statutory scheme did not create an expectancy of release or liberty interest for inmates serving a life sentence. Finally, the court found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because the statutes, when read together, provided sufficient information regarding how and by whom a sentence may be commuted to a fixed term of years.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that held the parole statute to be unconstitutional and that granted immediate parole eligibility to the inmates.

State v. Code


No. 91-KA-0998


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


627 So. 2d 1373; 1993 La. LEXIS 3431



November 29, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF CADDO, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE GAYLE K. HAMILTON, PRESIDING JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with four counts of first degree murder, and the jury found him guilty. The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) sentenced him to death, and defendant appealed the conviction and the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant committed three multiple homicides during a period of a few days. There were many similarities between the three events, and the authorities concluded that they were the work of a single serial killer. At defendant's trial on the first multiple homicide case, the state offered evidence that defendant's fingerprints were found at one of the other crime scenes and that the three homicides had distinctive similarities. After the jury found defendant guilty, the state again offered evidence concerning the other two multiple homicides. Defendant claimed that the admission of this evidence against him was improper. The court ruled that the evidence was properly admitted. The court found that (1) the evidence was admissible under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 404(b)(1) to prove identity; (2) the state showed by clear and convincing evidence the commission of the other crimes and defendant's connection to them (3) the probative value of the evidence was not substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice; and (4) the state gave defendant notice of its intent to use the evidence at the sentencing phase to show defendant's character and propensities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the sentence imposed against him.

 

173 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Cosse v. Allen-Bradley Co.


No. 93-C-0301


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


625 So. 2d 486; 1993 La. LEXIS 2963



October 18, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIFTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee was awarded damages in his personal injury action against defendants, manufacturer and designer. Intervenor employer received a compensation benefits award, reduced by the employee's fault and by liability for some of the employee's recovery costs. The Court of Appeal of Jefferson Parish (Louisiana) reversed the reductions and the employee sought review.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed that the employer's reimbursement recovery should have been reduced by his fault because a 1985 amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1101 applied as a restatement of a preexisting rule that a compensation carrier could only recover to the same extent as an injured employee. The court held that the reduction was not permitted because the employee's accident arose before the amendment's effective date and the amendment was a substantive change that did not apply retroactively. The unambiguous language of the statute in effect at the time of the accident did not qualify the employer's right to recover any compensation amount paid and comparative fault principles did not modify this absolute statutory right. The court ruled that the appellate court incorrectly gave retroactive effect to a 1989 amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1101(C) that limited the employer's liability for the employee's costs to one-third of the employer's recovery for pre-judgment payments or pre-judgment damages. The trial court applied the proper formula, but recalculation with current figures was required.


OUTCOME: The part of the judgment that did not allow the employer's reimbursement to be reduced by the employee's fault was affirmed. The part of the judgment that limited the employer's liability for the employee's costs was reversed and the case was remanded for a new calculation based on the proper formula and updated figures.

Succession of Terry


No. 92-CA-3155


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


624 So. 2d 1201; 1993 La. LEXIS 2466



September 10, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Direct Appeal from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court Parish of Jefferson



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant decedent's succession appealed directly from the judgment of the Twenty-fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which found that La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1493 as amended in 1989 and 1990 was unconstitutional because it violated La. Const. art. I, § 3, and which decreed that plaintiff decedent's adult child was the sole forced heir entitled to a portion of the decedent's succession.


OVERVIEW: La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1493 was amended in 1989 and 1990 to extinguish the right of forced heirship for persons such as the adult child who were competent and over 23 years of age when the decedent died. The trial court found art. 1493 unconstitutional as amended because it violated La. Const. art. I, § 3, by being an arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable discrimination against a person based on age. It denied the adult child's claim that art. 1493 was unconstitutional as amended under La. Const. art. XII, § 5, because it abolished forced heirship. The trial court applied the law that was applicable prior to the unconstitutional amendments and decreed the adult child to be the decedent's sole forced heir and entitled to an undivided one-fourth forced portion of the estate. The court, based upon a ruling earlier that day, found that La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1493, as amended, was unconstitutional, but because it violated La. Const. art. XII, § 5. It did not determine if La. Const. art. I, § 3 was also violated. Regardless, the trial court had reached the correct results in finding that La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1493 as amended was unconstitutional and by applying prior law.


OUTCOME: The court amended the trial court's judgment to declare the statute unconstitutional as amended because it abolished forced heirship, without reaching the adult child's challenge based on age discrimination. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in all other respects.

 

175 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dorthey


No. 92-KA-3120


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


623 So. 2d 1276; 1993 La. LEXIS 2464



September 10, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 24, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, DIVISION J, PARISH OF ORLEANS



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF DISTRICT COURT REVERSED; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Division J, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which held that the habitual offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers clause of La. Const. of 1974, art. II, § 2, where a district attorney attempted to enhance defendant's sentence for possession of crack cocaine under the habitual offender statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of crack cocaine and sentenced to serve five years. The district attorney filed a bill of information invoking the habitual offender law to increase defendant's sentence, asserting that he had three prior convictions. The district court quashed the bill, finding that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 violated the separation of powers clause. Based on the traditional role of the district attorney in criminal prosecution and the power of the legislature to vest him with discretionary functions pertaining to such prosecution, the court concluded that § 15:529.1 did not violate the separation of powers. By imposing habitual offender statutes, the legislature merely established a procedure which enabled the district attorney to seek, and the court to exact, more severe sentences on defendants who repeatedly violated the law. The legislature acted within its constitutional authority, which allowed it to determine and define a crime and provide its penalty. It did not delegate its duties to the judicial or executive branches, nor had it usurped the judiciary's discretion in sentencing defendant. Accordingly, no separation of powers violation existed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court holding the habitual offender law unconstitutional and remanded the case to the district court to determine whether defendant's sentence was constitutionally excessive.

 

176 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wigley


No. 92-KK-1503


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


624 So. 2d 425; 1993 La. LEXIS 2465



September 7, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 21, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO THE DISTRICT COURT


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State appealed a ruling of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which reversed the trial court's denial of defendants' attorneys' motions for payment and compensation and ordered the attorneys be paid $ 1,000 each for representing the indigent defendants.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys were appointed to represent defendants who were both indigent. The attorneys filed a motion for payment of expenses and compensation, which was denied by the trial court. The court of appeal reversed the judgment. It held that to require the attorneys to defend without fee violated the attorneys' right to substantive due process and La. Const. art. I, § 13. The court affirmed the court of appeal's finding that appointing attorneys without reimbursement constituted an unreasonable extension of their professional obligations. The court ruled that the attorneys' appointments were unreasonable and oppressive, because they were not assured reimbursement, nor had they been reimbursed for their properly incurred expenses. The court reversed the award and that part of the judgment holding that to require an attorney to defend without fee violated his right to substantive due process and § 13. The court ordered that the attorneys be reimbursed. It remanded the case to the trial court for a hearing to allow the attorneys to present evidence to establish their reasonable overhead costs and expenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment holding that appointing attorneys without reimbursement for expenses constituted an unreasonable extension of their professional obligations. The court reversed the order that the attorneys be paid only $ 1,000. The court remanded with instructions to hold a hearing to establish the attorneys' reasonable overhead costs and expenses.

 

177 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Succession of Lauga


No. 93-CA-0034


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


624 So. 2d 1156; 1993 La. LEXIS 2479



September 7, 1993 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 4, 1993. Released for Publication November 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Direct Appeal from the Thirty-fourth Judicial District Court Parish of St. Bernard.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant heir and intervenor attorney general challenged the decision of the Thirty-fourth Judicial District Court Parish of St. Bernard (Louisiana), which found in favor of plaintiff children that La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1493 (as amended 1989, 1990), was unconstitutional because it violated La. Const. art. XII, §5 (1974), and because it arbitrarily, capriciously, or unreasonably discriminated against the age of a person.


OVERVIEW: The heir and the children were all survivors of the decedent. By statutory will, the decedent left his entire estate to one child, the heir. The children filed suit against the heir to annul their father's statutory will. They challenged the constitutionality of La. Civ. Code art. 1493 (as amended 1989, 1990), which abolished the right of forced heirship and deprived a child to an equal share of a forced portion of a decedent's estate. Summary judgment was denied the heir and the attorney general, and the trial court found art. 1493 unconstitutional. The heir and attorney general argued on appeal that the statute was clear and unambiguous and no further interpretation of its constitutional intent was necessary. The court disagreed and found art. 1493 unconstitutional as well. The court found the statute abrogated the constitutional principle of equality of heirship established in La. Const. art. IV, § 16, and abolished the whole legal institution of forced heirship. The court reasoned that the statute deprived the children of their individual right as a child to an equal share of a forced portion of their father's estate as constitutionally provided in art. XII, § 5.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was amended so as to declare the statute unconstitutional. As amended, the trial court judgment was affirmed.

 

178 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Chamberlain v. State ex rel. Department of Transp.


No. 93-C-0472


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


624 So. 2d 874; 1993 La. LEXIS 2467



September 3, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties appealed a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Louisiana) judgment that affirmed the district court judgment which awarded limited damages in a ceiling under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106(B)(1) after plaintiff parents sued defendants, state, agency, and contractor, for plaintiffs' son's personal injuries after he fell from a bulkhead.


OVERVIEW: After their son suffered brain damage when he fell from a bulkhead, plaintiff parents sued defendants, state, agency, and contractor, for personal injuries. When the district court limited monetary damages in a ceiling under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106(B)(1), both parties appealed. The court reversed and remanded. The ceiling on general damages imposed by § 13:5106(B)(1) was unconstitutional. The ceiling contravened the constitutional proscription against sovereign immunity under La. Const. art. XII, § 10. La. Const. art. XII § 10(A)'s unequivocal, self-executing waiver of sovereign immunity as to suit and liability in contract and tort cases constrained the legislature and the courts from imposing limitations on the constitutional right to sue the state. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106(B)(1)'s ceiling on general damages could not, despite the legislature's disclaimer to the contrary in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106(E)(4), be construed as anything other than a partial resurrection of sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the limit to plaintiffs' damage award and remanded because the statutory ceiling was unconstitutional and contravened the proscription against sovereign immunity, so that the ceiling on general damages could not be construed as anything other than a partial resurrection of sovereign immunity.

DeSalvo v. State


No. 92-CA-2882


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


624 So. 2d 897; 1993 La. LEXIS 2469



September 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District, Parish of East Baton Rouge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State and the Department of Public Safety and Corrections (Department), appealed a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:398(H) unconstitutional as violative of plaintiff attorneys' state constitutional right of equal protection of the laws.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys filed an action against the State and the Department, seeking to have § 32:398(H) declared unconstitutional because it prohibited their access to accident reports, denied them equal protection of the laws under La. Const. art. I, § 3, violated their First Amendment right to commercial speech, and denied their right to examine public documents under art. XII, § 3. The district court denied the attorneys' claim that their constitutional right to inspect public documents had been violated. It declared the law unconstitutional as to the attorneys' equal protection rights. The court reversed and declared § 32:398(H) to be constitutional. The court ruled that the law was valid as a reasonable time, place, and manner regulations, it left open all channels of lawyer advertising, and served a significant governmental interest. The court held that the State carried its burden of showing that § 32:398(H) furthered the state interest in protecting the right of privacy of individuals. The statute provided that the reports of motor vehicle accidents should be confidential, exempt from the provisions of the public records law, and available only to certain classes of persons.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment declaring the law unconstitutional.

Cox Cable New Orleans v. City of New Orleans


No. 92-WA-2311


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


624 So. 2d 890; 1993 La. LEXIS 2473



September 3, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which declared unconstitutional an ordinance enacted by the city that purported to "clarify the application" of the preexisting amusement tax on the gross receipts of "admission charges" to certain amusements so as to impose the tax on the subscribers of appellee cable television company.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted an ordinance, New Orleans, La., Mun. Code § 14300, that imposed a five percent tax on the gross receipts representing admission charges to a number of "described amusements," including a "production." The cable company, as required by the ordinance, collected the tax from its subscribers and remitted the funds to the city, but notified the city it was doing so under protest. The cable company filed two separate actions: a declaratory judgment action seeking a declaration that the ordinance was null and void, and an action to obtain a refund of the taxes paid by under protest. The court of appeal reversed the summary judgment rendered in favor of the city and rendered judgment in favor of the cable company, declaring the ordinance unconstitutional and holding that the cable company had a right of action to seek refund of the taxes paid under protest, and ordered a refund to the cable company, to be distributed to its subscribers. The court held that the 1990 ordinance was the enactment of a new tax and was therefore an unconstitutionally enacted sales tax. The court further held that the ordinance was severable and struck only the offending portion of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment of the court of appeal declaring the ordinance unconstitutional to strike only that portion purporting to include cable television service subscriptions within the definition of production. As amended, the judgment of the court of appeal in the declaratory judgment action was affirmed. The court dismissed the remainder of the action.

Polk v. Edwards


No. 93-CA-0362


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


626 So. 2d 1128; 1993 La. LEXIS 2366



August 6, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court For the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Honorable Carl A. Guidry, Judge. On supervisory writ from the First Circuit Court of Appeal



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens appealed the judgments of the District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which declared that the Cruiseship Gaming Act, the Louisiana Riverboat Economic Development and Gaming Control Act, and the Video Draw Poker Devices Control Law , and the Louisiana Economic Development & Gaming Corp. Act, with the exception of one provision that was severed, were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: In consolidated actions, citizens sought declaratorys judgment finding the following statutes unconstitutional: the Louisiana Economic Development & Gaming Corp. Act (Casino Act), the Cruiseship Gaming Act, the Louisiana Riverboat Economic Development and Gaming Control Act, and the Video Draw Poker Devices Control Law. The trial court declared unconstitutional the provision of the Casino Act that provided that employees of the casino corporation were not subject to civil service provisions. However, the trial court severed that provision from the remainder of the Casino Act and declared that all four of the statutes were constitutional. The court consolidated all appeals and affirmed the judgments. The court held that the legislature properly exercised its authority in determining that limited gaming activities were in the best interest of the state for the safety and welfare of its citizens. The statutes constituted general laws rather than local or special laws. The casino corporation was an instrumentality of the state and was subject to the provisions of the civil service system, which was why that provision was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that the four gambling statutes were constitutional with one exception. The court affirmed the finding that one provision of the Louisiana Economic Development & Gaming Corp. Act was unconstitutional but was severable, leaving the remainder of the statute unaffected.

State v. Barrilleaux


No. 92-K-0978


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


620 So. 2d 1317; 1993 La. LEXIS 2163



July 2, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF LAFOURCHE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of Lafourche (Louisiana), which affirmed his conviction on six counts of theft over $ 500 in an attempt to defraud several insurance companies and denied his motion to suppress the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of six counts of theft over $ 500. The trial court denied his motion to suppress the evidence obtained in search of his business premises. It acknowledged that the affidavit presented by the officer did not establish the identity of the informant or the source of the informant's information. The trial court concluded that the warrant was properly issued under the totality of the circumstances, and the evidence was validly seized under the facially deficient warrant under the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule. The court of appeal affirmed. The court ruled that the affidavit alone was insufficient to establish probable cause for the issuance of a warrant. It failed to give information about the reliability or the identity of the informant, information about the basis of the informant's knowledge, or about independent police investigation following the tip that would have provided credibility to the tip by the unidentified informant. However, the court affirmed the denial of the motion because, under the overall circumstances, the exclusion of the evidence seized did not outweigh a good faith violation of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 162.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for theft over $ 500.

 

183 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hattaway


No. 91-KA-0894


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


621 So. 2d 796; 1993 La. LEXIS 2164



July 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring Opinion Dated July 8, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Parish of Winn



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Eighth Judicial District Court, Parish of Winn (Louisiana), which found him guilty of first degree murder, claiming that he was denied assistance of counsel during interrogation, and therefore his conviction should be reversed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first degree murder. Before trial, defendant was transferred to a different parish without notice to his appointed counsel. While at the second location, defendant was unable to communicate with his attorney, family, friends or witnesses. The police interrogated defendant and obtained a confession without the consent of defendant's counsel. Defendant was found guilty of murder and appealed his conviction. The court held that La. Const. art. I, § 13 guaranteed defendant the right to counsel and to be able to rely on counsel as the medium between himself and the state. The court stated that the state could not obtain a waiver from the defendant or otherwise communicate with him with respect to the offense except through his defense counsel. The court also determined that defendant's right to counsel extended to critical stages of prosecution including interrogation of the defendant. The court concluded that the state violated defendant's rights when it transferred defendant without the consent of his attorney and interrogated him without counsel being present. The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court.

State v. Peart


Nos. 92-KA-0907, 92-KD-1039


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


621 So. 2d 780; 1993 La. LEXIS 2301



July 2, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA, AND ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans, State of Louisiana, which found in defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:145, 15:146, and 15:304, and the system for securing and compensating qualified counsel as a whole were unconstitutional as applied in the city of New Orleans.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an indigent, was charged with armed robbery, aggravated, rape, aggravated burglary, attempted armed robbery, and first degree murder. The trial court appointed a public defender to defend on all but the murder charge. The attorney had at least one serious case set for trial for every trial date during the period and received no investigative support for routine cases. The indigent defender program had no funds for experts, and their library was inadequate. The trial court found that the attorney was not able to provide his clients with reasonably effective assistance because of his work conditions and found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:145, 15:146, and 15:304 were unconstitutional for providing inadequate funding for indigent defense. On appeal, the court held that while the trial court might question the political wisdom of requiring political subdivisions to fund the system, the statutes were not unconstitutional. However, in light of excessive caseloads and insufficient support with which their attorneys must work, indigent defendants were generally not provided with effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with instructions that when trying defendant's motion and any others that were filed, to hold individual hearings for each such moving defendant and, in the absence of significant improvement in the provision of indigent defense services, to apply a rebuttable presumption that such indigents were not receiving constitutionally effective assistance.

State v. Bourque


No. 92-KA-0968


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


622 So. 2d 198; 1993 La. LEXIS 2300



July 1, 1993, Decided

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30. The 16th Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Martin (Louisiana) sentenced defendant to death in accordance with the recommendation of the jury. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence based on 77 assignments of error.


OVERVIEW: The court found no error in the trial court's denial to recuse, or order the sequestration of the district attorney, because defendant failed to show resulting prejudice. The court held that short form indictments were constitutional, and that defendant had notice of the aggravating circumstances upon which the state relied. The court held that a lawful investigatory stop was made, that defendant was advised of his rights, and his statements made thereafter were spontaneous statements. The court held no error was made in voir dire by the trial court's refusal to have individual sequestered voir dire, by denying challenges for cause of certain jurors, or by allowing the state's explanation of reasonable doubt; the court found no prejudice to defendant by these rulings. The court found no error in the guilt phase of the trial in the trial court's evidentiary rulings regarding statements regarding other crimes, admission of physical evidence, res gestae evidence, or testimonial evidence. The court held that evidence of other crimes exceeded its limited purpose to show defendant's character, and invalidated the jury's subsequent recommendation of the penalty of death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction of first degree murder, but reversed and vacated the death sentence. The court remanded the case to the trial court for a new sentencing trial.

State v. Shelton


No. 92-K-3070


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


621 So. 2d 769; 1993 La. LEXIS 2170



July 1, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the decision of the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit (Louisiana), which ruled that the State failed to provide sufficient proof of defendant's prior felony conviction under the Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, where the State did not introduce the actual transcript of the plea colloquy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of purse snatching. At defendant's habitual offender hearing, the State introduced a minute entry which stated the judge "gave the Defendant his rights" and a well-executed guilty plea/waiver of rights form, rather than introducing the actual transcript of the plea colloquy from the prior conviction. The trial court sentenced defendant as a multiple offender. On appeal, the intermediate appellate court reversed. On further appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the State sustained its burden of producing a contemporaneous record that showed that defendant knowingly and intelligently waived his rights as required by § 15:529.1 because the submitted form listed several rights, including the right to trial by jury, the privilege against self-incrimination, and the right to confront accusers, and showed that defendant had initialed these and other statements, and that defendant and his counsel signed the form.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the intermediate appellate court, which had ruled that the State failed to sustain its burden that defendant knowingly and intelligently waived his rights during a guilty plea in a prior case during a habitual offender hearing.

Circle Food Stores, Inc. v. City of New Orleans


No. 93-CA-0332


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


620 So. 2d 281; 1993 La. LEXIS 2169



July 1, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the city and the Director of Finance (Director), sought review of a decision of the District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which declared the ordinance unconstitutional because it violated La. Const. art. VI, § 29. The city was ordered to refund plaintiff retailers the sales, use, and consumption tax paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: After paying the tax imposed by the ordinance, the retailers filed a class action seeking to have the ordinance declared unconstitutional. The district court declared the ordinance unconstitutional because it violated La. Const. art. VI, § 29. It ordered the city to refund the retailers the taxes paid under protest. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held that coupled with other taxes levied by the city exceeded three percent and was not authorized by the legislature or approved by the voters. Therefore, the ordinance violated § 29. The court ruled that the ordinance was a tax on the sale at retail, use, or consumption of tangible personal property, particularly tobacco products. The court found that by imposing the tax on the retailers and postponing imposition of the tax until after the sale at retail, the retailers would pass the tax on to the consumer. Because the tax on the sale at retail failed to meet the requirements of § 29, the ordinance was a nullity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment declaring the ordinance unconstitutional and ordering the retailers to be reimbursed for the taxes paid under protest.

Taylor v. Giddens


No. 92-C-3054


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


618 So. 2d 834; 1993 La. LEXIS 1805



May 24, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 7, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF CADDO, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a widower and surviving children, appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Caddo, State of Louisiana, which affirmed a decision of the trial court sustaining defendant doctors' exceptions of prescription under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 to plaintiffs' wrongful death and survival claims arising from alleged medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' decedent died of esophageal cancer after doctors' failure to timely discover the cancer based in part on accidental failure to X-ray her esophagus. The widower admitted that when he saw a medical malpractice attorney before his wife's death, he knew there had been a foul-up. He did not return to the attorney or question the doctors until after his wife's death. Plaintiffs filed a petition for medical review pursuant to the Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41 et seq., one year after the decedent died. An intermediate appeals court affirmed the trial court's sustaining of doctors' peremptory exceptions of prescription under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. On appeal, the court held that while § 9:5628 applied to the survival action, it did not apply to a wrongful death action because such action did not necessarily come into existence simultaneously with the malpractice action. Instead, wrongful death actions were subject to prescription under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3492.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment sustaining the peremptory exceptions as to the survival action and reversed as to the wrongful death action. The court remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Tucker


Nos. 92-KO-2093, 92-K-2130


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA

PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF CADDO, STATE OF LOUISIANA

Previously Reported at 619 So.2d 38 and Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.
 State v. Tucker, 619 So. 2d 38, 1993 La. LEXIS 1803 (La., 1993)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEAL AFFIRMED AS TO COUNT ONE; JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEAL REVERSED AND CONVICTION AND SENTENCE REINSTATED AS TO COUNT TWO.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review, by application of writ of certiorari, of a judgment from the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which held that defendant's motion to suppress should have been granted and that the evidence was the fruit of an unlawful seizure. Defendant also sought review of his conviction on count one, alleging that it was not supported by sufficient evidence.


OVERVIEW: Police patted down the suspect and found a firearm on his person, a plastic bag containing 26 rolled marijuana cigarettes, a single-edged razor-blade, a number of small plastic bags, and considerable cash. Three days later, defendant was arrested for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute after a bag he tossed away was retrieved and it contained 47 rolled marijuana cigarettes. The district court found defendant to be a third time felony offender on count one and, as such, sentenced him to 25 years at hard labor. The district court also sentenced defendant to 25 years at hard labor on count two. The appellate court affirmed the conviction on count one, but determined that defendant's seizure as to count two was unconstitutional under La. Const. art. I, § 5, and held that the evidence was the fruit of an unlawful seizure and was inadmissible. The court held that it could not conclude that an actual stop of defendant was "virtually certain" to occur at the time he abandoned the evidence and therefore he had not been unconstitutionally seized. The court held that there was substantial evidence to support defendant's conviction on count one.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeal as to defendant's conviction for count one. The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal as to count two and reinstated the trial court's conviction.

 

190 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Radiofone, Inc. v. New Orleans


No. 92-CA-1523


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


616 So. 2d 1243; 1993 La. LEXIS 1419



April 12, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring Opinion Dated April 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the city, the mayor, and the members of a city council appealed a decision from the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) in favor of plaintiff, a mobile telephone company, in its declaratory judgment action. The court found unconstitutional New Orleans, Louisiana Ordinance No. 14211, § 52-202, M.C.S. (1990) imposing a one-percent charge on subscribers of intrastate telecommunications services.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from a decision in favor of a mobile telephone company, the court affirmed, holding that § 52-202 was unconstitutional. The imposition of a one-percent charge on subscribers of intrastate telecommunications services was a sales tax, which had been adopted without having been approved at a public election as required by La. Const. art. VI, § 29(A)(1974). Section 52-202 imposed a new tax on previously untaxed telecommunications services and providers. The 1990 Ordinance was subject to the constitutional and statutory requirements in existence at the time of its enactment. Because the city failed to submit the proposed tax to the public for its approval at an election, the tax was unconstitutional. The city argued the sales tax imposed was merely a re-enactment and continuation of a 1968 telecommunications tax ordinance which was tacitly ratified by the 1974 Louisiana Constitution. The court disagreed, holding that because § 52-202 imposed taxes not contemplated by the 1968 ordinance, it imposed a new tax and was subject to the constitutional and statutory constraints in effect at the time of adoption in 1990.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision declaring unconstitutional a section of a municipal ordinance imposing a new sales tax on subscribers of intrastate telecommunications services.

 

191 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Talley v. Succession of Stuckey


92-C-2298


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


614 So. 2d 55; 1993 La. LEXIS 902



February 22, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ST. MARTIN, STATE OF LOUISIANA


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit (Louisiana) that affirmed the trial court's judgment that La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1705 did not unconstitutionally discriminate against her illegitimate child, and held that the testator's will was valid and should not be annulled due to the subsequent birth of the testator's illegitimate child.


OVERVIEW: The mother challenged the appellate court's affirmance of the trial court's judgment that art. 1705 did not discriminate against her illegitimate child, and that the testator's will that excluded the child was valid and should not have been annulled due to the subsequent birth of the testator's illegitimate child. The appellate court asserted that the different treatment of illegitimate children was justified because of the difficulty of proving paternity after the testator's death. The court reversed and noted that the purpose of art. 1705 was to effectuate the distribution of property pursuant to the presumed intent of the testator. The court noted that the testator was presumed not to want his will to stand if a child was born of him after he made his will, but who was not provided for in the will. The court held that the state's purpose in the orderly distribution of property was not substantially related to the discriminatory treatment of illegitimate children who were able to prove their filiation to the testator in a manner prescribed by law. The court held that the statute could still stand and accomplish its purpose, severed the unconstitutional word from the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's affirmance of the trial court's judgment that the testator's will was valid and should not have been annulled by the subsequent birth of the illegitimate child.

 

192 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Church Point Wholesale Beverage Co. v. Tarver


No. 92-CA-2658


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


614 So. 2d 697; 1993 La. LEXIS 911



February 22, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON DIRECT CIVIL APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. DIVISION "I", PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State, through various officials, sought review of the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Division I, Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, which, in plaintiff beer wholesalers' suit, granted partial summary judgment declaring the Beer Tax Statute (Act), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:342, unconstitutional and granted in part and denied in part the State's exception of prescription.


OVERVIEW: The beer wholesalers filed an administrative claim under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1481 et seq. for recovery of excise taxes paid without protest under the Act and filed suit for a declaration that the Act was unconstitutional. On appeal from the trial court's partial summary judgment, the State argued that the wholesalers' sole remedy was under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1576 and that their claim had prescribed. In vacating in part, the court ruled that the payment-under-protest procedure in § 47:1576 was not the sole remedy and that the claims-against-the-state procedure under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1481 et seq. was also available to recover overpayment of tax, which included taxes paid under an invalid statute. The court ruled, however, that the alleged discriminatory effect of the Act ceased after 1982 and that the wholesalers' claim was not filed until 1988, which meant that their claim for the taxes paid prior to 1983 had prescribed under the three-year period of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1623(A). The court held that, while prescription did not bar a declaratory action, it deprived the wholesalers of the standing required under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. arts. 1871 and 1872.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the summary judgment of the trial court declaring the beer tax statute unconstitutional, affirmed the trial court's ruling on the State's exception of prescription, and remanded for disposition of the wholesalers' remaining claims.

Brossette v. Alcoholic Beverage Control Bd.


No. 92-C-1758


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


611 So. 2d 1391; 1993 La. LEXIS 65



January 19, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF REVIEW TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant club owner sought review of a decision entered in the Court of Appeal, First Circuit (Louisiana), which affirmed appellee liquor board's suspension of his liquor license and assessed costs against him.


OVERVIEW: The club owner was charged with violating a city ordinance by operating his bar in a manner adversely affecting public health, safety, and morals. The police chief asserted that the club was in a high crime area and that he received 102 complaints for that block. The chief requested that the club be closed. The club owner employed off-duty police officers from December 1987-April 1988. Aggravated assaults took place in the club's parking lot, as well as second degree murder, and weapons offenses. The alcohol board suspended the club's liquor license for six months. The club owner appealed to the district court, which held that the findings of the board were supported by the record. The court of appeal affirmed. On review, the court held that the club owner did not aid, abet, or encourage the behavior that went on at the club. Rather, he attempted to hire security to prevent such occurrences. The court also found that the hearsay evidence presented at the Board level should have been excluded from the district court. In addition, the court held that the suspension was not moot even though the six-month period elapsed, as it affected his ability to obtain future permits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal and vacated the six-month order of suspension.

 

194 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Gregory v. Louisiana Bd. of Chiropractic Examiners


No. 92-CA-0742


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


608 So. 2d 987; 1992 La. LEXIS 3666



November 30, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, JUDGE WILLAIM H. BROWN PRESIDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board of chiropractic examiners sought direct review of the decision of the 19th Judicial District, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) that held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 37:1743 was an unconstitutional infringement upon plaintiff chiropractors' freedom of commercial speech.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff chiropractors brought suit against defendant board of chiropractor examiners, as the agency with authority to administer the laws and regulations governing chiropractors, to enjoin the board from implementing La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 37:1743 which banned direct mail solicitation of patients who were victims of automobile accidents. The chiropractors argued that the statute was an unconstitutional restriction on their right to freedom of commercial speech. The trial court found the statute unconstitutional and the court amended the affirmed and held that while the state had a substantial interest in protecting its citizens from possible overreaching by health care providers who attempt to influence people to seek medical aid, any abuses could be controlled by less restrictive means than a blanket ban on direct mail solicitations. The court held further that the state was required to use the least restrictive means of regulating commercial speech which was in proportion to the interest that was served. Further, the court held that the interference with commercial speech in the statute at issue was broader than necessary to prevent the evil feared by the board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that the statute was an unconstitutional infringement upon the chiropractors' freedom of commercial speech.

 

195 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


St. Paul Fire & Marine Ins. Co. v. Smith


No. 92-C-1043


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


609 So. 2d 809; 1992 La. LEXIS 3675



November 30, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed from a judgment of the Third Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana), which reversed the trial court order and held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1103(B) (1989) applied retroactively. Thus, the proceeds from plaintiff's action against defendant tort-feasors and their insurer, including non-economic damages, had to be applied first to reimburse intervenor workers' compensation carrier for payments to plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee was injured in a 1988 work-related auto accident, and brought an action against defendants, the other driver, his employer, and the employer's insurer. Plaintiff received benefits from intervenor, his employer's workers' compensation carrier, which sought reimbursement of those benefits from the proceeds of the action. Defendant insurer paid its policy limit into the court in a concursus proceeding. The trial court held that under existing case law and the pre-amendment version of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1103(B) the intervenor was entitled to reimbursement only from the proceeds allocated to non-economic damages. The circuit court reversed, holding that the 1989 amendment to § 23:1103(B) applied, and the entire award had to be first applied to reimburse intervenor. Plaintiff appealed, and the court reversed, holding that the 1989 amendment did not apply retroactively. The court found that the amendment was substantive, thus could only be applied prospectively, because it significantly altered the respective rights of the injured employee and the employer (or compensation insurer).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, which had reversed the trial court and had held a 1989 statutory amendment applied retroactively, entitling intervenor workers' compensation carrier to reimbursement from non-economic damages paid to plaintiff employee by defendants, a driver, his employer, and the employer's insurer. The court held the amendment was substantive, and thus applied prospectively only.

 

196 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


American Waste & Pollution Control Co. v. St. Martin Parish Police Jury


No. 92-CA-1433


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


609 So. 2d 201; 1992 La. LEXIS 3676



November 30, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARTIN STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant parish appealed a judgment of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Martin (Louisiana), which granted plaintiff waste control company's motion for summary judgment in an action filed by the waste control company for an order declaring that certain zoning and land use ordinances enacted by the parish were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The waste control company attempted to secure a permit to construct a solid waste disposal facility on property located within the parish. The parish enacted a zoning ordinance which set forth a comprehensive parish-wide land use plan and it enacted a land use ordinance which set forth requirements for the initial siting of solid waste landfills. The trial court held that the ordinances were unconstitutional because the parish's police jury did not have legislative or constitutional authority to zone or restrict land use. The court held that the parish had no home rule charter and thus, it could only exercise those powers expressly granted to it by the state constitution or by the legislature. The court held that pursuant to La. Const. art. VI, § 17, the parish was only given the power to zone or regulate land use if the legislature had established uniform procedures for the exercise of such power. Because the legislature had not established such uniform procedures for the parish, as it had for municipalities and certain other parishes, the parish lacked the authority under the constitution to enact the ordinances at issue and thus, they were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

197 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bennett


No. 92-K-0944


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


610 So. 2d 120; 1992 La. LEXIS 3728



November 30, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring Opinion Dated December 8, 1992. As Amended February 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL THIRD CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state, by writ of certiorari, appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, State of Louisiana, which reversed defendant's conviction on retrial of solicitation to commit murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:28.1 and sentenced him to five years at hard labor. The court of appeal concluded that the original judgment was final when this court denied rehearing and, therefore, the one-year prescription on retrial lapsed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court noted that both the criminal and civil procedural articles related to finality provided for the finality of a court of appeal judgment when there was no application for rehearing and when there was a denial of an application for rehearing. However, the court found that only La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2166 specifically provided for the finality of a court of appeal judgment when a timely filed writ application was denied by the supreme court. The court found that the parallel criminal procedural article, La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 922(C) was silent as to this issue. After analyzing the legislative history and intent behind art. 922(C), the court found that the silence was inadvertent and resulted from the fact that such a procedure did not exist in criminal proceedings at the time of its enactment because the supreme court's had exclusive jurisdiction over criminal appeals. Therefore, the court held that where a writ application was timely filed with the supreme court, a judgment of the court of appeal in a criminal proceeding was not final until that writ application was denied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal, which vacated the conviction. The court vacated the court of appeal's order releasing defendant and remanded the case to the court of appeal to address the remaining assignments of error raised by defendant in his appeal.

 

198 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Butler v. Department of Public Safety & Corrections


No. 92-CA-1918


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


609 So. 2d 790; 1992 La. LEXIS 3724



November 30, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 17TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF LAFOURCHE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant Department of Public Safety and Corrections appealed a judgment of the Seventeenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafourche (Louisiana), that reversed the Department's administrative order of suspension of respondent driver's driving license after an arrest for driving while intoxicated (DWI) on the basis that the administrative procedure violated the state and federal constitutional guarantees of due process and equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The driver had his license suspended, and the suspension was affirmed at an administrative hearing. This was done per the Implied Consent Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 32:667, 32:668. The driver alleged that the adjudicatory function of the Department combined with the executive function of the Department in suspending his driver's license was unconstitutional. The trial court had found that the State acted as investigator, advocate, and adjudicator in both the criminal trial and license hearing thereby depriving the driver of a neutral and detached arbiter. The court did not accept this argument. Even where de novo review was available, an impartial administrative decision maker was required for due process. According to the court, a distinction was made in the law between a commitment by an adjudicator in advance about the facts or his personal stake in the outcome of an adjudication and the combining of functions within a single administrative body. The court also rejected the argument that given the criminal prosecution and sentence the driver's license suspension was a second punishment for the DWI. A driver's license suspension was a civil and not a punitive measure.


OUTCOME: Ruling against the driver and in favor of the Department, the court reversed the judgment appealed from and remanded with an order that directed the trial court to reinstate the driver's license suspension ordered by the Department's administrative law judge.

 

199 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bernard


92-KK-0997


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


608 So. 2d 966; 1992 La. LEXIS 3633



November 12, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the judgment of the court of appeal authorizing the general admissibility of victim impact evidence is modified as set out in this opinion, and the case is remanded to the district court for notice of the specific evidence sought to be introduced by the prosecutor and a hearing on the admissibility of that evidence.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ of certiorari following a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which reversed a trial court's judgment that victim impact statements were not admissible at defendant's sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for first-degree murder. During pretrial proceedings, the State informed defendant that it sought to introduce victim impact evidence in the sentencing phase of the bifurcated trial. The trial court held that the evidence was inadmissible and the appellate court reversed. Defendant sought certiorari. The court held that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.2, allowed only evidence which was relevant to the circumstances of the offense or the character and propensities of the offender. Some evidence of the murder victim's character and of the impact of the murder on the victim's survivors was admissible as relevant to the circumstances of the offense or to the character and propensities of the offender. To the extent that such evidence reasonably showed that the murderer knew or should have known that the victim was a unique person and that the victim probably had survivors, and the murderer nevertheless proceeded to commit the crime, the evidence bore on the murderer's character traits and moral culpability, and was relevant to his character and propensities as well as to the circumstances of the crime.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the appellate court, and remanded the matter to the trial court for notice of the specific evidence sought to be introduced by the prosecutor and a hearing on the admissibility of that evidence.

 

200 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


92-KK-1000


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


608 So. 2d 949; 1992 La. LEXIS 3511



November 12, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE J. MICHAEL MCDONALD, PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: The rulings of the district court on defendant's motion to limit other crimes evidence and related motions are set aside, and the case is remanded to the district court for reopened hearings on defendant's motions in accordance with the principles expressed in this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a writ of certiorari to the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) on his motion to limit other crimes evidence in a death penalty case which was in the pretrial stage. The trial judge denied all defense motions and ruled that all of the other crimes evidence was admissible. The court of appeal denied defendant's application to review the rulings.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been indicted for the first degree murder of a 74-year-old woman who was stabbed several times with a knife during the course of an aggravated burglary and/or armed robbery. Defense counsel had moved to exclude or to limit the evidence of the other crimes and filed related motions, including motions to require a hearing on the admissibility of other crimes evidence either prior to trial or outside the presence of the jury. The trial judge denied the motions and ruled that all of the other crimes evidence was admissible. The court reversed and limited the criminal conduct on which the prosecutor could introduce evidence to that conduct for which the period of limitation for instituting prosecution had not run at the time of the indictment of the accused for the first degree murder for which he was being tried. The court also held that delinquency adjudications in juvenile court were not per se inadmissible, but that the admissibility of such adjudications was limited to adjudications based on an offense that would be a felony if committed by an adult.


OUTCOME: The rulings of the district court on defendant's motion to limit other crimes evidence and related motions were set aside, and the case was remanded to the district court for reopened hearings on defendant's motions in accordance with the principles expressed in the opinion.
